O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, very dear children, I have completed this book, which is the last of the science of medicine along with its fulfillment, and I have made the end through its expositions and through its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I would complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say, "surgery.
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is very difficult in our region and is wholly strange, so is the science lost and cut off, and nothing remains of it except the small descriptions in books of the ancients that hands have changed.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come error and vanity, and the understandings are closed, and the science is estranged.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Now it seems to me that I want to revive it along with the ordering of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will come along with the forms of the iron tools for cautery, and of the other instruments of the work with the addition of the declaration and preparation of them, as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason of this that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is estranged.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for whoever undertakes this to excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the arrangement of the limbs, and the forms and the conjunctions and the separations of them, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and veins, and their number, and the movement and the moving and resting veins, and the place of their exit.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this reason, Hippocrates said that the name with the name is much, and with the work is little; and especially in the art of hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you in the introduction of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable of the aforementioned things should beware lest they fall into error and kill men, as I have many times seen several of those who meddle with this science and abandon themselves without knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish man who cut an abscess on a woman's neck, and cut the arteries of the neck, so much blood flowed out that the woman fell dead into his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another man who extracted a stone from an old man, and the stone was large; he also took a piece of the bladder away with it, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to extract it, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and knew well that if it was cut, he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another man who took on the cure of a duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the break there was a wound; and the man, full of ignorance, bound the break over the wound tightly, and did not apply any dressing to the wound, and left it like that for a time; and he commanded him not to loosen it at all; and it remained like that until the leg became completely swollen, and the foot, and it came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come and untie the leg; and when I loosened it, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all the same, the corruption had already set in in the limb, and I could not heal it; and the corruption did not stop travelling through the limb until the entire limb was lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another man who opened a festering abscess, and then inflamed it through the malice of his skill.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a chancre, when it is pure of melancholic humor, it is not necessary to touch it with iron unless it is in such a place that one can remove all that is corrupt.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And therefore, dear son, you need to know that the work of the hands is divided into two divisions: namely, work where there is danger in many situations; and I will show in every place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Therefore, you must be careful so that foolish men cannot speak ill of you.  If you take up your weapons in consultation, and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best way so that through the grace of God you come to safety and be praised; and leave behind the terrifying illnesses of grievous sickness; and remove your weapons from what causes you fear, and have faith in yourselves so that you can come from this world to the next in glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen said in some of his admonitions: "Do not take on a serious illness unless you are called a foolish physician.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is of cauteries by fire and of cauteries by sharp medicine, and the chapter is ordered from the head down to the feet; and of the shapes of instruments, and of the iron implements of cautery, and of everything that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is of cutting and piercing, and of cupping and wounds, and of the extractions of arrows, and of similar things; and the chapter is ordered and the forms of the instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is of restoring dislocations and distortions, and of similar things; and is ordered from the head to the feet, and of the shapes of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Before we remember the work, it is necessary for me to speak of the quality of the help and the harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of aid and harm are the longest speech and the subtle science and the secret answer; and about this many wise men spoke, and agreed on this; and their words are of little use to me, for I fear the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cautery aids universally in all complexions where there is matter, except two complexions: that is to say, a hot complexion without matter, and a dry complexion without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In a hot and dry complexion with matter, some disagreed and said that cautery is a great aid; and others said the opposite: that cautery is not helpful for diseases that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be used to cure a hot illness by heat, or by dryness; and the one who says the opposite says that cautery is a great help for a hot and dry illness that comes into the bodies of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man and its moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it sometimes by experiment.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in any case, do not interfere except those who have tested it, and who know through long use the chapter on cauteries, and the diversity of the complexions of men, and their dispositions and the causes of their illnesses, and the occurrences and the passage of time; of other complexions we have no fear, especially in cold and moist illnesses.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the doctors gathered and agreed upon cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that cautery with fire is among the secrets of cures, and of greater goodness than cautery of burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not affect anything other than the affected limb, and does not harm other members very much.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Burning medicines travel from one limb to another, and cause serious illnesses to the limb; and perhaps kill the patient.  Fire, because of its intensity and the goodness of its substance, does not do this, unless there is excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found through experiment and the length of service and study I have put into the art, and it was based on the truth of things; and therefore I apologize for the length of the speech, for it does not please me to deprive you of the secret hidden in fire, and the quality of the work, how it expels illnesses from the body, as the philosopher says in demonstrating; now receive it into your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on the time when cauteries should be performed, and chose springtime.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cautery is appropriate at all times, because the harm that comes upon is lessened by the use of cautery; and especially if the cauteries are necessary for pains strong and urgent that cannot wait for the time when greater malice might come to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And do not think about it, dear son, as the foolish do; for the illness cured by cautery has no return; and they say it thus; but it is not as they suppose, because cautery is only a medicine that changes the complexion and dries the humors that are the cause of the pain, and is more valuable than other medicines for its speed of action and for the virtue of its work and its authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And a possible thing is that the illness sometimes comes according to the complexion of the sick person and the location of the illness and its strength; and superfluities gather within them through the intake of food and similar things, if it is not cauteries administered in places where there is little superfluity and moisture, such as cauteries for toothaches, and similar things, and such pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cautery is called the last resort of medicine, and that is true; but they do not believe that cautery is worth anything after other medicines, but their intentions are false, and cautery is the last resort of medicine because when we have tried various cures for an illness and they are ineffective, then we administer cautery, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it is clear that cautery is the last resort of medicine, and not according to the intentions of the foolish.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that gold cautery is better than iron, and they did not say this except for the quality of gold and the high nature of its substance; and they said that the cautery spot does not cause corruption, but this is not true, for I have experienced it and have found it to be true in some men; and gold cautery is better than iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And yet, when you heat a gold instrument, you do not know when it is hot by the color of the gold, and it cools quickly; and if it is heated too much, it will damage the fire; and thus there are enough impediments.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason, we use iron cautery, which is more suitable for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or I have arranged this chapter from head to foot, so that the way may be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	of olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	These cauteries are useful for moisture and cold on the brain, and there are two of them used for the cause of a disease called "soda," and for the cause of many humors that descend from the head to the eyes, and to the ears, and for a multitude of dreams and toothache and sore throat, and especially for all diseases that come from coldness such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged with a solution medicine, purifying the head for three or four nights, according to the strength and age and custom of the patient can bear; and then raise the head of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on his knees; after that put the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes; and leave where your middle fingers will go, so it bleeds then heat the cautery that is called "olivare," of which this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it on the spot marked with ink, and move it downwards while squeezing your hand little by little, turning it; then quickly lift your hand, and look at the spot to see if you see the bone a little bit; and if you don't see it, then repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I told you; after that take a pinch of salt, and put it in water and soften some cotton inside, and put it on the spot, and leave it for three days; after that put wet cotton in butter; and leave it until the inflammation is gone; then treat the wound with the ointment that is called "tetrafarmaçon" until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the ancients said that the longer a wound remains open, the more it purges; and therefore this is a helpful method.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some of these said that one should leave the cautery until part of the bone is burned, and then the burned part of the bone should be removed and treated.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And others say that one should leave the cautery on for a long time, and press so hard that one removes a piece of bone as wide as a spindle that women use in their spindles, so that the humors may flow outwards; and one should leave the wound open for a long time; after that, one should treat and close it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cautery do not seem to me to be entirely good, except in some people where there is a need for fear; and I rather think that I should leave it; for the shoulder is weakened by the continuous solutions of nature, as we testify in other members; and even when the patient's shoulder is weak by nature, the first semblance of cautery seems safer and milder to me, and I use it in these cases for the sake of safety.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When chronic pain occurs in the whole head and lasts a long time, the patient should use herbs and pills called "cochie," and head purges, oils, and plasters; and if one applies the cautery as we have previously described, and it does not work.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Be careful if the patient's shoulder is of strong nature and not too cold; then cauterize a little below the cautery we have mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After that, cauterize on each horn of the head down to the bone, as we have said before, and make one cautery on the place called "vasselz"; and there is one place where cupping is applied; and ease your hand so that you do not see the bone: the patient feels much greater pain in this cautery than in the others, and I will talk about that elsewhere; and the cauteries on the horns must be finer than those used to cauterize the middle of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	of the cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain arises in a part of the head, and the patient's suffering extends to the eye, and the head is purged by purifying medicines, and the other cures that I have mentioned in the division of diseases have been applied, and none of it has been effective: then apply cauteries according to two methods, namely with sharp medicine and with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauteries of sharp medicine are done thus: take a clove of garlic, peel it and cut it a little in two pieces, then cut the temple where the pain lies in such a way that you can place the clove of garlic under the skin; and when it has been placed, tie and compress it well, and leave it like that for twelve hours; and then untie it and pull the clove of garlic out, and leave the wound like that for two or three days; then place on it cotton soaked in butter until suppuration occurs.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment with ointment, until it is healed; and if you wish, do so with some of the burning medicines that I have written in the twelfth treatise on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The cautery of iron is done in this way.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery, of which this is the form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the head is made in the form of a close, where it has a slight curve, and in the middle a small appearance; and place it over the painful area, hold your hand and turn the iron a little gently, until half the thickness of the skin is burned; and lift your hand so that the artery, which is outside, does not burn, and abundant blood flows out.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	Afterwards, place cotton in salted water and put it on the area for three days; then place moistened cotton in butter, and then treat the area with ointment until it is healed; and if you want to cauterize this headache with the cautery called "cultellare", using the entire point, and be careful not to cut the artery in this headache, which is not ancient.
de emigraine	of headache
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat a headache, as we have previously said in the divisions of diseases, and it does not work, and you see that the previously mentioned cauteries of medicine and iron are not enough, then you must heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white; and thus, make a mark on the aching area, one-and-a-half fingers long, and remove your hand once, and make sure you do not cut the artery and do not reach the bone; and be careful of the jaw that moves when one chews, and that the nerve does not move and that spasms do not come to the patient, and beware of blood flowing from the artery when it is cut, or cutting it brings great fear, especially for those who do not know or understand and who are not students and experienced; and leave the work half-done; but I will tell you how to stop blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it is appropriate in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these cauteries are not sufficient for the illness, and the patient is suffering, cauterize the middle of the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed; and if you wish, administer the cautery that we mentioned in the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery having two blades; and this cautery is better than the other and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain of the ears due to cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain in the ear comes from cold, and one has used dissolving medicines and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division, and the pain does not change, then heat this cautery, which is called "poins," of which this is the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then prick all around the sick ear, or around both if the pain is in both, and move a little above the root of the ear after you have marked the place; and have ten pricks around each ear; then treat the area until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture that must be treated with cautery is no stronger than those caused by phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of diseases; and do not use cautery for those that come from dryness and spasms of the nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this kind of torture caused by phlegm from dropsy and purging of the head and gargles, and this does not work, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, another a little outside the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips; and place the cautery on the seemingly healthy part, and apply it to the head of the ear slightly below the ear's tip, and another in the temple as long as a thumb; and leave the cautery on until half of the kernel is burned; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it is similar to the scalpel we mentioned before, but it is slightly more subtle, and the knife should be a little thicker; then treat the area as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When the apoplexy is long-standing and you treat it as we have said, and it does not help, and the patient does not have a fever, then apply four cauteries: two on the two temples, one in the middle of the head, and one on the area called the "vessel," as we have said before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; and treat as we have said before.
de litargie	of lethargy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this illness, give the patient large herbs and pills to cleanse the brain; then, cover the patient's entire head and apply a mustard plaster to the back of the head, as written in the treatise on plasters; and this is the method of cauterization: do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If he is healed this way, it is good; and if not, apply three cauteries from the middle of the head, descending down to the neck, with one inch of space between each cautery; and treat it like the others.  And if you wish to add more, and the patient can bear it, apply one cautery in the middle; and if necessary, two others on the two temples, and treat until he is healed; and let the cauteries be "olivare" type, as I said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the cold of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	The head must be cleansed with herbs and as previously mentioned; then cover the patient's head, apply a cautery in the middle of the head and on each temple, and one at the back and three along the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient can bear it, and the illness is severe, apply four cauteries along the spine of the back; and leave them until most of the area is burned, and remove your hand; then treat it until healed, and let the cauteries be "olivare" type, as we said before.
de l’epilempsie	of the epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	An epileptic should not use fire cauteries unless they are phlegmatic, and it is necessary first to cleanse the brain with herbs and other treatments as we have described in the section when the patient is large and can bear taking medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it's a child who cannot bear it, give them gargles and chewing motions, cleansing the brain frequently with good food; then cover the head in the middle, and apply one cautery as we described earlier, and one on the vein, and one on each temple; and if the patient is strong and can bear it, apply cauteries as I said for those with paralysis and body softening, along the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped as I described.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, apply one subtle cautery according to this method:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When, due to melancholy, superfluities or corrupt moisture and thick phlegm exist, then cauterize with cauteries as we described for those with paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if, due to melancholy, the superfluities are inclined towards melancholy and the patient's body is moist, then give them to drink things that cleanse the brain, according to what is mentioned earlier in the section.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After covering the patient's head, then make a linen band, like a circle, and place it around the head; and the patient sits cross-legged, held securely from all sides; then apply the liniment, and it is worth a dose of old beeswax; and heat it gently with fire, so that the patient can tolerate the application; then remove the circle from inside the head and allow it to cool; and do this for the patient every week once, with other good treatments, until they are healthy.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or if you wish to cauterize by making several punctures with the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This manner of cauterization softens the brain evenly; then place moistened cotton in butter and goose fat on top.
de l’awe des eulz	of the water of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When water comes first to the eyes by the signs that I have described in the division, then begin and give the patient to drink things that cleanse the head, and guard it from all moisture, and make them sweat in a bath several times on an empty stomach.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	Afterwards, he commands the patient to rest their head, and cauterizes in the middle of the head, and makes two cauteries on the two temples if the descent of water is to both eyes together, or in one if the descent is in one; and cut with the entire cautery all the veins and arteries that are under the heart, and let the cautery be long according to the width of the temple; and be careful of the flow of blood, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stop it with the power you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and the incision the caution how you will stop it; and sometimes one cauterizes or makes incisions below the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	from the body of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears from the eyes are long-standing and habitual and are on the veins, or beside the arteries that are on the apparent surface of the head; and one sees that it is from cold, phlegmatic superfluities, then apply the cautery that I have described at the beginning of the water descending to the eyes: one cautery in the middle of the head, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries or incisions below the two bones; and if there is further need, then cautiously cauterize above the eyebrow with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	from the body of tears within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat it according to what we have said in the division, and it does not help, then give the patient three nights' worth of remedies; afterward, shave the head, and make a cautery in the middle of the cautery (olivaire); and make two cauteries of the cautery called "clavilis" on the two eyebrows, a bit below the hair; and be careful not to cut the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery that is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the eyelid is softened by illness and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	of which this is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you wish, make two cauteries on the two eyebrows as long as the eyebrows are; and do not leave your hand there except until the third part of the eyelid is burned, according to the method that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Sometimes it happens that the hairs of the eyelids turn inward and prick the eye, and cauteries are made in two ways: that is to say, of fire, or of burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For cautery by fire, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they grow and are even, then place the patient in your care; afterwards, mark on the eyelid a shape that is like a myrtle leaf, and let the beginning of the mark be next to the hairs; then place moistened cotton in egg white and persillion mucus on the eye, then heat the cautery with which this shape is made:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cauterize over the shape you have marked little by little many times, so the skin is burned in that spot; and the sign of the success of the work is that you see the eyelid retracted, and the hairs raised at the point of the eye; then remove your hand, and leave it like this for three days, then put moistened cotton in butter until the burn is gone; afterwards, treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if afterward the hairs come back, and the eyelid is softened, then repeat the cautery on the same spot, as you did first; and if the hairs have disappeared, cauterize it until the eyelid is raised to its natural place, and is even, and the hairs do not prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The cautery of burning medicine is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow large and even, then make a shape of a myrtle leaf from parchment; then take French soap and hot water, one ounce of each, and grind them together well; and do it quickly so it does not cool, then spread it over the shape you made, like the myrtle leaf, and place it over the eyelid; and if the patient only has pain in one eye, one should work on one, and if in both, likewise; and put under the eye cotton moistened in egg white; and the patient's head should be in your care, and place your index finger on the medicine, and press it slightly and move it every time the patient feels the medicine biting, for it feels biting like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, remove the medicine from your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the biting sensation has passed, remove the wetness from the area, and observe if you see the eyelid raised as if it had been raised by the constriction of fire or by an incision; and if it is like that, it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, then put more medicine on the area where the medicine has not worked, until your work is even, and your eyes are set right; then place moistened cotton in butter until the inflamed part is calmed; after, treat the area with the ointment called "dyafenis" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if it is necessary, be careful in your work, taking great care that no medicine drips into the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the eyelid becomes soft afterwards, and the hairs prick the eye, then reapply the medicine to the area softened by the eyelid properly, as you did before; then treat it until it is healed; and this is the method of the myrtle leaf:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of humans are diverse in size and smallness, and according to that, let your constrictions be; and the correct way is not easily found for someone studying this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the treatment of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have described in the divisions of diseases, and your treatments do not work, then you must cauterize it according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Tell the patient to place his head in your lap; and let the attendant hold his head between your hands so that it does not move, nor does he remove his head; then place moistened cotton in a mixture of egg white or parsley juice over the eye; then heat the cautery which is shaped: and is pointed at the top like the shape of a swallow's feather, that is how the cautery should be; if you wish, it should be pointed from one end to the other, and if you wish, it should be like a tent; however, this pointed one is better for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	Then press the fistula if it is open, and remove the pus and dry it; and if it is closed, then open it and remove the matter; then apply the hot cautery firmly, and hold your hand over the cautery on the part near the eye, so that your hand does not cause harm; and place the cautery on the fat of the eye and burn it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you get to the bone with the cautery, that would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, then repeat the cautery one more time, and again if needed, and leave it for three days; then apply moistened cotton in butter, and treat it with a drying ointment until it is healed; and if forty days pass and it is not healed, then apply an acid corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed; and treat it according to what is in its chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cauterizing a fistula that some of the ancients described.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Understand the fistula and open the area; then place in the fissure one thin spatula, of which this is the form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and it is the size of a lead coin; and hold your hand on the spatula firmly, and let the patient not move at all, so that the melted lead does not run into their eye; and it is necessary that you place on the patient's eye moistened cotton in egg white or in water: the lead burns the fistula area and heals it with marvelous health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have described, that is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, it is necessary to administer a puncture to the nose, and to bring the fistula back to the body of the nose according to what is suitable in its proper place.
des crevaices en levres	cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Often cracks in the lips, which are called "poil," occur, especially in children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks with what we have said in the divisions, and the treatment does not work, then heat a small, knife-like cautery according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it quickly on those cracks until it reaches the bottom; afterwards, treat the area with ointment until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess occurs at the root of the throat, or on the uvula, or the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it causes decay and rot and becomes old and develops into a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in the divisions, and it does not work: then it is necessary that you have a cautery according to the size of the fistula; afterwards, place it in the opening or perforation of the fistula, and hold your hand until the hot iron reaches the bottom and the innermost part; and do this once or twice, then treat it with what we have said in the treatments until it is healed; and if it is healed this way, it is good; and if not, then you must expose the area and remove the corrupted bone, as you find it in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	of the movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines, and this is of no use, then place the patient's head on your lap; afterwards, heat the cautery, of which the shape will be shown later, in such a way that you place a stick on the tooth; and immediately put the hot cautery inside, and hold your hand until the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; afterwards, remove your hand and reapply the cautery as you wish; afterwards, have the patient fill their mouth with salty water, and rinse for an hour and spit it out.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way, the tooth that was moving is strengthened, and the softened gum is tightened, and the corrupt moisture dries.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When toothache comes from cold, whether there is actual cold or not, and the treatments of medicine are not effective, then there is a need for cautery in two ways: cautery with butter and cautery with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cautery with butter is such that you take cow's butter, and put it on the end of an iron or copper spoon; then take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a tent, and soak it in boiling butter, and put it quickly on the aching tooth and hold it until it cools; and do so often until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth, and if you wish, soak wool and cotton in cold butter and put it on the aching tooth, and place a hot iron on top until the heat reaches the tooth's tip.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The cautery with fire is such that you take a piece of iron or copper, and make it large enough so that the fire does not reach the patient's mouth; then heat the cautery, the shape of which will come later, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools; do this often, for the pain will be removed that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary for the patient to fill their mouth with good butter during the application of this cautery, and then remove the fire; and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make cautery of whatever shape you wish, and according to your ability; and this is the shape of the cautery:
des scrophules	of the scrofulas
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrofulas are of phlegm and cold moisture, and are not obedient to digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery, the shape of which will come later, and have two openings for the fumes to escape on the other side of the cautery; and place the hot cautery on the abscess once, or as much as needed, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, place the cautery according to the size of the abscess and leave it thus for three days; and place soaked cotton in butter until the burning is gone; after that, treat the area with ointments and dressings until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the cautery:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the moisture overcomes the channels of the lungs, especially when it comes from a cold temperament, then the patient must first be emptied by dissolving medicines; afterward, make a cautery at the root of the throat, and be careful not to go all the way down to the throat and not to burn the heart, but only a little bit.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterward, make another cautery at the joint of the neck to the top of the spine, and let the cautery, which is called "clavile", be of the shape we have shown before; and treat the area as we have said before until it is healed.
de la toust	Of the cough
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When coughs and lung illnesses are of cold moisture, and the patient has neither fever nor dryness, and the illness is longstanding, then make two cauteries on the ribs in empty spaces; and one other cautery in the middle of the chest between the two breasts; and let the cauteries be the "clavile" type, according to the form previously described.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you wish, make a cautery by pricking, with the type of cautery called "poins" of which the form is shown previously in the illness of the ears; and let the pricks be up to 30, or even more around it.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	Afterwards, treat the area according to what was previously stated, and let the cauteries be in three rows according to this shape:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because of this, the cauteries are lighter, because you make three in a stroke.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterwards, let the patient lie on their back and on their side; then lift the heart that is inside the armpit with the fingers of your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated inside, heat the cautery which has two nerves, of which this is the shape:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and cauterize the heart until it pierces the ribs, and the figure of the cautery would be like four cauteries; and therefore a cautery with three nerves is made, so that the figures of cauterization are six cauteries; and the nerves are according to the thinness of a tent, and this is the shape of the cautery with three nerves:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And sometimes one nerve is added to this, so there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	Afterwards, place the cautery on the bruised area with a bandage; afterwards, have the patient rest, and do not move the limb for a long time until it is well healed.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated above, which rarely happens, then cauterize on the thick part of the clavicle cautery, or many cauteries by pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When chills and much moisture come to the stomach, such that it is contrary to its complexion, and the catarrh is multiplied in him, and in the usual methods of treatment, and it does not profit, then it is necessary that the patient be placed on his back, and extend his legs and arms.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	Thereafter, apply three cauteries; one under the breastbone, the size of a finger, to the entire clavicle; and two more on the outside of the two ribs, so that the shape of the cauteries forms a triangle, and there be sufficient space between them so that they do not join together when they put out pus; and let the cauteries be so deep that they reach both sides of the heart, and the shape of the cauteries follow this form, without overlap.
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach, following this form; and whoever is afraid of this cautery, cauterize by pricking and marking on the stomach with pricks according to the quantity you desire; then cauterize with all the cauterization that is called "puncture".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the treatment that we have had before, until he is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver is afflicted with pain from cold, moisture, and great wind, so much so that it is greatly disturbed from its natural complexion by the superfluities; and the patient is treated with what we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit him, then it is necessary that the patient be placed on his back; and mark with three cauteries, according to this form, this figure, and this quantity, on the liver, outside the hypochondria, where the man's ribs come from; and have a space of one finger's breadth between each cautery; and let the cauteries be of the length of the body, and do not press your hand too much on the entire cautery; and let only half of the heart be burned, and the patient should be standing upright on his feet; and if he cannot, let him be lying down, and extend his legs and raise his arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if you wish, cauterize these cauteries with a scalpel, if you are skillful and wise in the art, and be careful not to burn the entire heart, for you would dry up the whole body; and do not let it reach the boil, because the heart is very delicate in that place, and you know it to be true.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess on the liver, and you wish to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain, but not too strong; and if it is in the membrane, he feels intense pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And when this treatment should be applied, the patient must be placed on their head; and then mark the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery that resembles a ray, of which this is the form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize the cautery until the heart is burned and it reaches a scab, so that the pus is completely gone; after the treatment according to the treatment of wounds, until it is healed; and it is not appropriate for anyone to use this cautery except those who have studied medicine for a long time and through whose hands these illnesses have often run their course.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he may boldly operate, and nevertheless, it seems to me that letting it be is better.
dou cautere de pleuresin	Of the cautery of pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that one should use cauteries of aristolochia roots for pleurisy, and in this manner: take a long aristolochia root, the largest you can find, and let it be dry, and as thick and long as your fingers; and moisten it in oil, and place it in the fire, and cauterize between the shoulder blade and the neck, and two small cauteries slightly down in the part below the beard; and two cauteries between the fifth and sixth ribs, sloping slightly backward; and one cautery in the middle of the chest, and another above the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two on the sides of the chest outside the cautery between the two shoulders; and do not press your hand, but act gently as if smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And some ancient ones said that some men use a cautery of iron resembling a razor, heating it and placing it between the ribs until it reaches the abscess; and the pain subsides, as we have said for the liver abscess.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is danger, where the patient dies now, or a fistula results that cannot be healed.
de la mice	Of the mice
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of mice according to the divisions of treatments we have discussed, and it does not help, then three types of cautery are applicable, all of which are good.
