Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Of which one method is that you make three or four cauteries, in lines along the length of the mouse, following the shape of the liver cautery we mentioned before; and do not press your hand too hard on the cautery, and the patient should often be on their back; and another method of cautery is that you heat the cautery that has two nerves, as we showed in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the heart which is near the mouse, or where the patient's pain comes from the left side, and the elevation you lift the heart according to the heart, according to the length of the body, and the cauteries should be along the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After that, put the two inflamed nerves until the heart is pierced on the other side, and then pull out the cautery, and thus there will be four. And if you want, cauterize with a cautery of three nerves.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the treatment, when it has cast off corruption for a long time, and this is as good as the other treatments mentioned before.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cautery is not useful for a person with dropsy, except in the manner called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat it according to the methods we have described in the divisions, and your treatment does not work, then you must make four cauteries around the ribcage, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the spleen, two behind the back on the spine, and one on the breast; and let the cauteries be very close to the thickness of the heart.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	Afterwards, leave the cautery open to discharge corruption for a long time, and do not cease the patient's treatment after the cautery; and healing will be hastened, and the two intentions will work together with God's help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cautery for the belly should be the clavicle that we have previously shown; and that for the back should be olive-shaped, according to what has been mentioned earlier.
de l’enfleure des piez	Of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in someone who is hydrops, and are full of yellow water, you must cauterize on the back of the foot between the ring finger and the little finger; and lift your hand with the cautery without turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply, lest the yellow water be forced out, and let the cautery be according to this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	Afterwards, make two cauteries on each leg at the tip of the knee; and let the cauteries be long, one beneath the knee in front and the other outside, in the middle of the leg; and leave the cauteries open for a long time without treating, that the water may come out; afterwards, treat with the other treatments that we have mentioned.
de la menoison	Of the menstruation
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When abdominal discharge comes from cold and moisture, so that the retentive and digestive virtues in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be cured by other methods; and you see the patient suffering greatly and of strong constitution, then make one large cautery on the stomach, according to what has been discussed previously in the cautery of the stomach, circular cautery; and four cauteries around the navel, each a small, pointed cautery, and two cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see abundant moisture and the patient is suffering, then make a cautery on the groin, and one cautery on each side, and two small cauteries on the stomach next to the large one, for the treatment is beneficial when there is good assistance.
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When hemorrhoids are in the fundament, one or more, and are old and of thick, cold, moist, corrupted humors, and have been treated as we have described in the divisions, and it does not benefit, then apply cauteries: three on the spine of the back, one after the other, gradually, in a triangular shape, and one cautery below the navel, two fingers deep; and if you think the stomach is cold, and food does not digest, and the face is seen to swell, then on the face, apply one large cautery on the stomach, as previously stated, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen, each a pointed cautery; and leave the cautery open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment, leave the area until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	Of the fleshiness that is called "thelul".
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the althelul, heat the cautery, which resembles a scraper, and then put it, all ablaze, onto the cut althelul; and keep your hand there until the cautery reaches the origin of the vein, from which blood flows; do this once or twice, and if there is a lot of althelul, cauterize each one as we have said; after this, treat with beneficial ointments until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on the alchatim, you will have greater help.
de plaie mal curee	Of a poorly treated wound.
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot tolerate cutting or opening, as we will describe in its place, such an illness arises that cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When a fistula has come upon someone, and is old, throwing out putrid matter and corrupt moisture, you should probe it entirely with a thin probe, and make sure to know the total depth of the probe.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	Afterwards, heat the cautery, which resembles a scraper, and place it into the fistula according to the extent the probe entered, and repeat the cautery until the putrid and corrupt flesh is burned, once, or twice or three times, according to its need; and beware of burning the surrounding nerves and large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula goes to the bladder or the intestines, beware of these places, and do not apply the heat except to the fleshy areas, and consider that it is not penetrating; afterwards, treat the area until it is healed, and if the area is sealed, and the matter has been removed for a long time, then you know the area is healed completely; and if the matter has not been removed, know that the area is perforated, and the bone at the bottom is corrupt; and thus as one of those which we will describe in its place.
de la maladie des reins	Of the illness of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain from cold comes to the kidneys, and from great windiness, and a woman does not take the cure, then you must cauterize the kidneys on either side with a split cautery as we have previously said; and if we cauterize it in the middle, then there will be three cauteries in a line, and this will provide greater assistance.
de la vessie	Of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is weak and soft from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then cauterize the outer part of the bladder, where the pubic hair begins, one on the right and one on the left, and each cautery should be as long as the width of a finger; and make one cautery on the back, or two if needed; and let the cauteries be split in the previously described manner.
de la marris	Of the spleen
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the spleen is cold and moist, and does not allow conception, and the flowers are corrupted and their ends delayed; and when they come, it causes great pain: then it is necessary that three cauteries be made around the spleen, as we said in the chapter on the cautery of the bladder, and two cauteries on the outside of the back; and let the cauteries be split, as we have said.
de la hainche	Of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When viscous moisture descends to the hip joint, and for this reason it moves from its place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the separation is found empty, then you must cauterize the patient on the hip joint with one cautery shaped like a circle, and mark in front of the joint around it as it turns, so that the joint is within the circle; and let the cautery be like the one used to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not available, make three cauteries with large olives, and let the cauteries be as deep as all the others; and treat it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	Of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the hip joint, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient has been treated with what we have said in the division and the treatment is not working, and the illness is old; then you must purge the patient of the thick humors with fetid pills, or other similar good pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After that, apply cautery; and the method of cautery is according to two types: namely, burning medicines together, and cautery with fire.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Cautery with fire is in many ways, one of which is this: that you cauterize three triangular cauteries on the hip joint according to this shape, and make them deep and large, and have the space between each cautery the thickness of a finger, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped; sometimes cautery is done in the middle on the head of the hip, so there are four according to this shape:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you wish, cauterize it with the circular cautery that we have previously mentioned in the dislocation of the hip; but do it in such a way that the circle encompasses the entire hip, and all the thick parts of the core are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the method used in sciatica, when the pain is in the hip and does not reach the thigh or the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it reaches the thigh and leg, then make two cauteries where the patient says the pain is, and one cautery above the ankle four fingers, slightly to the left side; and let the cauteries be knife-shaped, and let the thickness of the core be burned; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to the toes or near the heel, cauterize the places where they feel pain with three or four points with the cautery called "points.
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, make more; and if you know the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, make a cautery with a knife-shaped or circular cautery, and be careful in all your cauteries that you do not leave the cautery so long that you burn the nerves and major arteries, and that you do not cause the patient more harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen several who have made cauteries on the ankle of the foot, and left them so long that the leg swelled entirely, and the foot as well, and the entire foot was pierced and corrupted.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a solution of the belly from which he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two parts together, make cauteries in one and the other, according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise men said, concerning the cautery of the hip, that this is the manner: make one such iron, and let it be at the head as thick as a fingernail, or a little less, and let it be by intervals, and let it be from one interval to the other the width of a finger's breadth; and let the intervals be opposite in two parts, and let them be also like knots, and let there be a well-made iron handle; and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be heated until it is all red and throws sparks, and then it is placed on the sore hip, and turned on the healthy side; and cauterize it once with one cautery run and leave it for three days; and then apply a plaster of butter, and leave the wound open a long time; after the treatment with ointment, until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use this cautery little because of the fear of its effect, and we see few who use it; and nevertheless, it is a good cautery for those who can endure it, and in the places where it is appropriate.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The cauteries of burning medicine are such that you make an instrument with intervals, in which the margins of the wound descend, and it should be of bronze or iron, with a long side, and in height it should have two lines, and there should be between each the thickness of a finger; and let them be open at the front and on top, and let them come together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After that, place it on the patient's hip lying on their healthy side, and press your hand firmly on the hip; then pour hot water between the two circles of the hot water that has been warmed a little in the fire, and leave it for an hour, and let the patient endure the heat and burning.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it finds there a burning as of fire; and when the burning is over, lift your hand with the instrument and wash the hip with sweet water, and leave it for three days, and put on butter until what is black from the scalding is removed; and leave it three days so that the rottenness will come out; and this would be the final help after the treatment with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has spread to the thigh or to the leg, make an instrument that holds water according to what you have done to the hip in the same way; and this is the method of hot water, and I have written it in the treatment of the rectification of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and quicklime, as much of one as of the other, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	Where there is a small hole to escape so that the point of a razor can enter; and place another pot, well-sealed, over that pot, and put alkali and lime and sweet water on top, until there is a finger's width above the powders when you have well held it in your hand; and leave it like that until water comes down, thin and clear, into the sealed pot, then take all that water and pour it over the lime and alkali as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then it will be very thin and is administered in many ways in medicine and in cauteries of other limbs. For it works like fire, and there are other medicines with which one can cauterize the hip well, such as turpentine, honey, and mastic, and lime with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a cure with which a man was cured of pain in the hip and sciatic vein, and praises it greatly, saying that no other cure was made, and that he was healed in one single time when this cure was done, and he had bathed as he will teach us next.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he says in this manner that you take fresh and dry green litharge, and grind it much with a little fat, and put it on the hip and thigh and leg where the pain is, and bandage it; and leave it for three hours, and for as long as the patient no longer feels the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make him enter the bath until his body is slightly wet, and put him in bed, and the pain will go away completely and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use cautery with such medicines unless it is after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's dung, it greatly helps; and the cauteries should be made in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take wool and soak it in old oil, and place it on the hollow that is between the big toe and the other toe, called the 'foscile'.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	Then take dry goat's dung and heat it in fire until it is embers, and put it on the wool, and leave it until it is extinguished; and do this again, and do not cease doing so until you think by feeling that it reaches the hip, and that the pain has ceased; and this manner of cautery is called "goat's dung cautery".
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain in the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from falling or striking or from too great an evacuation, or from the spread of cold matter, none of these types is helped by cauteries, except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary, after the patient has been emptied of foul pills or other such things, that one make three lines of incision on the back, wherever the pain lies, and on each line five cauteries, or more, according to the strength and the amount the patient can bear; and let the cauteries be done according to the cautery called "puncture"; and if you wish, make three or four cauteries at the middle clavicle cautery according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This illness often comes to young children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a narrow gait when they rise, and fear; and you find the evidence in the spine of the back and on the appearance that comes upon the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and wish to cure it, cauterize it with a circular cautery according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the cautery touches each part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you wish, cauterize around the spine with a piercing cautery of two or three lines, and let the punctures be close together.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After treating the area until it is healed according to what we have said, and be careful not to apply cautery to swelling that is in the path of a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain is caused by moisture spreading throughout the body's members, and when the pain is in the feet, what physicians call "podagra" properly, and when it is caused by cold and cannot be cured with medicine, it is cured by cauteries in this way: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary to cauterize on the sole of the foot, make a cautery in the entire shape that is called "point.
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains reach the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, make three or four cauteries on each knee, of each part, all olive-shaped; and if you need more, make more, but do not hold your hand there longer than until the thickness of the flesh is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knees and back, administer the cautery that we have described in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make points around the wrist two lines; and if any pain remains in the fingers, make points on each joint and on the skin of the hand; and if the pains reach the elbows or shoulders, cauterize each part, and give good care to the patient and administer medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give him good care and purge the phlegm, he will be healed by God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the surface
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When a rupture occurs in the groin, and the bowels descend to the testicles and it's recent, then when you want to cure it, he should not eat that day; and let him use things that loosen the belly, so that the stool descends from his belly.  Afterwards, make him sit on his back between your hands, and instruct him to hold his breath until the bowels have returned, and bring them to your fingers, and make a cut below the rupture on the bone of the groin, and make a mark that resembles half a circle above the body. Then heat the cautery of which this is the shape:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until it is white and gives off sparks.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then bring the bowels back to their place; and let the attendant hold his hand over them to prevent their return; and support the patient's thighs well, and put a cushion under him and a servant on his thighs, and another on his chest to hold his hands; then place the cautery on the mark with your whole hand, hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you don't reach it the first time, try again until you get to the bone.  And watch carefully that the bowels don't jump out when you apply the cautery, that you do not burn him, and that the patient does not die or suffer other harm from this.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that if you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your efforts are useless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And the cauteries for children should be small, according to their size, and for adults, as large as their size; after three days, treat the cauterized area with butter until the burning is gone; afterwards, treat it with other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient lie on their back for forty days so that the wound is well-sealed; and it is necessary that his nourishment be light for a long time, so that the bowels do not jump out when he tries to get up and move around.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wishes to get up, give him a well-made bandage, and keep it on for forty more days; and let him have good rest, let him not work too much, and avoid excessive drinking and eating, and loud shouting; and when he follows this instruction, he will be completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will now describe the treatment of cutting in this chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures occur in other parts of the belly and are known to be contained, and you see that they are not growing, apply one cautery of cauterization according to its size, and burn one-third of the core; afterwards, treat it according to what we have said; and some of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with a cautery having three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	But first mark the area and make a line along the width above the rupture, and another outside it, and then place your hand in the middle of the entire cauterized area.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are gentler and milder.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain occurs in any limb, whether from falling or striking, and that pain lasts a long time, and the remedies of medicine are of no use, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the cautery called "points," and the cauteries should be according to the length of the limb, its smallness, its weakness, its strength, its location of twisting, and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If it is healed by the first cautery, that is good; if not, repeat another cautery on the previous one, for such is the custom that it must spread to the part of the limb that is closest to it, therefore you must apply cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of the disease
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	Sicknesses are sometimes aided greatly by cauterization, especially those that come from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	When you see it to be cauterized, be watchful if the illness is in its beginning stage, and if it is treated according to what we have said in the division, and it does not diminish or persist, and you doubt that the corruption might spread throughout the entire illness, then make five cauteries on the head: one in the middle of the head, another toward the forehead at the end of the hair; and two on the two temples, and one behind on the nape of the neck; and let your hand remain until the cauteries reach the bone, and until the skin comes out so that the vapors of the thick humors can escape; and cauterize the area above the affected spot according to what is found there.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And if the illness is spread throughout the body, and it visibly weakens, you must cauterize with the cauteries that we have described for the head, and one cautery on the nose, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the buttocks and another beside it, and two on the two shoulders; and two on the elbows, and two on the tendons of the chest, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and watch out for the nerves that are behind the heel, so you do not burn them; and sometimes one applies a cautery on the bone of the finger, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more cauteries you make, the more aid you give, and the greater the benefit; and know that the sick person does not feel any pain from the cauterization as healthy people do, because the body is already completely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And the cauteries should be large or small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you find in the different types of irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treatment, apply a mixture of flour, figs, and honey, along with other remedies, until it is healthy.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling occurs in any limb and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and it is not yet healed, then you should apply cauteries to the limb according to its size; and let the cauteries penetrate slightly into the depth of the affected area; then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And sometimes cauteries are applied to the hand, foot, and back, at the point where the nerve controlling the limb emerges, and in this way, the swelling is removed; however, no one should intervene unless they are knowledgeable about the limbs and the exits of the nerves that move the body.
de albaras	of albaras
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" has become chronic, and the remedies of medicine are of no use, then cauterize it with a cautery a little deeply, according to the thickness of the affected area, until the discoloration is removed and its color changed; then treat it with flour of figs and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of a colon and blood of an almond, each in equal parts; and mix them all together, and bandage the area with a cloth, and keep it air-exposed until healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of a chancre by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a chancre first appears, and you want to stop it, cauterize it with a cautery that resembles a circle, all around the chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And yet, wise people say that one should also cauterize the middle of the chancre; and yet this does not seem good to me, for I fear it will become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen this happen on several occasions; and a more correct approach is to cauterize around it, with the cautery called "circular", as we have said in the section on cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	Of the inflammation that cannot be healed
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has an illness called "adubelati," and it is slow to heal, either because of the excess it causes, or because of the patient's age—if they are frail—and they have little blood, or because of the time it has taken; and you want to hasten its healing: then cauterize around it with many small, pointed cauteries; afterwards, leave it like that.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will hasten to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you want to pierce it with the whole cautery, heat the cautery with this shape:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of this illness, called "adubelati," until the cauteries have pierced the core, and let the cauteries be such that the patient feels them outside in such a manner that the course of the decay is relieved.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Afterwards, treat it until it is completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The treatment by fire with iron.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	There is another type of illness called "corrodens," which is nothing other than a consumption of a limb, for it consumes the limbs just as fire consumes dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this illness in a place that can tolerate cauterization with fire, then heat the cauteries small and large, according to what is appropriate for the place where the illness is; then cauterize from all sides until you remove all the corruption, and nothing of it remains, so that everything that is corrupt is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it three days, and apply a soothing poultice with oil to the cauterized areas until the heat from the fire is gone and all the corruption is removed.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment with ointments that cause flesh to grow.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that healthy flesh has not grown, that is good; and if not, then repeat the cauterization on the remaining corrupted areas.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this ailment is sometimes treated with sharp medicine instead of fire cauterization; however, fire cauterization is of greater help, and I have already described the treatment with sharp medicine in the division; take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of the boils that come on the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Often it happens that on the feet, from outside, a disease called "clos" in our understanding arises, and it is a large, pus-filled thing that hurts the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauteries for this disease are according to two types.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, fire cautery and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is that you heat a cautery, shaped like a vaulted pen, and made of good iron, to the size that it can encompass the nail on all sides, and with narrow margins; then put it, hot, on the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it reaches the bottom of the nail; and leave it like this for three days until it begins to discharge pus; then make a poultice of crushed wild mallows with salt, and leave the poultice on all night, and the nail will fall and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the area with a healing ointment until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted by fire on the body, and this happens many times on hands and feet, you must administer hot water cautery; and it is done this way: take a copper or iron rod, or a vaulted pen, and put it on the nail and the wart, and put the rod so that it encompasses it entirely, then put a little hot water on it, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand, turning so that the edge of the rod reaches the root of the nail, and can find a way through the hot water to the root; and let the patient endure a little the burning of the hot water for an hour; then leave it like this, and it will uproot itself from all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Do this one after another, until you remove all those that are on the body, then treat them with healing ointments.
li cure dou trembler	The treatment for trembling.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone trembles from cold nerves, or from quartan fever or other such fevers, you should apply four cauteries along the spine, one cautery between each spine; and one cautery on the feet, and one on the stomach with an olive-shaped cautery; this will stop the trembling, and hasten the recovery from the cold illness.
des pustules puans	Pustules that are foul-smelling.
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes, foul-smelling pustules or boils appear on the body, caused by corrupt, thick matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	Therefore, as soon as they appear, one should apply a cautery to each head of the pustule: a thin cautery made of myrtle wood, whose point is heated in the fire, or from the root of long aristolochia, or a lentil-shaped cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And sometimes, they are cauterized at the beginning when they appear, in this manner, and they cannot grow any further; the superfluities from which they come are broken up, and they are healed; but this must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often, great flows of blood occur from the artery that is cut in an external wound, or in the incision of an abscess, or in the cauterization of a limb, and similar things; and it is a very serious matter to stanch it.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet, when this happens to someone, quickly place your index finger on the wound of the vein, and press it firmly until the blood is still beneath your finger, and no more drops come out; then place several small and large olive-shaped cauteries in the fire until they are completely red; then take one, large or small, depending on the wound and the location where the artery is cut, and apply the cautery to that vein where you are holding your finger, and hold the cautery there until the blood is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it spurts out again when you remove your finger from the vein, and the cautery goes out, quickly take another cautery from the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease doing this one after the other until the blood is stanched; and beware that you do not burn the nerve beside it, and that other harm does not come to the patient; and know that when blood flows from the artery, it cannot be well stopped especially when the artery is large, unless it is by one of the four ways that we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction if it is not extracted, or by a strong ligature of thread, or by medicines applied that have the power to stop blood; and be bound and pressed.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever attempts to staunch it by tightly binding bandages or by putting burning things on it, or other similar things, will not profit much from it.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and they do not have a mirror or medicine present, they should place their index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and press it firmly until it is stanched on the wound and on the vein; and do not move the finger, but moisten it frequently with very cold water until the blood is congealed, thickened, and stanched; and do the things needed with cauteries and medicines afterwards.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of the surgeries.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	In the first chapter, we have told you about all illnesses requiring cauterization with fire or burning medicines, and the causes, instruments, and forms of cauteries; and I have arranged that chapter from head to foot, and I will follow the same path in this chapter so that one may more easily find what one desires.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And before I begin this, my dear son, you should understand that this chapter involves more peril and fear than the first on cauteries, and therefore greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to undertake folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come to cures.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	For some come so enraged with their illness that they die easily from the frenzy they find in their sickness, and from the greatness of their malice; and of these one should be afraid.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And of these there are some who give you their consent, and say, "Wait, I am healed"; and the illness is spiteful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	You should not agree with those who come to you with this manner, but place greater trust in your honor than in your greed, and do not act foolishly but wisely with those of whom you are certain, and of whom you can have taken and praise; and use prognostication and indication in the cures of your sick, so that health may be converted; and this will help you acquire good renown, and glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear son, Our Lord grant you good understanding and uprightness, and may He inspire you with the holy inspiration of His hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now, I have arranged this chapter in divisions, following the chapter on cauteries, which I have explained from head to foot, so that you may find more easily what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	a head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness often affects children during childbirth, and when the midwife grips the child's head too tightly; and sometimes it arises from unknown causes.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I never saw this illness in anyone but children, and death quickly followed in all those I saw; and therefore it seems to me best to leave the practice of such treatments.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose head was full of water, and the head grew larger each day until it could no longer support it; and the swelling grew so much that it died, and this swelling is assembled beneath the bone on the surface, between the heart and the bone; and the treatment is such if the swelling is between the heart and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you make a wide incision in the middle of the head; and as long as two fingers, until the swelling runs out; and here is the form of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the swelling is more extensive, and the abscess larger, then make two incisions in the form of a cross, according to this shape:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the swelling is beneath the bone, and the signs that you see the sutures of the head open on each side, and the fluid jumps out when you press it with your hand inside, and this is not understood: then it is necessary that you make three incisions in the middle of the head in this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, remove all the swelling outward.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	Afterwards, bind the incisions with bandages and powders, and apply wine and oil, and leave it this way until the fifth day; then unbind it, and treat the wound with tents and ointments, and leave the head to heal evenly, and give the patient dry food with little moisture until the limbs are strong and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look where the swelling of the abscess is, and the accumulation of the fluid; for sometimes it is in front; sometimes behind; sometimes on the right; and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Then cut where the abscess and the fluid accumulation appear, and make the incision according to your ability; and be careful not to cut an artery; and if blood flows, so that the patient dies from the bleeding and the evacuation of fluid.
de reume	of rheum
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When a disease called "catarrh" occurs in someone's eyes or chest, and the illness is longstanding, and the treatment with medicine is of no use, then the final cure is cautery, where the two arteries are cauterized.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is necessary, then, when you intend to cauterize them, that the patient tilt their head back; afterwards, rub the area with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then the patient should tighten their neck with the whole cloth; then look where the veins begin, and the location of each is next to the ears, and they are close together; then mark the spots, then cut one and the other with a sharp spatula from two sides, until the cut reaches the bone, and this should be done across the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you wish, place the spatula under the artery and cut above it, cutting in the same way as you would through it.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, blood spurts out continuously upward.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not appear on feeling, you must measure the space of three fingers, then mark it and cut to the bone; and the amount of blood that should be released is six ounces, and perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can tolerate and the fullness of the artery; then examine the wound: if there remains on the bone any sign of pus, cut it so that no inflamed abscesses form, then bandage the wound and apply ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When chronic migraine comes, and acute catarrh, due to the moisture of tears and heat in the temples, and old-fashioned madness and similar things, and he is treated by various medical cures and none of it benefits him, we will extract the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extracting them is that the patient should pull back the hair from their temples, and locate the artery that appears in the temple, because it appears clearly through its pulsation, and is rarely visible except in some very cold individuals; and if it is visible, the patient should compress his neck with some cloths, then rub the area with a rough cloth, and apply hot water to the area until the artery is clearly visible; then take the spatula which has this shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	then lightly scrape the skin until you reach the artery, then pull it upward with forceps, and separate it well from the tissues beneath on each side; and if the artery is thin, then turn it with the point of the hook, then cut it from that part according to the size of two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, the blood will not entirely stop flowing.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out six ounces of blood, down to three; and if the artery is large, then you must tie it in two places with a strong double silk thread, so that no decay comes before the wound is sealed, and bleeding occurs; then cut the excess between the two ligatures at the same time, and then, if you wish, cauterize it with a knife cautery down to the bone until the fingers are cut; and this is the best work if the patient does not have a fever and is of a hot temperament.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cauteries are a remedy to end moisture; for this reason, they are of greater help against moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For the extraction of arteries, it is necessary to fill the place with old cotton and put well-made bandages over it; and when they are removed, treat it with dry medicines that promote healing, and with bandages, until it is healed; and if blood flows from the artery while you are working on it, hurry to cut it with cautery, or fill the space with vitriol and hold it with your hand to stop the bleeding; and if you do not have this available, put your finger over the place until the blood is clotted, and wash the area with cold water until the bleeding stops, and it is held as necessary; and the best and easiest way in the extraction of an artery is to cauterize the vein with this sharp cautery from two sides, but the cuts should be wide to maintain their heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too thin, it holds its heat less.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there should be one finger's width of space between the two blades, and then when you have marked the two places, put the burning iron on it until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two places; and the two cuts should be far apart, for it is not completely sealed by this cautery; and this is the form of the cautery.
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When tears from the eyes flow down the veins that are on the head's surface, and no medical treatment helps, and you see the patient's forehead turn red, and feel a tremor-like sensation on the forehead; and where the skin is thin and moist, so that the hair on the temples has fallen out, and the temples are heated and scorched by the heat of the tears, then this treatment is needed.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And the ancients called it "contused cure", and what you do for the patient with this ailment is to remove the hair on their forehead, then make three cuts on the forehead equally along the length of the forehead; and one cut should be as long as two fingers, going straight down the forehead towards the nose, and the other two are alongside the temples, taking care not to cut the arteries that are beside the temples; and keep your hand away from the line of the two jawbones, and each wound should be about three fingers wide; and have a piece of sponge and many cloths ready to wipe the blood, then take a pointed spatula from two sides, and this is its form:
