des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	And make the incision from the one next to the temple to the second incision; and cauterize all the area between the two cuts on the whole surface that is above the bone, then do the same from the middle incision to the other second one, and then remove the spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Then place the instrument called "cultellaire" into the first cut, which is very sharp on one side, and gentle on the other, not sharp, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the cutting side towards the flesh near the area, and the gentle side towards the bone, and insert it until it reaches the middle cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes, until the incision is continuous to that of the area, and then do the same in the middle cut, until the other cut; and then drain the blood equally, and press the area to remove the blood; then put a tent of old cotton in each cut, and put over it cloths moistened in wine, oil, and vinegar, and watch that no hot abscesses arise; and on the third day, remove the bandage, and apply plenty of warm water, then treat it with basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other remedies used to heal wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the cold in the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When some have an acute cold, and you see the eyes sunken and small, and the sight weakened, and the eyelids burning; and the hair falls out, and a sharp pain occurs in the head, and the patient sneezes; then know by these symptoms that these materials and this cold come only from many veins, and the best cure for it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you order the patient to lie on their back, then make a large incision across the forehead, and another one from the wide I shape.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begin the incision from the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision reach the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move the jaw; and when the bone is exposed, wipe away all the blood with a sponge, and then separate the two edges of the incision and place old cotton and linen bandages there; then bind over them cloths moistened in wine and oil, and be careful of a hot abscess; when it is removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow there, then treat it with drying things that make flesh grow.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this way: take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster of it; and apply it to these wounds to cause flesh to grow everywhere.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stopping up of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that falls into the ears is one of four things: either grains, or an animal, or a mineral stone or similar thing like iron; or seeds, such as beans, peas; or flowing things such as water and air and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When a stone or other object falls into the ear that does not join with the ear or grow within the ear, put the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, then drip a little violet oil or oil of sesamum, then administer extraction; and make him sneeze with something, and stop his nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put strips of cloth or wool around the ear; and hold the ear upwards.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often, pus comes out with this treatment; and if it does not come out, administer extraction with fine forceps, of which this is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it does not come out with the forceps, it is good; if not, administer extraction with a fine, small double-edged hook; and if it does not come out with that, make a small copper wire and insert the end of the wire into the ear opening firmly, and seal the area around the wire with softened wax so that wind cannot enter with the wire; then pull out the pus forcefully, for often pus comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this way, take glue that birds use and put on it a suitable instrument to do this and put a little cotton around it; then press the glue on the stone or whatever it is and pull out the pus.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not come out with all these things we have said, hurry to cut the ear before a hot abscess and spasm come into it; and the manner of the incision is that you first make the patient bleed from the cephalic vein, and draw out blood according to its strength, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn their ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear, in the fatty or dependent area; and let the incision be like a crescent, until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your ability, and quickly suck it into your mouth; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain inside and it swells, administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, administer a thin, fine spatumile according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and administer an incision to that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think the grain is moist due to ear moisture, until you have made many pieces; then extract it with fine forceps and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is eased.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the water then that falls into the ear, the patient must use a first conditional sneeze, and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let him lie on that same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps out because of this, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, then he takes many stones, according to the length of your finger, and light, and heats them a little in the fire; and the patient puts one or more in the hole of his ear, and jumps on them with his feet on the other side, and pushes another stone on the stone that is in the ear; and he does not cease to put stone on stone until the water completely escapes, and thus it jumps out completely; and if you wish, take a reed, and put one end in the ear, and the other end in the fire until the softest part of the reed is burned; and then do the same with other reeds until the water comes out entirely, as we have said for the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the removal of the pest, if it is small, like a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is large enough to be felt, administer extraction with tweezers; and this is the easiest thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In extracting worms embedded in the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the division and in the treatment of distillations, and the treatment does not work, you must look at the ear in the sun: if any worms are visible, remove them with fine tweezers, and if none are visible, take the stick with which this form is made:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it is narrow underneath and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And insert the finest end into the ear according to the patient's suffering, then suck strongly on the entire stick; do this often until all the worms are out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not come out, stuff around the stick with cotton as I have said for stones; and if they do not jump out as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have tested in the excision of worms, and you will find them in the treatment of distillations; and distill your oils and medicines into the ear with this instrument, of which this is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it should be made of silver or bronze, narrow underneath with a small opening, and wide above for distilling; and for pressing the distillation within, use a well-made bronze instrument for this, and if you wish, take a scraper and wrap cotton around its point; then put your oil or juice, and what you want of your medicines into the stick, and the stick should be in the ear; then place the scraper with all the cotton inside, and press gently with your hand until the oil is distilled into the ear; and the patient should smell it inside, and the distillations should be a little warmed on the fire before they are distilled into the ear; and make sure it is not too cold, for the medicine will not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stopping of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without any hole in the ears; and this same thing happens to men due to the stopping of a wound, or flesh growing within the ear, and these blockages sometimes go deep into the ear, so that one cannot see them; and sometimes it only slightly obscures the opening, and one can see it clearly.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, the one that goes deep, so that one cannot see it, requires a more serious treatment in several ways, and for the one that is visible, you must place the patient's ear in the sun; and look inside. If you see the obstruction clearly, then open it using this instrument, of which this is the form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And it should be sharp and cutting at both front and back, completely smooth so as not to injure the ear; if the obstruction is formed of flesh or a growth in the ear, hold it with fine tweezers and cut it gently, until all the flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the obstruction is deep within the ear, take a small, gentle scraper and warm it a little in the fire, then place it in the ear canal.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the obstruction, causing the patient pain when hearing, pierce it gently, and be careful not to injure the nerves of the ear; then place a tent in the ear according to the width of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for several days until the wound is healed, or take a tent and moisten it in rose water, and dust with powdered vitriol; and if you see the ear swollen, you must pull out the tent and apply another tent moistened in a cerote made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then treat it until it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if a discharge of blood comes, immerse a sponge and cloth in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the blood discharge, which are found in the treatment of hemorrhages.
de la char des papieres	From the skin of the ears.
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This ailment, where the skin around the ears is moist and dry, you must stretch it using pliers and forceps, and cut it away from its roots with a spatula; then apply powdered vitriol to the area.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if blood is discharged, cauterize it with a thin lenticular cautery, and the cauterization after incision is helpful; and many times they heal, even if anything remains from their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	Of hail.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times there appear on the skin around the eyes things that resemble hail in shape and hardness, and for this reason this illness is called "grandine," and it is a collection of thick moisture on the skin above and below; the treatment is as follows: Observe whether the hail moves from side to side, which is easy to see; then cut it away from its surroundings, then gently scrape it from each part, then grasp it with forceps and cut it away.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cut it without piercing the skin a little, do not worry the patient; and if the cut is large, stitch it together and treat it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not apply any force, for the ointment will quickly restore it and create flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the grandine is extending into the inside of the ear towards the upper part, turn the skin inside out, and grasp the grandine with forceps, cut it and press it on either side; and if the skin is separated by the incision, it will not hurt; and when the grandine is cut, wash the area with salty water and treat the area with what creates flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	Of the fat of the eyes.
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that grows in layers on the skin above, and this happens more to children than to adults, and it causes much suffering to their eyes, and catarrh comes to them in the mornings, and they cannot bear the light of the sun because their tears flow profusely from their eyes; and for this they often lie on their faces, sleeping on their faces, and their skin beneath their eyebrows is moist, and swelling and the appearance are covered by the exinach which shows in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the area with your fingers and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of the procedure is that the patient puts their head in your lap; and then take a linen cloth, and prepare a tent-like circle according to the amount of exinach in each part, then place it over it; and press with your fingers on either side, so that the exinach is gathered within the circle; then cut a slit in the middle of the moisture, with a sharp spatula, and it should not be any larger than the incision made in the bloodletting of a vein; and cut the skin deeply until you reach the exinach; and in various places the exinach comes out of the slit, in the form of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then extract it entirely, a piece of cloth held between your fingers to protect it from further harm; and turn your hand to the right and left until it is dispersed; and be careful not to press into the slit, so that you do not damage the entire spatula all the way to the eye, so you do not injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the exinach does not appear at the beginning of the slit, slightly enlarge the slit until it appears; then extract it as we have said, then wet cloths in oil and water, and place them on the area, and bandage it.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And some men grind seaweed and apply it to corrupt the remaining moisture.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hot abscess comes to the area, treat it with soothing poultices until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of the stones
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow on the stones in addition to those natural, and they become aged, they harm the eyes, and cause various illnesses such as persistent tears and softening of the stones and albugine, even to the point of destroying the eyes; and the cure is according to four methods: either by cautery with fire, or by sharp medicine according to what is before in the chapter on cautery, or by incision and stitching or by cauterization, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must place the patient's head in your lap, then turn the stone of the eye to your left hand; if it is turned, it is good; if not, insert a needle the entire length of the thread above it, and this should be next to the edge of the stone where the hairs grow beside those hairs, and pull the thread upward over the entire stone, and turn it with the rasp; then pierce on the underside of the stone, below the added hairs, with a sharp lancet, from the large tear duct to the small one; then pull out the thread, and place a small tent of cotton and cloth under the stone, then apply a figure of a bandage to the stone, like the leaves of myrtle, and nevertheless the figure must be according to the size that you desire to lift the stone which is designed for all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there is one who needs a large quantity of the stone cut away, according to how the stone is softened; then cut into the entire space along the two lines that you have marked, and begin from the large tear duct up to the small one; and let one of the incisions be near the natural hairs, the width of a root; then insert the lancet into one of the two corners of the center, and then scrape the entire area; then bring the two flaps together with a stitch of a needle and a fine thread of wool, and wipe away the blood, and dry the excess threads above the two eyebrows with some gluey substances, if you wish to do this; and if not, do not bother; then leave the stitch and threads for three or four days; then treat the wound without stitching with dry and constricting things, for the stone rises again with the healing of the wound and the bringing together of the flaps, but the stitch is more difficult (as the ancients said), and this work is without fear; and there is another way: and that is that you mark the stone with a figure that is like the leaves of myrtle, as we have described, with three separate incisions according to the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what rises above in small equal portions according to the shape that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you are unable to hold the forceps, and the things are not equal, take a needle with a thread, and insert it into the figure; and insert another thread next to the large tear duct, and the second thread next to the small one, and bring the threads together between your fingers equally; then lift your hand equally, and lift the entire skin above what you have marked, as we have described, then bring the two flaps of the wound together by stitching, and treat it until it is healed; and if an abscess occurs at your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar soothing ointments; and sometimes the hairs of the stone are turned: then you must use what we have said about the incision; but the stitching in one and the other is more skillful.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of the tendons is according to this form: and it is that you turn the stone and cut it within according to what I have said, and then make two tendons by art, and two thin cords as long as the stone and the width of the space; and cut at the two ends on either side where you hold the threads; then bring one and the other together subtly over what rises from the eye stone, and bind the two tendons from both sides tightly; and leave it thus for several days, and the skin that is bound will die, turn black, and rot, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes a long time, cut it with strength, then treat it until it is healed; and when the wound is closed, and the stone has risen, and the hairs will no longer prick; and this is the form of the two tendons that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you take a fine needle, and insert a fine and soft silk thread; then bring the ends together and tie them neatly, and let the threads be a palm in length; then arrange in the case another fine silk thread briefly, and tie the ends of the thread; then place the patient's head in your healthy position; and let it be next to the sun so that the work is clear, for it is a delicate and precise work; then insert the needle into the entire case at the base of the added hair, and make it pierce the stone quickly until you pull it over the natural hair; then pull the hair up to the case, and put that hair into the case, if there is one, or two, or three, or more; then pull your hand so that the hairs come out of the entire case into the stone with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the case is pulled and the hairs do not come out with it, you will pull the case beneath all the threads you have arranged, until the case comes out of the hole above and you see it with your eyesight; then you will pull the case and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair settles in its place and the flesh grows; and if the hairs are small, attach a long hair from the natural hair, and lift it with that or leave it until it is elongated and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the corruption of the eye.
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease, called "aleacrati," or corruption, comes to the eye, there are two types: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens through the wounding of a cut, or surgery, or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of treatment for it is that you split the wound, separate its edges, and place linen strips inside, and keep it bandaged until it heals; and you should not use things that dry out and constrict in treating it.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do that, the disease will return worse than before; but use softening things, such as fenugreek; and apply water or cooked linseed and diachylon ointment melted in some oil, and wrap it in a bandage, and treat it with this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the success of your treatment is that you must ensure that it does not rejoin in the same way it was before; and these treatments we have mentioned are only ways of addressing this disease so that it does not return in the same form as before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the film that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease, which is truly called "axacrati", is both natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accidental cases come from wounds and cuts and cauteries and similar things; and the method of treatment is that you should take a needle, with a double thread on it, and pierce the flesh, from the left tear duct to the right, so that the thread comes out at two points in the flesh; then stretch the flesh above the needle, and cut it with a wide spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns as it should, that is good; if not, take a scraper and place it in the fissure, and turn the paper, and make two cuts along the inside of the paper; and let the ends of the two cuts be at the two corners of the incision you have made, and make angles so that when they are brought together, the shape is like the shape of a letter called "a Greek I"; then remove the flesh, according to the amount of its sharpened edges under what was holding the paper, then join the two separated parts and stitch them with a wool thread; then treat it with the softeners and poultices we previously described, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the ailment comes from a cut or a stitch or a cautery, you must make a clean cut beneath the hairs of the papers, and according to what has been said before; then separate between the two edges of a poultice, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the ailment, for it is very diverse in form, and wise masters devise tools to their utmost power to restore the form to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to the work and instruments required in various situations.
dou soudement de la papiere	From sudden tearing of the paper.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this adhesion occurs in men in such a way that the paper on top adheres to the white of the eye, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must place the point of a scraper under the paper and lift it upward; and stretch it with forceps, until you cut what is in the air with a thin spatula, which must not be too sharp or too cutting, so that the patient cannot tolerate the spatula being too sharp and injuring the eye; and your incision, with which you scrape that joining, must be gentle, so that the paper returns to its natural shape; and the entire joining is healed, and sometimes they use salt water for the eye, and rinse with fresh water and poultices; then put a linen poultice between the paper and the eye, and place wet wool on top of the eye, abundantly mixed with egg white; and after three days, use poultices and softeners until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	Of the nail of the eye.
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail is of two kinds: one is nervous and resembles hard skin, and another which is not nervous, but resembles frozen white moisture, and when touched with iron and tried to be torn with forceps, it cannot be; and both of these kinds begin near the large tear duct, and grow little by little until they cover the entire sight and all the light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of the incision is that the patient puts their head in your lap, then opens their eyes; and you lift the paper with your hand, then grasp the nail with small forceps and pull it upward; then take a needle and put a horsehair, or cowhair, or oxhair, and a strong thread; and slightly double the tip of the needle and insert it into the nail, piercing it with the entire needle; and tie the nail with a thread and pull it upward, and scrape all the hair from the side of the nail that touches the pupil and the silk to the hair down to the root, then cut the rest at the root of the tear duct with a thin spatula and gentle force, leaving the natural flesh or tear duct so that the flow of tears does not come from the incision; and sometimes the nail is pulled out with a hook alone and with a thread, as we have said; then the nail is scraped with a very soft spatula, the shape of which is like this:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the spatula does not touch and break the fleshy tissue, and that the pupil is not pierced; and after the incision, put a little crushed salt and a poultice made of litharge in the eye, and leave it until the next day; then treat it with whatever is necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot insert the needle and the hook cannot enter, this type of nail growth is often treated with medicine; and it grows as I have described in the division, and if you wish to cut it, open the patient's eye and take a thin, sharp spatula, like this shape:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And carefully scrape the nail upwards, and if you see that it diminishes slightly and the flesh around it tightens, then instill into the eye a poultice made of litharge, red ointment and crushed salt, from your mouth, and bandage the eye until the next day; then repeat the procedure according to this same method until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is nothing else wrong in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then leave it, and treat the hot abscess first until it is healed, then resume the procedure as before until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the tear duct flesh is causing significant damage to the eye, then hold it with the hook, and cut off a part, but not all, so that no tears come; then instill red ointment, made of litharge, into the eye.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows over the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	In the eyes of some men, red flesh sometimes grows, covering the pupil and tightening over the eyelids and turning outward, like a rose of baluster. The procedure is that the patient rests their head in your lap, then opens their eyes, and you draw all that flesh with suitable hooks, holding it firmly. Then cut away the first layer of flesh, continuing to shave it away entirely, being careful not to injure the eye in the process.  The incision should be made with the same precision as we described for removing a nail, using gentle force to remove the growth as the examples in this chapter show. Once the incision is complete and all the flesh is removed, fill the eye with crushed salt, or apply red ointment and similar corrosive medicines. Place a bandage of cotton, with an egg white bandage, over the eye so it is protected from a hot abscess. If anything remains, and a hot abscess threatens to develop, leave the eye and treat the abscess with calming agents; then return to your procedure until it is healed, and do this for all growths of this kind in the eye.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, you must also consider the treatment of each eye according to its natural and accidental condition, and if there is iron used; do not put your hand to any of these procedures until you see the limb withstand the treatment.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Red veins that are visible on the eye impair its function and weaken the eye continuously.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Therefore, first, you must examine whether the eye in which the veins appear is healthy and has no other ailment besides the growth; then remove it in this way: instruct the patient to place their head in your lap, then draw those veins with a hook, according to your skill, and the hooks should be slender and double, following this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let two hooks be on the same piece, in the shape of an I.
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then gently remove those veins with the hooks, and wipe the blood one hour after the other, until you see those harmful veins removed from the eye; and be careful not to injure the eye with the points of the spatulae, and do this work at noon before the sun, and be very diligent in your work so that you only cut the veins; and when you have done this, pour green and red coloquintida into the eye to destroy any remaining traces of the growth.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to remove all of it at that time, place a poultice on the eye of things that soothe eye pain, and leave it for several days until the pain subsides and any abscess is resolved, then recommence according to the previous method until it is healed; and this is the form of the procedure:
de la fistule de l’oil	Of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The ulcers, known as "arissati" fistula, if you treat them with cautery and burning medicines as previously described, and they are not healed, there is a way to open over the abscess, where it should be, and to extract all the moisture, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and blackness, you must use the appropriate instrument for this, which is called "a sharp head." It should be made of iron, and have a pointed end like a file, as shown in the current form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it over the corrupt bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand a little until you know that the corruption is removed; and do this several times, and then restore the area with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the area is healed, and flesh grows, and the pus dries, and it remains like this for 40 days, and it does not re-open and is not an abscess, and no bad accidents occur, know that it is healed. If not, there is no other remedy than to bring the fistula back to the nose's opening, according to this form.  You must expose the bone a second time with iron and sharp medicines. And once it is exposed, take a drill according to this form, and let the iron head have three angles, and the shaft be tapered to the tip, as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone near the tear duct, and move your hand away from the eye a little, and then turn the entire drill until it pierces the bone, and the patient feels it because air comes out if he holds his hand over his nose. Then restore the area with dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and the area hardens, the matter goes into the nose.  This is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	Of the discharge from the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye is completely open, and there is no disturbance to the nose or lessening, you must bandage the patient. Then cleanse it, then apply leeches or cupping vessels without striking to draw out, then place on the eye a compress made of acacia, aloe, frankincense, and gum tragacanth, and then press the eye, and apply the plaster over bandages and strips.  The way to do the strips is to take soft strips, fold each one in four, and then place one over the other according to the eye's need. Then press it over a tough bandage very tightly, and repeat the cupping without striking.  Remove the cupping, and leave the eye pressed day and night, and if the compress softens, you must press it more firmly.  Remove the compress after day and night, and if you see the eye improving, it is good. If not, repeat the plaster, the strips, the bandage, and the cupping until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Of the tearing of a cloth or garment.
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a tear appears in a garment, and it opens and comes out from the edges, like a grain of resin, and is frightening to see; if you wish to mend it, the work is as follows: you place a needle into the base of the tear, and another needle where there is a doubled thread from the edge.  Pierce it, and leave the first needle in place.  Cut the doubled thread, and tie a part of the fabric around it, and press it tightly, and then remove the needle. Put on wool soaked in egg white, and leave it until the thread comes out with the fabric.  Then treat the area with strengthening things until the wound heals. And sometimes the wound is held together by the fabric on each side with a circular cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye shows significant damage, pierce it with a very fine needle that goes deep into the eye, and drain the white fluid and lower the eye, and immediately insert it back. Then press it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	Of the boil on the eye.
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This ailment, called "alcunnati," is nothing more than a boil gathered in the eye, appearing like a descending water droplet, but it is not water.  The method for treating it is to have the patient sit on a prepared and upright seat, then take the head in your hands on both sides and gently move it until the boil appears above your eyes. If it remains inside and does not descend and the vision is cleared, the patient will see things as before. If the boil does not descend, know that it is an infection, and if the lowering of the boil is not as described.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then have the patient sit between your hands, take a very fine needle, and make a small incision into the cornea along the junction of the conjunctiva, cornea, and eyelid, until the boil comes out.  Once it is out, instill warm water mixed with honey, or water with fenugreek boiled in it and honey, into the eye. Then treat it with other remedies until healed.
des aigues de l’oil	Of the infections of the eye.
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have already described the types of infections, and what is needed for treatment; therefore, act accordingly based on the patient's health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	You should have the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from sunlight, and press firmly on the healthy eye.  Then place the patient's affected eye on your left hand if it is the left eye, or your right hand if it is the right eye.  Take the instrument called "almagda" in your right hand if it's the left eye, or your left hand if it's the right eye. Then place the point of the instrument next to the eyelid, about the width of a finger, on the white part of the eye near the tear duct.  Gently insert the "almagda" instrument, and move your hand until it pierces the white of the eye, and you feel the almagda reach the hollow area.  The depth of the almagda's insertion should be equal to the distance from the pupil to the edge of the dark part of the eye; this is the eyelid.  You will see the bone through the clarity of the cornea, and you can then move the instrument to the location of the infection, then apply pressure in one direction after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the infection is now subsiding, the patient will see in front of them, and the instrument within their eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After a short rest, if the infection returns a second time, apply pressure with the instrument. When it is firmly placed and does not rise, gently remove the almagda by rotating your hand slowly.  Then, put a little gem-salt into the eye and rinse the eye with it.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply a bandage of wool or soaked linen, in rose oil and egg white, and bandage over the healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, place a common bandage with egg white on it.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some people who have very hard eyes, then you must take the instrument called "alberit," of which this is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then pierce only the conjunctiva, and do not go too deep, but make a subtle opening, then put the almagda in it, as we have said; and for the completion of the work, prepare for the patient a comfortable bed, on which he sleeps on his back in a dark place; and be free from all movements, and eat light foods, and do not move his head to either the right or the left, and be bandaged according to his condition until the third day; then unbandage him in the same dark room, and test his vision, and have him look at some objects, and then rebandage him until the seventh day; and it is not necessary to do this during or immediately after the operation, but it is necessary to delay it, because the infection rises rapidly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If a hot abscess comes, that you unbandage the eye before the seventh day, and treat it with that which soothes the abscess; and when it is calmed, unbandage the eye and place a bandage over his face to cover it for a few days, and keep him in that dark room.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then gradually leave the room, and return to his normal life; and know that no disciple should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us from the country of the Yrach, who told us that in his country people pierced an almagda, from which they drew out the water, but I have never seen any in our land, nor have I ever read about it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the shapes of almagda, so that those who do not know them may see them; and they should be properly of copper.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And their heads should be of the same subtlety, and the rear in three sharp angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes various extra pieces of flesh grow on the nose, some of which resemble scorpions with many legs; and there are some where the flesh is deeply ingrained with a dark color, and there is soft flesh of a good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In the case of the soft flesh, not ingrained, you must have the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; open their nostrils, and apply the forceps to that flesh and pull it out; then cut what you can hold onto with a sharp, fine scalpel on one side, until you know that all of the flesh is removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if anything remains that cannot be cut, remove it with all the fine instruments gently, so that nothing remains; and if it overwhelms you, or there is a festering abscess, treat it as appropriate; and if it is a malignant abscess, hurry and cauterize it until the blood is stopped and all the flesh is removed, then apply to the nose readily and sharply either wine or vinegar.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nose opens and moisture flows down to the palate, know that it is healed; and if the moisture does not flow as it should, know that there is flesh grown on the bone above, to which the instruments do not come to cut: then you must put a linen thread somewhat thick, and knotted by hand, and have a space of a finger or less between each knot; and the patient should put the end of the thread into their nose as much as possible, and pull it, while smelling, until it comes through the nose into the mouth; and often children do this in schools, and it is an easy thing for whoever wants to do it; then hold the end that comes through the nose in one hand, and the other end that comes through the mouth in the other hand, and pull one after the other while sitting in the place where the thread is.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you know that the knots have corrupted the flesh, then pull out the thread, wipe away the blood, and dip the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nose as before; do this for 3 days or more, until the ointment corrupts all the remaining flesh; and then put a lead strip in the nose for several days until it is healed, and if it needs drying medicines, use them; and this is the method of the instrument for purging the head, with which oils and medicines are distilled into the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or bronze, resembling an open lamp, like a strip, and the conductor likewise; and if you wish, make a closed strip, and let the instrument be full to purge the head; and let there be a handle on the top to hold it when heating the oil or some liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times, a disease called "telul" arises on the head of the nose, grows and becomes large often, until it is a visible thing to look at; and for this reason, you must cut it at the beginning, and remove all of it forcefully, then place the cautery or burning medicine on the spot; and if one delays cutting it until it is large, be wary if it is hard, of a dark color, with poor feeling: do not touch it with iron, for it is a festering abscess, for when one cuts it sometimes, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of a soft touch, not dark in color, and you see it can be cut entirely, empty the patient and cut it without fear, and treat the area with drying and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuation comes to one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, when this happens to someone, check if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then bring the two lips together with a suture, and treat it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, you must cauterize all parts of their edges until they bleed, then bring the two lips together with a suture, and bind it tightly, and sprinkle on powder of dragon's blood and crushed frankincense; and place a piece of strong or other uniting plaster over the powders, and leave it until it dries, then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the suture is that you assemble the solution: either with needles, as we have said in the suture of the belly; or with thread, as I have made known to you.
des apostemes des levres	Of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.
