Many people get hard abscesses inside the lips, resembling grains of millet, small and large; then you must turn back the lips, and cut open each one, and take it with forceps and cut it in each part; then fill the place after the incision with powdered vitriol, until the blood is stopped; and then take it out; and treat the place with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	Of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times, extra flesh grows on the gums, which the ancients call "albulus"; you must hold it with forceps, cut it at its root, and let the pus or blood run; then put powdered vitriol, or other astringent and drying powders, on the spot; and if that flesh grows back after the incision, which happens many times, cut it a second time and cauterize it: it will not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	Of sordes
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes hard, rough scales gather at the base of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums; and sometimes the teeth become black, yellow, or greenish, with the decay spreading to the gum, and the teeth stink; you must have the patient sit between your hands, with their head in your lap, and scrape the teeth or scales away wherever they appear until nothing is left; and do the same for the blackening, greenness, yellowness, and other spots, until they are cleaned; and if you remove what is there on the first try, that is good; if not, start again the second and third day until everything is scraped; and be aware that teeth require various shapes of tools for scraping, according to what the craftsman demonstrates, because the scrapers used to scrape the teeth have different shapes from those used to scrape between the teeth; and these and other forms must be prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary, when treating a toothache, to delay pulling it out as much as possible, for this should never be done; because it is a substance quite high up until such a time that there is no excuse for scraping.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then, when the patient insists on having it pulled, you must be certain of the aching tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain deceives the patient, and they believe it is in a healthy tooth, and they have a good tooth pulled; nevertheless, the pain does not depart by this, until the bad tooth is extracted, because we have already wanted to do this to our masters; and when you are certain of the aching tooth, you must scrape around the tooth thoroughly with a strong spatula to protect the gums on all sides; then grasp it with your fingers or with fine pliers, pulling and pulling gently until it is well loosened, then firmly grasp the pliers; and the patient's head should be in your lap between your knees, and hold it firmly so it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	Afterwards, extract the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not easily come out, use one of these instruments and gently push it from each side, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and decayed, you must fill it with linen where the holes are; and carefully grasp it with pliers so it does not break when you pull; and you must work very cautiously around the gums to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be very careful not to break it and leave a piece behind, which will return to the patient, causing greater pain from the root than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware that you do not do as the ignorant do, who, through their haste and boldness, sometimes break the jawbone, and do not achieve what we have described; but they sometimes cause great illness due to the roots that remain or because they broke the jawbone, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is extracted, wash the area with wine, or vinegar and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, fill the area with powdered vitriol; and if that is not sufficient, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments used to pull teeth initially should have long points and thick handles so that they do not bend when you pull the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should have thick members so that they do not bend when pulling, and they should be of well-made, strong iron, and be toothed to hold the teeth.
de la racine des dens	of the roots of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains after extraction, you should place cotton soaked in butter on the area for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the area is softened, then use the pliers called "algefri", whose shape resembles a bird's beak; and they should be made like a file, and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots will not come out with these pliers, you must expose the flesh all around the root, and apply the instrument called "althali", that is to say, a wedge, whose shape is:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it should be strong and thick so as not to break, and if the root comes out with this, it is good; if not, use all the instruments whose shapes are shown below:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument that has two prongs, whose shape is shown here:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are shown in the illustration of the teeth, and this instrument that looks like large pliers, whose shape is:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And these instruments should be strong enough not to break, and know that many dental tools exist; and also other instruments, that are not listed; and the skilled and clever master finds his own instrument according to the work and the patient's condition, because there are such diseases where the ancients did not teach any instrument due to the diversity of others; and if you break a bone or other bone that you should have, then seek the necessary instruments that I have told you, and use the gestures whose shapes are:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and firm to hold the bone, so that it doesn't slip, but that it can be held and removed; and then restore the place with appropriate medicines, and if there is a small rot in the bone, remove it with all these instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural body, and its shape is unsightly, especially in young women, you must know if the tooth is growing after another tooth and is not in the correct place and cannot be smoothed or filed; then, remove it; and if it is growing alongside the tooth, take this instrument, whose shape is like a small beak, and is made of sharp, pointed steel:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And cut it little by little over several days due to the tooth's hardness and so that you don't move the others, and if it appears possible to file it, file it with a file like the one shown here:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file used to make needles; and file the tooth little by little over several days gently, so that it does not move until it is gone; then smooth it at the end with a rasp, and if the tooth is too sharp and injures the tongue, then file the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not injure the tongue or impair speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth loosens
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front teeth loosen, either from impact or falling, and the patient cannot bite without them falling out, and you have treated them with astringent medicines, and this is not working; then you must bind them with a gold thread, for silver thread turns green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you want to straighten the teeth, take the thread and place it doubled between two healthy teeth, then place the ends between the loose teeth, if there is one or more, until you carefully reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then continue the wrapping back to the point where you started, and gently and skillfully tighten your hold so that it does not move; and keep your binding at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the ends of the thread with pliers, assemble them, and rejoin them between the healthy tooth, and position it so that it does not injure the tongue; and then leave it as tight as it can remain, and if it loosens, or the thread breaks, bind it with another thread; it will remain and serve thus for its entire time, and this is the form of the teeth and the method of straightening the two healthy and two loose teeth, as you can see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, it is put back in its place, little by little, as we have said; and no one should meddle with it who is not wise and skillful, and sometimes one makes a form of a cow's tooth of bone, and places it in the place where it is missing and binds it as we have said, and it remains and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut the tongue's ligament
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this ligament under the tongue is congenital, or arises from a healed wound; and the procedure is as follows: you open the patient's mouth, holding their head steady, and lift the tongue; then cut the nerve ligament from the side, so that the tongue is loosened from its attachment, and if there is hardness or swelling, due to a healed wound, use a hook and cut that ligament from the side; and be careful that the incision is not too deep, due to the artery underneath; and when you are done, cleanse the area with rose water and oil, or cold water, then place a linen pad under the tongue; and the patient should keep it there every night, so that the wound cannot heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding occurs, apply powdered vitriol to the area; and if the blood is excessive, cauterize it with a small cautery iron, which is suitable for this; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see a dark, black, or hard discoloration, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is tending toward whiteness, and there is moisture, use a small hook and split it open with a fine spatula, and remove it from both sides; and if the bleeding is excessive during your work, apply powdered vitriol until it stops, then return to your work until you remove all the matter; then cleanse the area with oil and salt, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes boils called "godath" appear in the throat, properly called the two tonsils; and when treating them, as we have described in the division, if they are not healed, be careful: if they are hard abscesses with small, dark-colored heads, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also because of the bleeding; but let it mature, and then you will lance it, or it will break open on its own; and if it is pale white, and the root is small, prepare your instrument for cutting, but first check if the abscess is warm and calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then have the patient sit facing the sun, and his head should be supported, and let him open his mouth and the surgeon grasp his tongue underneath the instrument, which is shaped like a small knife.  It should be made of silver or fine bronze.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	When you press the tongue with this instrument and see the abscess, take a lancet and insert it into the tonsil, and draw it upwards as much as possible; and draw out any matter with it, then cut it with the instrument, which is shaped like a pair of tweezers.  Its tips are bent, one towards the other, and are very sharp; and it is made of iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument, cut it with pliers, which are shaped like this:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And it should be sharp on one side and blunt on the other.  And when you have cut one tonsil, cut the other in the same manner.  Afterwards, have the patient gargle with warm, clear water.  If bleeding occurs, have the patient gargle with water or boiled pomegranate bark or myrtle leaves, or similar things, until the bleeding stops.  Then treat it until it is healed.  And sometimes other abscesses form in the throat besides the two tonsils; in that case, cut them in the same way as the two tonsils.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that had formed in her throat, namely a small abscess.  The entire throat was almost completely closed, so that the woman could not breathe because the passage was blocked, and she could not eat or drink.  She would have died if she had stayed like that for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had grown so large that it had pushed two ribs through the two nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened then, and inserted a lancet into one nostril, and then pulled it out, and a large portion of pus came out.  Then I did the same in the other nostril, and opened her mouth and pressed on her tongue; afterward, I inserted the lancet into the abscesses and cut away a portion, and only a little blood came out.  And thus the passage in the woman's throat was opened, and she began to drink water, then wine, and I continued to cut away at the abscess for a long time.  The abscess would repeatedly grow back and fill the space I had emptied, until it became very large.  Then I cauterized it within the throat.  Then it stopped growing.  I left the woman, and I do not know what God did to her after that.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When rheum descends to the eye, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is swollen beneath, large and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have described in the division, and the treatment does not work, and you see that the inflamed abscess is calmed, and it is subtle, then you must cut it; and if it is round, collected, and not long, and it is sanguine or a dusky color or black, then you must avoid cutting it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner I have described, of its whiteness and length, you must make the patient sit before the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument of which we have made mention previously; then, pierce the eye with the awl, draw it underneath, and cut it at one of the two instruments that I have mentioned in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not cut more than the excess that is beyond the natural limit; for if you cut more, you injure the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said about the incision of the two almonds, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient is afraid of the cutting, you must use a method of cauterization to allay the fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of cautery is sharp, sharp.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient should place their head in your hand, then press their tongue with the instrument we mentioned in the cautery chapter, and cauterize with sharp, hot irons, so that they are not too thick nor too thin; and apply the head of this instrument, of which this is the shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And there should be a receptacle on the head where the medicine is placed, like the bowl of a spoon, and place the instrument with all the medicine on the ulcer; and the patient should lie on their side, so that the saliva and mucus run from their mouth into the medicine, so that it does not run down into the throat, and hurt it; then hold your hand with all the medicine and press it against the ulcer for half an hour, until you see it healed and the medicine's burns are appeased; and if you wish, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and soak the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument with the cotton to the wound, so that the cotton sticks to the ulcer; and do this often until the cauterization is complete, then let it dry, and it will fall off after four or five days. And if you need to re-cauterize with medicine, do so, and after the cauterization, wipe around the ulcer with cotton soaked in butter, and clean the area around the medicine; and rinse with cold water, and treat with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is more effective than cutting, than cautery; if it is treated with fumigation according to this method, take calamint and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and yarrow and similar herbs, and put them all, or some of them, in a pot, and add oil to it, and boil it; and the pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and inside the pot there should be an instrument shaped like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be of silver or bronze, and one of the heads should be placed in the patient's mouth so that the vapor rises to the ulcer through the wound, until the ulcer is dead; then do it again often until the ulcer dries; and be careful not to do this at the beginning of a hot abscess, because many things happen; and do not do this except at the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not available, take a tube and place a raw egg inside the head, so that the patient's mouth is not too hot; because the raw egg prevents the vapor from burning the mouth, and it is a good treatment overall and healthy.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times bone or fish spine, or some other thing, gets stuck in the throat; so you should pull out what you can see, and press the tongue toward the sun with the whole instrument, so that you see the object move; and what is not visible and is stuck in the throat, you must make the patient vomit before the food is digested in the stomach; perhaps the object will come out with the vomit; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie a thread to the sponge, then they swallow it; and when it reaches the location, it will adhere, and you will then pull it out; and if it does not come out by what we have said, then take a lead instrument in this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the head so that it can enter the throat more easily, and have the head lifted high; and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, so that no harm comes to it, nor push the bone in; it is better if the patient pushes the instrument, so that it moves where the object is stuck; push it down, or pull it out with the whole instrument equally, until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the leech of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes the leech is medicated, as I have said in the division, by medical treatment; and when this does not work, then look into the patient's throat with the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the leech, then pull it out with a small hook, or with fine pliers that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this doesn't work, take a heated chain, and put it in the patient's throat, then put a hot iron at the end of the chain, and do this repeatedly.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is feverish all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, and open the mouth, and pour it in without swallowing, and move it with his hand often; and as soon as the leech feels the water, it will fall.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida, with the instrument that I have mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will fall without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the method of fumigation is that you take a pot in which there are glowing charcoal embers, and the pot is covered with a pierced lid, and through that hole is the end of the instrument; then put your fumigation in it, and the patient puts the end of the chain in his mouth, and closes his mouth tightly, so that the smoke does not come out, but goes directly to the leech; and the leech will now fall, and if it does not fall, then restart the fumigation many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty and dry things, and drink no water; and then it will be necessary for it to come out forcefully by this method.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which one pulls the leech, is, when one can see it, like bent tongs for entering the throat; and it resembles the beak of a bird, and there is roughness like a file, so that what it takes, it cannot leave; and see here the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many kinds of abscesses exist, according to what remembrance comes next from one and another in this book, and they are diverse in perforation and incision; and there are two types, one being in its own appearance, and the other in what moisture it holds.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second type is according to the locations where they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and abscesses of fleshy areas are different from those that occur in joints, and each has its own judgment in practice.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the swelling is ripe according to its completion; and there are those that must be pierced when they are inflamed but do not ripen according to their completion, such as abscesses near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when an abscess develops near a joint, and one leaves it to rot around, the ligaments and nerves of the joint may be damaged, which causes contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Where the abscess is near the main limb, and you delay perforation until it is ripe, it will harm the main limb; or if it is near the foundation, it should be pierced before it is ripe; and you should not pierce an inflamed abscess without complete digestion, except for those near the foundation, lest it rot deeply, spread inside, and cause a fistula, and it cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the time to pierce a ripe abscess according to its completion, which is when the pain subsides, the fever subsides, the pain and redness diminish, and the swelling and sharpness of the abscess head, and the other signs; and you must make the incision at the most dependent part of the abscess, where it appears to be moving; and the incision should be along the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places equally where there is no skin fold.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that bend, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy area, it is better to leave the perforation until it is fully digested, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before that, the poison's body will spread, and it will be full of foul matter; and perhaps the edges and the depth of it will harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And some abscesses should be pierced according to the breadth of the body, according to the limb's need.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you must make small perforations in small abscesses; and large perforations, and many incisions, according to the size of the abscess; and some abscesses require a lancing of the core, and cutting; when it has become like a flap, and has subsided, you must do the same as with boils; and some are cut into three angles, and some are cut like myrtle leaves, like abscesses of the groin; and some have a round incision, and other cuts and similar incisions.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those that do not have a head, like a superficial soft abscess, you must pierce completely; and when the abscess is large, and it has collected a lot of pus, and you pierce it, do not remove all the pus at once, but remove a part; then bandage the abscess until the next day, then remove some more; do this repeatedly, gradually, until all the pus is out; especially if the patient is weak, or a pregnant woman, or small children, or decrepit old men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirit sometimes jumps with the outflow of pus, so that the patient might die, and you do not realize it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, approach this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced the abscess, dry the wound and see if the abscess wound is small; and if it is a clean incision, place linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many incisions, you must place a bandage in each so that they meet; and if you have cut a part of the skin in the abscess, and have cut around it, you must fill it with old cotton or linen rags without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then remove it and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs during your work, apply cold and easy water, and moisten a cloth, and place it repeatedly over the bleeding area.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, apply remedies and treatments, and the powders I have mentioned in this book in appropriate locations.  If it is winter and the area where the abscess is is very sensitive, you should place bandages and cloths soaked in warm wine and oil; if it is summer and the area is fleshy, you should apply cloths soaked in water and oil, or cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said.  Then open the abscess, dry it and treat it as necessary until healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this should be universally known in treating abscesses: now I have told you how to proceed with treating abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where the head's core comes small abscesses, and there are various types, such as those in webs, like the yolk of an egg, and many similar ones.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	Some are fatty and contain moisture, like pus; and others are hard and stony to cut, and there is no doubt if the artery does not oppose it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the incision is that you test with any instrument called an "entromissor," of which the form will appear afterwards, what thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then cut it along the length.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is emptied, then cauterize without leaving the skin containing that moisture, for it returns often when one leaves anything; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if present; otherwise, in water and salt, and fill the wound with it, and leave it until the next day; and this will dry that which remained from the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then repeat the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that nothing remains from the night; then treat the wound with ointment suitable to it, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds a thick fat, then cut it along this shape, lengthwise; and apply your cauteries, and cauterize it from all sides, and put all your treatment to draw out the force where it lies; and if the artery resists you, then do what I have told you afterward.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And likewise do for an abscess if it is stony, and in cutting and treating it, as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the cut on a stony and moist abscess is easier, because they are of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses are in the head where there is no moisture, and this was the abscess that I cut on the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess as hard as a rough, white stone, and could not break it; and if one had struck it, one would have made a wound as with a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming to the head, other than those that come to the heads of children and to the roots of the ears, the opening should always be in the most dependent place, to let the pus escape; and treat them as appropriate.
des scrophules	of the scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses occur on the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they come elsewhere on the body, and are numerous, and are interwoven together.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofulous boil is properly within its own tissue, just like the pustules and abscesses of the head, as we have said; and the appearances of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are malignant ones that will not obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In the one, then, that you see of good disposition upon touch, and is similar in color to the body, and is soft on all sides and is not near the nerves of the neck nor to the artery nor to the conduit, and is not deep; you should cut it from above, and scrape it from every part, and spread the two lips of the wound with forceps, if you need them, as we have said for abscesses of the head; and draw it out little by little, and be careful that you do not cut the nerve or vein, and let the lancet not be sharp or sharp-edged, lest your hand slip and go too far, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and this hinders your work, then put powdered vitriol or some other blood-stopping powder into the wound, and compress the wound; and leave it until the abscess is calmed and the wound softens and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood is stopped, return to your work until you complete it; then look with your index finger if there remain any small boils, and cut and cleanse them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein in the root of the boil, you should not cut that boil at its root, but tie it with a strong doubled thread, and let it fall off by itself, without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, and then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut the entire boil, you must bring together the two lips of the wound and stitch them now, since there has remained no excess due to the size of the boil.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	then you must proceed to cut the root of it, and draw it out, and stitch it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those boils that contain excess matter, pierce where it appears ripe; and pierce it thus as the previously mentioned one, in dependence, then apply poultices with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what has remained of the corruption; and when the wound is cleansed, treat it with healing ointment until it is healed.
de squinance	of quinsey
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the incision of the throat; but I have never seen anyone in our land who performed it, and this is the record of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those with quinsey, it is necessary that the slit in the throat, called the "epiglottis," be drained; and no help should be given through this, because all the veins and the internal organs of the sick person are affected by those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or throat, or in the tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the lung, it is necessary to cut the epiglottis to avoid the death that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, we must cut it below three or four small transverse slits, between the two circles or by the amount of the slit on the surface, not into the cartilage; and that place is so suitable for cutting the epiglottis that there is no flesh there, and the vessels are far away.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is afraid, he must stretch the skin of the throat all the way, then cut the skin until it reaches the channel; and drain the blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cut the surface, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the cutting of the phlegm from the channel which jumps out through the broken place, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a time.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the time has passed where strangulation is feared, bring together the two edges of the wound on the skin, and stitch it all together without the cartilage; then administer medicines that promote healing, until it is sound.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says that one should not do this until the throat is completely obstructed, and the patient is judged to be dying, and the breath fails.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then the epiglottis is cut so that the patient cannot breathe, and they breathe through the wound, and thus are saved from death; and for this reason, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease has passed, and it passes in three or four days. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and cure it, until it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw a young lady take a knife and stab it into her throat, cutting part of the channels of the windpipe; and I was called to treat her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound, and found the blood that had issued from it, and saw clearly that she had not cut any vein or artery except the throat, and the breath was issuing through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried and sewed up the wound, and treated it until it was healed; and the young lady suffered only a sore throat, and returned to her normal condition; therefore I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis there is no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat," and is a large abscess the color of a yolk, and is very common in women; and it is according to two types: natural, and accidental; where the natural has no cure.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental is according to two types, of which one is similar to fatty tissues, and the other type is similar to an abscess that comes from an artery; and there is fear, and one should not operate with fire except in the small ones, and prove and search throughout the surrounding area: if you find it like a fatty tissue, and it doesn't connect to any vein, then cut it, as one cuts tissues, and remove all its covering if there is any; and search well throughout, and treat it as necessary, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	of the tissues
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many types of tissues are there, of which I will describe all the appearances; and now it is necessary that I state the entire difference between tissue and issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that issue is heat and fever while the boiling is ongoing, and the putrefaction is complete; then the fever and heat cease.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With tissue, there is neither heat, nor fever, nor pain, and it contains a surface, which is its own sack and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a blister, and becomes large; and they are according to two appearances, either fatty or moist, and many colors are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to treat the tissue, that you first examine and inquire into it using all the instruments called "entromissoires," according to what its form will be in the chapter that comes after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the method of investigating abscesses of tissues is that you should take the moistest spot you find in the abscess and turn your fingers little by little until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, as is suitable for the size of the abscess; then withdraw the instrument, and be careful lest it should break.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If running moisture flows, whatever color it has, lance it as I have said of other abscesses; and if after the instrument no moisture comes, know that it is fatty, then lance it in a cross shape, and take it with forceps, and lightly scrape it from each side and be careful of the skin in which it lies, so that you remove it whole with the tissue; and if you cannot remove it whole, remove it in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if anything remains, the tissue will return many times; and if a little remains, and the blood bothers you, then fill the wound with some sharp, corrosive powders, and compress the wound, and apply soothing, hot remedies for the abscess, and treat it with other cures until it is healed; and if the tissue is large, cut the two edges of the wound, and treat it with what generates flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the throbbing vein is against you or otherwise, hurry and fill the place with crushed vitriol, and leave it for two or three days, until the wound rots and the boiling of the blood subsides; then return to cutting whatever remains of the tissue.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the shapes of the probing instruments, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and of them there are three squares, called "albaret", and one called "breb", and of them there are three kinds: large, medium, and small, for searching abscesses of fistulas; and they are like the needles with which sorceresses are sewn, and are of yellow copper, or iron, or silver, and the yellow ones are more effective, and are more proven with black lead for probing fistulous sores; and are of three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the amount of the width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of the forceps are of many similar types, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are forceps that have two curves of three kinds as well; and there are forceps that have three curves, and are also of three kinds; and there are forceps that have two curves, and forceps of one curve only, and are of three kinds; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of those with which one cuts are sharp, and of such there are some that do not cut much except on one side, with which one scrapes the tissues, so that one does not cut the vein or the nerve; and of these probes are the probes fitted into handles, so that the patient does not feel them during the opening of abscesses; and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one does not use them much except in fleshy places, such as legs, and arms, and breasts, and sores, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another small instrument, similar to the scraping of fistulae, according to this shape, with which one stops the blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is sometimes placed in the area that bleeds from cuts of veins and arteries, and sometimes according to this large shape:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, so that they seem like women's breasts; and they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, it must be done according to this shape of this line .b. up to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then scrape off the fat, and fill the wound with a medicine that generates flesh, then bring together the two edges of the wound with stitches, and treat it until it is healed; and if the breast sags and is softened due to its size as happens in women, then split it into two sides above, by two similar cuts; of which one must be attached to the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this shape, from this line .b. up to the line .g.; then scrape off the skin that is between the two edges, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitches and powders, and what is necessary in the treatment, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not entirely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the flow of blood, then you must fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it melts the remaining flesh and fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	Of the abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the armpits are a type of hard scrofulous swelling, or if there are bumps, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this shape, from line .b. up to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess has been drained, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with an appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is like scrofulous swellings, then lance it as we have said in lancing scrofulous swellings, and if the wound returns pus, apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is ruptured, and the skin is closed over it, abscesses often result, and likewise it occurs in a swollen vein and abscess; and one recognizes it as being from the artery when the abscess is long and deep; and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel a tightening; and when it is from the vein, there are noticeable swellings; and it is folly to cut this abscess, especially when it is under the armpits, and in the groin, and neck, and in many other places, and is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary then to avoid the iron treatment, and the one that is chief should also be avoided, and in one that is from the swelling of an artery, lance it through the skin lengthways; then open the incision with a lancet, and carefully separate the artery from the tissues, until it is exposed; then insert a needle underneath and make it pierce to the other side, and tie the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then puncture the area between the two ligatures with an instrument until the blood that is there is released, and the abscess is relieved; then apply the treatment that removes pus, until the ligature falls out; then treat it with an appropriate ointment until it is healed; and if the abscess is from a wound of a vein, you must hold in your hand the part of the abscess that is over all the skin, then insert the needle under the place you are holding in your hand, and pierce it, and put a double thread, so that you pull it from the other side; then tie the abscess as I have told you, or the ligature on one of the two sides on the two ends of the thread; and if you doubt that the thread will not come out, then reinsert another needle into the thread underneath the whole abscess at the incision of the first needle, and tie the threads in four places; then cut the abscess until the excess comes out, then cut the excess of the core and leave what is tied; then put a cloth moistened with wine and oil over it, and apply dressings and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
