Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses come to the artery and vein, abscesses come to the nerves when they are injured, or through excessive labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often to the shoulders and hands and in all places where there are joints, and it is a grievous abscess, and its color resembles the color of the body, and is in various states with pain; and when it is squeezed tightly, the patient feels pain, and it is not deep within the body, but under the skin; and moves freely in all directions, and does not go forward or backward, or underneath or above, and one that is in a joint should not be cut with iron, lest a contraction results; and one that is on the head or forehead, lance the skin with a lancet.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with pincers and cut it at its root; and if it is large, lance it with a lancet, and scrape it, then remove it and stitch the wound together, and treat it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of large hanging boils
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes this happens in the belly and nowhere else, a disease called "fungus" because of its resemblance to them, with a subtle root and a large head; and there are small and very large ones; and I saw a man who had two in his belly that were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, they were white, with fine roots, and often split open and ran with moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them and found eighteen ounces in one, and six in the other, and the method in the incision is that you look to see if the patient is moist, and the color of the tumor is white and moist and of subtle root; then cut it with a wide scalpel, and have the fire cautery present.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For when cutting, there often comes too great a flow of blood, and if the blood overcomes you, then hurry with the cautery; and if you see the patient frightened and afraid of the iron incision, take a well-made lead thread and tie the tumor as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then tighten it, and do not stop tightening the lead thread until it cuts the tumor and breaks it without effort; and if the roots are large, there is fear of cutting, especially in the belly, but you can well cut the half, then cauterize it so it does not return; then treat the wound, and take care that you do not cut the tumor which is of a fixed color and of poor sense and milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is a festering abscess, and I will come to the treatment of ulcers afterwards.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the boil is ripe.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the boil appears from a cauterized wound or a rupture of the skin, and is on the abdomen and some boils emerge, as happens in other ruptures, or from blood flowing from veins or arteries according to what is before, or from wind; and if it is due to a skin rupture and the emergence of the boil, the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and is a slight thing without pain, and shows various exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the issue of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when pressed with one's fingers, it recedes and then returns, and perhaps it is hard, and grows greatly at the entrance of the bath and due to strenuous labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a slight thing, and shows well when you press it with your hand, nor does it constrain; and if it is due to blood, the abscess appears large and hard, and is fixed according to a certain quantity; and if it is due to wind, it is soft to the touch, and the work is that you look to see if the appearance is due to blood from the artery, or vein, or wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	Then you should leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, due to the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is due to the intestine or the bowel, you should instruct the patient to hold their breath, and be stretched out completely straight, then make a sign around the whole area; then instruct them to lie still between your hands, then go around the area you have marked with the entire spatula, then extend half of the abscess above the whole large incision; then tie it around with a strong thread, or a strong silk cord tightly, and let the knot of the tie be loose; then open the half of the abscess stretched above the tie, and put your index finger in, and search for the intestine; if you find it held by the tie, untie it, and put the intestine back out of the belly; and if you find the bowel, take it with the incision, and cut off the excess; and if the artery or vein opposes you, go around gently, then return to your work and take two needles, and put two strong threads on them, and put the two needles around what you have made in the cross that you made pierce; then constrain the abscess in four places above the needles, and if you wish, remove the needles, and leave the area until it rots, and the dead flesh falls off on its own; or you cut it when it is softened and rotten, then treat it as necessary, and close the abscess as we have said; and remove the blood or moisture you find, then treat the area as needed, and close it.
dou chancre	of the chancre
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have discussed the types of chancre, and how one should work on them with medicine, and how one should avoid iron treatment; and we say that chancre forms in the flesh, and great caution is needed in its treatment, and the ancients said that when chancre is in a place where it can be scraped off, like chancre in the breasts, and in the thigh, and similar places, it should be completely removed when it is in the beginning; and when it is large and old, you should not approach it, for I have never been able to heal one; nor has anyone healed one before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile several times; then make them bleed if there is a clear excess, then prepare a good place for the procedure; then apply your incisions to the chancre and close it on all sides, and remove it from everywhere without leaving anything; and let the blood flow freely, and press the area well with your hand or something else, and if the flow of blood causes you to hit the artery or vein with the incision, cauterize it until the bleeding stops; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already discussed the types of dropsy, how the accumulation of water occurs, the signs of each type, and the treatment using medicine and iron; the treatment is sometimes by cauterization alone; and one should not use iron in these two types: namely, tympanites and yposarche, because that is a fatal thing; therefore, when you treat this type of dropsy called "eclites" with medicine, and the treatment does not work, look to see if the patient is weak, or if they have another illness in addition to the dropsy, such as diarrhea and similar things; do not use iron, for there is doubt; and if you see a patient of strong constitution, and they have only dropsy and are not too young or too old, then you should proceed as follows: lift the patient upright in your hands, and press their belly by pushing the water to the lowest part of the body; then take a pointed spatula according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And it should be sharp on two sides.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And it should be pointed, and yet not so sharp that it can penetrate to the intestines when inserted, and cannot injure them; then see if the dropsy is in the intestines:  it is necessary to cut above the rib on the right side of the incision; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, make your cut on the left side of the third rib; and if it is due to the spleen, make the cut on the right, and the patient should not lie on the cut so that the excess fluids do not run to that weakened area; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and insert it, and lift your hand with all the spatula between the skin and the surface as if removing a scab at the depth of a fingernail or so; then pierce the surface until the spatula reaches the hollow place, and that is the location of the fluid, then drain it completely, and insert this instrument, which has this shape:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it resembles a thin silver chain, and is made of bronze or light metal, and has one small hole at the bottom, and three holes on one side, and two on another, and one on the other; and the tip is cut like a feather, and that is the shape of the incision, which the scribe makes when cutting a feather:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top is a flap, so that when the instrument reaches the fluid, it immediately descends onto the instrument; empty it then by half or a third, for if you empty more than is necessary at that moment, perhaps the patient will die from the resolution of their spirit from the instrument, or they will fall weak, or they will approach death; but empty it according to the extent of their strength, and according to the signs of the patient's constitution and their pulse; then remove the instrument and hold the fluid, and it is now held because of the diaphragm which seals the hole that is on the surface, of which I spoke, that you pierce according to this manner; then repeat the instrument the next day, if you see the patient tolerating it, and remove a small amount of fluid; do this for several days, and be careful not to overdo it so that there remains only a small amount of fluid.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt about the patient, and you leave a lot of fluid, treat him with warm baths or hot sand, and through sweat or bathing in the sun, and make him drink; and treat him with drying medicines until he is healthy, and cauterize above the stomach and the liver and the spleen after removing the fluid, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Of the stoppage of the penis.
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born who have no opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary, quickly pierce it with a very thin needle according to this shape:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then put a thin lead plug in the opening, and tie it, and keep it this way for three or four days.  When he wants to urinate, remove the plug, let him urinate, and then replace it; and perhaps it is not necessary, because the urine that comes out will not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	For those whose opening is small, be treated with a lead plug, as we have said, and it will widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the opening in its place are injured, for some are born with the opening at the top of the penis, so they cannot urinate until they raise their penis; and they cannot impregnate because the material cannot reach the testicles, and this is a serious illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the method of the operation is that the patient lies often on his back, then extends the top of the penis and cuts it like the slice of a feather, so that the opening falls in the middle, as is necessary.  And be careful of bleeding that often occurs, and if it happens, stop it with what stops blood, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	Boils on the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often these ulcers appear on the penis, and there is an appearance of foul flesh; and some are malignant and some are not; so you must take them with a fine needle, and cut and clean them all, then apply moistened cotton with Egyptian ointment; then treat it with diafinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the ulcer is malignant, of foul color and smelling, you must apply cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cut it, and if the ulcer is on the shaft of the penis, and part of it is inside the skin and part outside, you must remove the ulcer that is inside first; and when it is healed, treat the outside part.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it together, the penis is not assured that it will not be pierced, and blackness and corruption come to the shaft and the glans; you must remove all that is black and corrupted, then apply a plaster of honey and flour made from pomegranate bark and poppy seeds, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if a discharge of blood comes, apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery helps in two situations together: namely, for blood discharge and for corruption; and if the penis shaft is corrupted and withdrawn, you should insert a lead pipe into the penis, and let the patient urinate through it; and when the skin is chafed at the head of the penis, which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or it happens due to a wound or an abscess, you must then scrape it with a sharp instrument until the adhesion is loosened, and the penis is freed from all sides; and if it is a difficult thing to separate it, you must scrape with a spatula a little bit of the head of the penis and the skin; then separate gently between the two, and put a thin linen cloth moistened in cold water, so that it does not chafe again.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a simple separation like other wounds; however, when we perform this operation of our own will, and properly on children, it is necessary that we do the best and least painful operation possible.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not perform circumcision on their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we only have what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen most of the masters and those who performed circumcision using a razor, and by force, and with an entire scalpel; the heart avoided it because there are two layers, and perhaps one is cut and the other remains.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Now, if it must be cut, the pain is doubled, and the cleansing of the foreskin does not ensure the tip of the member; and with the cleansing of the skin, the blade perhaps slips, and the work is marred, and many times they are born such that they do not require cleansing, and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the cleansing done with force, throughout the entire length of the thread, I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the force cuts justly both above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, it cuts equally in all directions at once; but let the thread be firmly around the skin; and let the manner of the first work be that you make the child think, if he understands, that you are only tying the thread around the penis, and make him happy in all the ways you can; then hold him between your hands upright, and hold the forceps between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand on the penis and blow on the heart, and pull it up until the head of the penis is inside; then clean it well of the dirt that has collected there, then tie the place with a double thread, then tie it under one stitch to another; and hold it with two fingers by the second bandage on the thumb and forefinger, and cut between the two bandages, then quickly lift the heart above and pull the head of the penis; then let the blood run slowly, because that is the cure; and put powder on top, and on top of the powder a thin layer of a cooked egg yolk mixed with rose water, mixed with good and fresh rose oil, and leave it there until the next day, and cure it with another cure until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The shape of the forceps for cleansing is this: the two heads should be thin and sharp, and the heads should be as large as the handles equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in cleansing occurs when the heart inside is at the incision; then you must extend it with your fingernail, so that the place does not form an abscess; and cut it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, hold it with pliers and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if three days pass, and that which is below the penis is swollen, leave it until the hot abscess subsides, and lightly scrape it; then cut it as you can, and be careful of the part of the penis, it will harm it not at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the place with the things suitable for a wound, as we said in the treatment of powders, and if one cuts too much of the heart, and it goes above, it will not harm; then cure it, as we said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	Concerning the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to obstruction by stones, or congealed blood, or pus, or dead flesh, or similar things, as we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to a stone lodged in the neck of the bladder, the patient should be bent over their knees, and their feet placed on their back, and the patient extend their stomach from the back, and the patient should hold their breath as much as possible; and then the neck of the bladder is constrained by the stone's expulsion, so that the urine is released; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, you must administer extraction with an instrument called a "syringe," of which this is the form: and it should be of fine, thin silver, like the feather of a bird; and the tube should be one and a half palms long, and thin at the end.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the method of releasing the urine is that you take a double thread, and tie a small piece of wool or cotton to the end, and put the end of the thread inside the syringe; and cut off the excess of wool and push it down to the end of the syringe, then lubricate the syringe with oil or butter and egg white, and have the patient sit on a seat, and lubricate the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and warm water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the root of the penis, then bend the penis upwards towards the groin; then insert the syringe further into the bladder, and the patient feels it go to the empty space, and this is not done according to this order often because the passage it goes through is twisted; then pull the thread slightly and slightly with the wool, and the urine follows the wool, then pull it out quickly, and cause the urine to flow; and repeat the use of the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient should be relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	Of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scabs or blood comes into the bladder, or putrefaction gathers there, and you want to apply liquids and medicines, use an instrument called a "clepsydra," and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and has three openings: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the narrow passage through which the medicine flows should be such that it fits snugly around the penis without additional pressure, so that moisture can be drawn out and applied as needed; and when you wish to inject your medicines into the bladder, insert the end of the applicator into the moisture, and draw on the string that is inside; you will draw the moisture into the applicator, and then forcefully push the string back in; the moisture will enter, and go directly to the bladder so that the patient will feel it; and this is the form of a thin enema tube used for enemas in the bladder: it is like this:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is made of silver or bronze, and the tip is higher; and below it is a narrowing where the tubing falls; then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture you wish to use for the enema into it, then tie it between the two narrow points with a strong double thread, and heat a small amount of that moisture over the fire; then insert the end of the enema tube into the penis, and firmly squeeze the bladder with your hand until the moisture is delivered to the bladder; and if you do not have a sheep's bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle out of it, and pierce it around the edges; then insert a strong thread into these openings, then assemble the circle like an envelope, and put inside it what you wish of oil, moisture, and water, and tie it to the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, by squeezing with your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	Of the stone.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already discussed the types of stones, and their removal along with medicines; and I have explained the differences between stones lodged in the kidneys, and all the signs, and in which stones surgical intervention is appropriate; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you this clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that stones lodged in the bladder occur more often in children, and this is a sign that the urine escaping from the bladder is similar to water in its thinness; and there is a presence of sand, and the patient rubs their penis, and often bends over, and then stiffens; and many of these instances involve the foundation; and it is easier to heal children up to four years old, and it is more serious in the elderly, and is moderate in those between youth and old age; and it is easier to treat those with large stones than those with small stones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is first necessary to cleanse the patient with an enema, to remove all the waste matter from the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it sometimes hinders the search for the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and lift and move them downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes emerges from a higher position; then have him sit between your hands prepared, and his hands beneath his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely inclined downwards; then seek and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in the space, then hurry now to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not come out entirely on touching, then moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger if the patient is a grown youth; and put it on his foundation, and seek the stone, and when you feel it on your finger, draw it to the neck of the bladder; then press on your finger and push it towards the outside where you want to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the attendant to press the bladder with his hand, and instruct him to extend his right hand upwards towards the testicles, and with his left hand remove the skin beneath the testicles in the area where the incision is made; then insert the scalpel, whose shape is as follows:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And cut between that which is between the testicles and the foundation, not in the middle but on the side of the left groin; and keep it straight over the stone, and your fingers should be on the foundation; and let the incision be such that it is wide on the outside and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large; perhaps the pressure from the finger on the foundation will cause it to jump out without effort; and know that there are stones with angles and edges: these are difficult to remove; and there are some that are round, like a nut, and smooth, which are easy to remove.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	For those with angles and edges, make the incision larger; and if it does not come out, you must use tongs which are like a file at the tip, to press the stone so that it does not escape; or you insert a thin, curved instrument under it; and if you cannot extract it thus, enlarge the opening slightly, and if the blood flows, bind it with vitriol; and if there is more than one stone, remove the largest first to the neck of the bladder, then cut and push out, and remove the smaller ones afterwards if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it must be softened, and a larger wound made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or his urine comes out frequently through a gap that the wound cannot close; but nevertheless, strive to pull it out or break it with tongs until you pull it out in pieces; and when you have completed your work, fill the wound with incense, aloe, and dragon's blood, and bind it, and put a cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, over it to soothe the hot inflammation; then place the patient on their back, and do not loosen the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen it, wash the area well with oil and water, then treat it with diafinicon and basilicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if hot abscesses, corrosion, and blood clots form in the bladder, and the urine is retained in such a way that blood comes out with the urine: then insert your finger into the wound and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will damage and rot the bladder; then cleanse the wound with water, and vinegar, and salt, and help him in all the ways you know, until he is healed; and you must bind his thighs every time you treat him, and apply the medicines to the area.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small and lodged in the urethra, and the urine cannot pass; treat it as I have previously described, cutting it many times, and the cutting is excused by this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already tested this thus.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take an iron rod shaped like this, with three angled points forming a single branch.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the urethra below the stone, so it cannot return to the bladder; then gently insert the rod into the urethra until it reaches the stone; and turn the rod in your hand against the stone bit by bit until you can pierce the stone from the other side; then the urine will immediately flow, then press your hand on what remains of the stone inside the urethra.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is immediately broken, and it leaps out with the urine, and the patient is cured; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, tie a thread below the stone and another above, then cut the urethra at the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, and untie the thread, and cleanse the congealed blood that is in the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	Of the stone in women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	Sometimes a stone is lodged in women, and if it happens, the cure is difficult, and is forbidden for three reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a knowledgeable woman who will reveal herself to physicians, especially if she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that perhaps one cannot find a knowledgeable woman in this art of hands; and the fourth way is that the stone in a woman is deeper than the stone in a man, so that it is necessary to make a deeper incision, and there is great fear.  And if necessity commands it, you must take a knowledgeable midwife, and one is hardly found. If you find none, seek a discreet, experienced midwife; and present a wise woman experienced in the lives of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and instruct her to perform what you order her in the investigation of the stone; and carefully consider if the woman is a virgin.  Then she must insert her finger into the woman's opening and seek the stone. If she finds it, she must restrain it under her finger.  And instruct her to place her finger where the ailment is, and search for and press her left hand firmly on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, she must move it gently from the entrance of the bladder down to the base of the thigh, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then cut near the stone at the root of the thigh, near the middle of the opening, where the stone is most apparent, and feel for the stone in that area.  And do not move her finger over or under the stone, and let the incision be initially small; then, using the instrument, enlarge the incision if you feel the stone, so that the stone can be pulled out. And know that there are many kinds of stones: namely, small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and those with ridges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	So you know the signs to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if blood overwhelms you, apply crushed vitriol to the area, and hold it for an hour until the blood is stopped; then return to your work until the stone is removed, and have the instruments I mentioned for removing stones in men to help you in your work; and if blood overwhelms you, and it is from the cut artery, apply the powder to the area, and bind it with bandages and cloths, and do not resume this, and leave the stone and do not extract it, lest the patient die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood has subsided and the area is healed, then return to your work until the stone is removed.
de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Watery hernia is nothing more than a collection of moisture or white matter, which is under the core of the testicles, which contains the egg; and it is called "white matter," and sometimes is properly in the egg's fabric, so that one might think it is another egg; and it is the skin of the testicle between the white matter that we have mentioned; and this does not happen often.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this hernia comes from weakness in the testicles, and that matter is spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from a blow to the testicles, and this moisture has many colours: either it is a colour leaning towards jaundice, or it is without red, or black, or watery white, and this happens more often; and these are the signs of knowing this collection, for if it is the white matter that we have mentioned, it is a boil, a little long as the shape of an egg, and the testicle is not visible, because it is surrounded by moisture completely.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the fabric itself, the boil is attached to a part of the egg, and for this one thinks it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white matter, one feels it well; therefore, when you want to know the color of the moisture, you examine the whole indented area, of which the shape is before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, then, which comes after the indented area, judge what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, the patient must be bled as much as possible and his body emptied; then lay him on his back, on something a little high, and put many cloths under him; then sit him on his left side, and instruct the attendant to sit on the right, and extend the rod to one of the two sides of the testicles; then take the lancet, and cut the skin of the testicles along its length, from the place where the knife is, and make your incision straight in dividing the skin of the testicles to the white matter, and peel it carefully as much as you can; then pierce the white matter with water through a wide hole, and remove all the water, and then apply your forceps, and stretch the white matter upwards; and do not touch the core of the testicles, but only the white matter; cut all or by pieces, the side of it carefully, because if you do not cut it wisely, the water will return; and if the egg jumps out during your work, put it back in place when you have finished working on the white matter; then stitch the two sides of the testicles together, and treat it like other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the testicle corrupted by another illness, you must tie the vessels that are in suspension, fearing the flow of blood; then cut the testicle through the suspension, and remove the testicle, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the water is collected in two parts together, know that they are two branches; cut the other part in the same way you did the first, then dry the blood, and put moistened wool in rose oil in the wound; and put another wool moistened in wine and oil on the two testicles, and put doubled cloths on top, and bind it with all the bindings in accordance with this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and fill them with charpie wool according to this pattern, and they should be sewn together at the crotch of the breeches, and one of the ends should reach from the base to the back, and the other to the part where the knife is; and the other two ends should be on the two sides, and the whole constriction should be sewn into the buckle of the breeches; and sometimes this branch is treated with a cautery instead of an iron cut, and this is when you take a sharp cautery knife and cut the skin of the testicles, and it is heated as we have said, so that the white matter containing the water is uncovered; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that matter with forceps, and peel it with this sharp hot cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And cut it in every way you can, until you remove everything; and be careful that the fire does not touch the testicle; and know that this work is safer; and avoid the flow of blood, and be more cautious than the work of cutting; and if anything opposes you, or abscess, or bleeding, or anything else, treat what opposes you according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is afraid and does not want to undergo this operation because of its unpleasantness, administer a puncture, as I tell you; and this is that when you are certain, through the signs we have discussed, that the watery branch is present, have the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess on the lowest part, over the entire space, and make the puncture along the body; and the hole should be large so that all the water flows out; then put cotton on the area, and bandage it, and let the remaining water drain; then treat it until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the water to exit through the wound's opening, then you must put a tube or instrument to extract water from hydrotics, of which the shape has been described previously; and enlarge the wound a little, and know that the water returns and accumulates after six months or more, and when it accumulates as before, the patient will live for many days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the treatment of this branch, there is fear in many situations, for which it seems to me that it is better to leave it; and I will tell you about the treatment and the signs of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many abscesses arise in the body, and especially in the testicles; and this is in many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is to say, due to excess of acrid and sharp water, which spreads to the testicles, or from a blow; and the color of the abscess is according to the body's color; and it does not cause pain, and it is a serious abscess; and perhaps some serious abscesses are fearful and painful, and of fixed color, and sometimes it comes from a blood vessel rupture, or from vein inflammation.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from a blood vessel rupture, it is known by the hot nature of the abscess when you press it with your fingers; and you should not touch it at all.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	The one caused by vein inflammation is known by its appearance when pressed by the fingers, and one can well make the incision on this appearance, and on other parts of the body; and you should cut the testicles, then raise the testicle, and draw the white part away from the surface, and free the supporting tissue from all sides of the testicle.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the testicle is already attached to surrounding tissues, then you must pull the testicle and cut it; and if it is air-filled on the surface, or in the vessels within, you must release all the tension and cut it roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the attachment of the tissue is in the back, you must cut it all and remove the testicle, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is complete, fill the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess enveloped by a swelling resembling a boil, along with softening of the testicles, and the patient suffers greatly when walking; and the treatment for this illness is as perilous as the previous one, and nevertheless we will tell you the method of it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	You must have the patient sit on a raised seat, then lower the suspensory for the testicles to your fingertips, encompassing all the vessels near the penis, and the master must grasp and stretch them firmly; then, with a sharp, wide scalpel, cut through the tissue across the vessels until they are exposed, and then cauterize from each side, as we have stated in the extraction of arteries that are in the temples; then insert a needle with a double thread, and tie it to the initial point where the pus is, and re-tie it to the other end; then cut them straight in the middle, according to the length of the body, and extract the corrupted moisture; then treat the wound as with other wounds where pus forms, so that no vessels nourish either testicle; for this will not cause harm, and if pus reaches all the vessels, then you must separate the testicles from all vessels; so that the organ does not lose its nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and dries and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the rupture of the symphysis pubis
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The cause of this ailment arises from a rupture of the symphysis pubis, or an extension upon the abdomen in the groin area, causing the intestines to descend from that rupture to one of the testicles; and this rupture is either of the symphysis pubis, or of its extension, and these two types stem from many causes: either from impact, or a jump, or straining, or lifting heavy objects, and similar actions; and the signs when it is from the extension of the symphysis pubis, is that it occurs gradually, over a long period, and does not come suddenly; and the abscesses are even down to the depths, because the symphysis pubis is pressed against the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign when it is from a rupture of the symphysis pubis is that it causes sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscess appears diversely, under the skin nearby, due to the leakage of the intestines and the body away from the symphysis pubis.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the testicles descend with the intestines, and are trapped inside, causing the patient great pain, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these treatments there is fear of iron, therefore it should be avoided.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the method of treatment is that you instruct the patient to push the intestines back into the wound with your hand, if it can be returned; then hold it over their neck, between your hands, and lift the thighs; then extend the groin upwards, and cut all the skin from the testicles lengthwise; then insert the forceps of the necessary size to open the wound, so that the testicles can protrude; then scrape the symphysis pubis beneath the skin of the testicles until the hard white symphysis pubis is exposed from all sides; then insert your index finger into that which surrounds the testicle, into that which is between the white, hard symphysis pubis beneath the skin of the testicle and the second symphysis pubis; and separate that which is behind the testicle and between the second symphysis pubis; and then move your right hand inside the groin, and extend the white symphysis pubis upwards with your left hand, and raise the testicle with the entire symphysis pubis toward the groin; and instruct the assistant to lift the testicle upwards, and untie that which is above the knot; and feel with your fingers if there are any intestines wrapped around the hard white symphysis pubis, and if you find anything, push it back inside the abdomen; then take a needle with a strong thread made of ten strands, and place it in the rear part of the symphysis pubis, which is after the skin of the testicles; after the groin, then cut the ends of the threads until there are four threads; then join them one above the other in the shape of a cross, and bind the symphysis pubis, which we have said is beneath the skin of the testicles, with a strong bandage in two places; then wrap the ends of the threads and bind them in two places, so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter them, so that no suppurating abscess may occur; and put back the bandage according to the first bandage of two fingers of it; and after these two bandages leave the symphysis pubis that is beneath the groin the size of a finger; and after the rest according to the roundness that the testicle has; then cut in the area beneath the skin of the testicles, as long as the blood flows, and the wound heals, as we have said before; then apply oiled wool to the wounds, and apply the bandage we have described.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white symphysis pubis, which we have mentioned, is cauterized after the incision, due to fear of excessive bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens many times, and the bandage is left until it falls off by itself; and if it takes too long to fall off, it should be bathed in hot water, and apply what we have said, until it falls off; then treat the wound with another treatment, until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this procedure, I have never seen anyone who dared to perform the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is done like the procedure that joins the veins, in such a way that you tie the vessels, after the incision above or slightly below; then cut in half, and treat the abscess with what opens, until the vessel falls out; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
