Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes a rupture occurs in the groin, as we have said, and the opening appears; and none of the intestines descend into the scrotum, and if any descend, it is little, and it repairs itself at all hours; and nevertheless, if it remains too long in this condition, the wound or the hernia grows until the intestine descends; and this happens by the extension of the hernia in the groin, as we have said, for it is extended, then softened and swollen, the opening; and the treatment is by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes it is treated with iron in this way: and it is that the patient lies often on his back between your hands, then cuts the opening of the ruptured swelling with a width of three fingers; and then remove the hernia under the skin that surrounds it, then take a reed and place it on the visible part of the hernia; and press it deep into the abdomen, then stitch the two visible parts of the hernia onto the top of the reed, and stitch both; then remove the top of the reed, and do not cut the hernia or extend the egg or anything else, as I have told you in the treatment of the intestinal hernia; then treat it with the treatment for wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, cleanse it and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The hernia is constricted, and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cautery is milder in this place, and closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	Of the softening of the skin of the scrotum
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Often the skin of the scrotum is softened in some men, because the tissues within are softened, and it is noticeable; and it is necessary, when one wishes to cure it, that one make the sick person lie on his back, and cut the softened skin over the natural skin; then bring together the two edges with a stitch, and if you wish, first stitch the excess of softened skin with three or four firm stitches; then cut between the stitches, and treat it like other wounds, until it is healed, and the threads fall out.
dou chastrement	Of the castration
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that castration is forbidden in our law, and therefore I would not speak of it in this book; and it is necessary only for two reasons: one is that the physician should be able to answer when asked and to know the cure; and the other is that we often need to castrate certain animals to help us, such as goats, sheep, and cats, and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that castration is done in two ways: either by pulling, or by slitting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the way that we do by pulling, we make the animal sit in hot water, so that the testicles are softened and hanging; then grasp them in your hand, until they are retracted and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	For castration by cutting: you must restrain the animal, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory ligament, and cut each testicle with one stroke, once you have properly scorched them; and leave some of the fat and fine fat that is over the vessels; and this method of castration is gentler than the one done by pulling, because in the pulling, perhaps some of the testicles remain, which causes the animal to desire lust; then treat the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism in men is of two types: one is where, between the two testicles, there appears something like a woman's genitals, with hair, and sometimes urine flows from it.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other type is in women, and has a penis-like protrusion and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for both men and women is that you cut away all the added flesh and treat it like other wounds; in the second type, for men whose urine leaks through the skin of the testicles, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tenesmus
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tenesmus is an excess of flesh on the natural part, so unsightly; and some women have it as large as a hand, and that is the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You should remove the excess tenesmus with your hand or with forceps, and cut it gently; and do not go too deep, lest blood flow, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed; and there is another flesh that grows at the mouth of the anus, and fills, and perhaps breaks open, and is similar to a boil, and therefore the ancients called it "boil disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	You should cut it, as we have said of the tenesmus, and treat it until it is healed.
de erratique	of erratics
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic is it when the female's nature is not pierced, or the opening is small; and is natural from birth, or accidental from illness that has come; or is it from added flesh, or a thin or thick membrane, and is formed deep in the anus, or in the sides, or below, or wherever; and it prevents conception, childbirth, and perhaps the ability to have children; and the knowledge of this is through the examination of the vulva.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the numbness is close at hand, seek it with your fingers or a tool.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it's from a thin membrane, and it's close to the two lips, hurry and do this: place your two index fingers together, and have the woman on her back, legs spread apart; then gently spread the two lips, until the thin membrane is rounded, and the numbness is opened; then take wool, and soak it in oil, and place it on the area, and have the woman lie on her back each day so that it cannot heal.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the membrane is hard and thick, you must cut it with a scalpel, similar to a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the numbness is from newly formed flesh, lift it with forceps and cut it; and have blood-stopping medicines, such as dragon's blood, frankincense, mixed with a lot of egg; then apply a wide lead strip, so that the wound cannot heal; and thus it will be for a long time, and apply a dry linen bandage; then treat with other remedies until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when newly formed flesh comes to the sore, it must be cut in this manner, unless it is an entrenched abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an entrenched abscess that is in the sore, one should not touch with fire.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins from which blood flows habitually, and when hemorrhoids are old, they become painful; and we have already discussed their types, and their signs, and I will now describe those that receive cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and pain, when they are deep within the sore and are not apparent to the touch, should not be treated with a knife.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the opening of the sore, which can be felt, are those that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore, you should put the woman in a cold room, then grasp the painful area with pincers, and cut it at its roots, then apply powders of blood-stopping medicines, such as oak-gall, dragon's blood, and frankincense, and similar things; then put her feet against a wall for an hour, then place her in cold water; and if a discharge of blood comes, make her sit in a decoction of sumac, pomegranate bark, gallnuts, and similar things, and then take barley flour, mix it with honey and vinegar, and make a plaster for her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, apply leeches to the back and breasts without causing injury; then take wool, soak it in plantain juice or elderberry juice with old wine, and apply it to the affected area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess subsides, treat the area with ointment until it is healed; and the one called "albathir" is red and resembles a hard boil, so it should be cut as I described for the painful area; and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses of the marris
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscess arise in the marris, such as ulcers and stony abscesses and herpes and scabies and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other illnesses that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	Therefore, it is necessary for me to describe in this treatise the hot abscess that occurs in the marris, which is not one of the abscesses that collect pus; and if you wish to know the procedure for treatment, observe if the abscess is sharp at the beginning of its appearance, and full of heat and fever, and if it turns red so you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not rush to pierce it, but let it mature until the pain subsides; and then make the sick person sit on a seat, and have two small seats where he can lean, and rest on his back and bring his feet to the sides of his leg; and let his thighs be spread, and place his arms under his knees, and bind them well with a good bandage; then support him on his right side, and administer the instrument with which one opens the mouth of the marris, from which the following form comes; and it is necessary, when you want to administer this instrument, that you first insert the rod to know the depth of the marris, so that what enters the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and that it does not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the marris with cloths, so that the instrument does not harm him; and it is necessary that he place the cone of the instrument on top, and that he hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens, and it is opened by hand gently, it must be cut at the top, with the pointed blade; and when the pus is emptied, it is necessary that you place moist tents in rose oil, or in dry green oil, in the wound; and place the tent deep in the wound, at the bottom of the marris, and place clean wool soaked in water or cooked mallows on top of the marris and on the incision; then treat it after two days of the appropriate ointment, until it is healed; and sometimes the marris and the wound are cleaned with an enema of water and honey, and then water or cooked roots of lilies and long aristolochia; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is rejoined in the marris, you must avoid iron cauterization, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is necessary first for the midwife to know the nature of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman pressing down and wanting to smell the air: then the child hastens to come out; then know that this childbirth is according to nature, and the child comes out under its head, and the afterbirth with it; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press her belly, so that the child comes out quickly; because when it descends on its head, the afterbirth comes out with it, and the womb is cleared of its superfluities by good cleansing; and what comes out differently does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it sometimes comes out on its feet, and the body or head, or hands, come out, or it comes out on its belly, or side, and is perhaps turned on its neck, and by other bad figures; therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and clever in these things, and to avoid mistakes and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should help it.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out on its head through natural delivery, and the woman is giving birth with difficulty, and her strength is weak, have her sit on a chair, or the women hold her; and apply oil or fenugreek, cooked, to her nature, and then the midwife places between her fingers the small spatula whose form is this:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and cut the afterbirth, and cut it with her fingernail until the moisture that is inside comes out; and grasp the woman's belly so that the child descends, and if it does not descend, it is necessary to enema the woman with fenugreek decoction with sesame oil; then make her drink and sneeze with a concoction, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: the child will now come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands come out, it is necessary that you gently bring them back little by little; and if they cannot go in, place the woman on a stool, and raise her feet up; then lower the stool to the ground, and hold the woman so she does not fall during the lowering; and if the hands cannot go in and the child dies, cut the hands with the knife that is mentioned above, and remove the child, and bring them back as well.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the child's exit on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes out on its feet, it must be pushed upwards; and then turn it little by little, until it is straight; then take one of the feet and extend it little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	When it jumps up to the thighs, instruct her to grasp it, and make her sneeze with the concoction; if it jumps out, God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not come out as we have said, turn it little by little until it is in accordance with the natural form.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is easily done.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come out as we have said, take a mixture of aloe, and oil of sesame, and melted gum, and grind all in a mortar; and apply this ointment to the woman's body, and have her sit in lukewarm water up to below the ribs; and when she is softened from below, make her a compress of myrrh and place it below, and leave it an hour; then have her sit on a seat, then make her sneeze and hold her mouth and nose, and gently press her stomach, for the child will now jump out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the delivery of the child on her knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, the attendant should place their hands gently; then be supported on her neck, with her feet hanging down, and lying on a bed; and gently bend her hands, then take her hands on her stomach, and remove the cushions underneath, until she is positioned downwards; and if the child does not jump out, take her feet and move them forcefully, then move her stomach upwards, then put your hands in; and pull the child out little by little; and instruct the woman to press as much as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the delivery of the child who comes from the wide, one hand hanging down
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	One must devise a way to bring the hand back in; if it cannot be brought back, have the woman stand up and walk; if she cannot walk, have her lie down on a bed, and straighten her legs forcefully; then administer the ointment I have described; and if she does not give birth, have her sit on a seat, then try to bring the hand back; and deliver the child according to the natural form, and make her sneeze, and instruct her to press as much as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the delivery of the child on its mother's neck, with its hands spread out, and its face turned toward its mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	The attendant should hold its hand, then turn it gently, and pull it out gently; and when it is even, place the appropriate ointment and oil on the natural place, as we have said, then instruct her to move gently; and when you have done this, have her sit on a seat and tell her to press; and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same manner for the entire afterbirth
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes out in this manner for the entire afterbirth, cut the afterbirth with your fingernail until the moisture is emptied; and if the child hangs by its face and neck, cut it from the vagina, so it is not retained, and the child dies; then place the child inside, until you have positioned it correctly, and instruct the woman to press several times; then it will come out easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	Of the delivery of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens frequently.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are a strange thing, and do not live, except a little while; I know this, that they are multiplied, and are separated by the membrane that divides them, which is attached to the vagina; and sometimes they emerge just as naturally as a single child, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they emerge with difficulty, treat them as we have said, and let the midwife be skillful, and quickly and easily do what she must; and do this as if it were a matter of life or death.
de plusors enfans	Of several children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the womb one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, or more, up to fifteen, and are completely formed as children by the measurement of the wise and glorious, and it is necessary for the midwife to know all this, for perhaps similar things happen to her; so let her do what is appropriate.
de l’enfant mort	Of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat a woman with a dead child in her womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to manual work; then you must know if the woman is of sound virtue, and has no accident or fear of death; then it is necessary that the woman be laid on her back, and her head tilted down, and her legs raised; and the minister should hold her from two sides, or she should be tied to the bed so that she is not pulled down during the child's descent; then rub the mouth of the womb with moist oils with the mucilage of althea and fenugreek and flaxseed, then let the midwife anoint her hands with these oils and mucilages; then gently insert them into the womb, then find a place where she inserts the hooks that are suitable for this, and watch if the child is ready to descend from its head; then insert the hooks into its eyes or its neck or its mouth or its palate or under its chin or into the throat or near the sides, and if the descent is on the feet, insert it into the heels or the middle ribs; and it is necessary that he hold the hook in his right hand, and place the curve between the fingers of his left hand, and gently insert the whole hand, and insert the hook into any of these places that we have mentioned, until it reaches the empty space; and this is the form of the hook:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then insert another hook, or a third if you need it, so that the extraction is equal; and then extend it equally by moving from one side to the other, to cause it to come out, and let the hooks be toothed to hold it, as is the shape here:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains, then anoint some of the midwife's fingers with oil, and insert them into that part, and pull the other part; and if any remains, then place this hook in a higher place, and do this until it all comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes in front of the other, and it cannot be brought back because of the constriction, it is necessary that you wrap it in a cloth until it comes out completely; then cut it at the joint of the sole or with a knife, and thus you must do with the other hand, and with the two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's head is large and the passage is narrow, or if it has a sharp point, it is necessary that you place the spiny spatula between your fingers, and open the point and remove the sharp part; or you can round it with the instrument called "almidach", whose shape comes with the instruments in the chapter after this one; and do the same if the child has a large head naturally; and then pull out the bones with pliers, and if the head pops out and it is pinched in the throat, it should be cut open until the moisture that is in the body comes out; and if it cannot come out, cut it into pieces in the ways you can; and if it is swollen in the abdomen or under the ribs, it is necessary that you pierce it so that the moisture flows out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, the extraction is easy, and the alignment to the mouth of the uterus is easy.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is narrow in the belly or in the breast, you should extract it with a cloth wrapped around the hand; and cut the belly or the breast until the moisture that is there flows out; and if the other limbs are removed, and the head remains, then the midwife places her hand deep in the uterus, and pulls it towards the mouth of the uterus; then inserts a hook or two, and pulls it out; and if the mouth of the uterus is narrowed due to a hot abscess that has formed there, do not work on it, but apply moist and greasy things; and apply poultices, and soak in soft and moist water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on its side, and you can put it straight, apply what we have said about a living child; and if one has no strength, pull it out piece by piece, and leave nothing of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, apply what we have said about hot abscesses that come in the uterus; and if a discharge of blood comes, put it in constricting water, and administer other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly a child had been stillborn, then another one above that one, and the other one also died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess appeared in the buttock, and swelled until it opened, and began to discharge profusely.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the treatment, and pondered long, and could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong-pulling plaster, and one bone came out, and after a few days another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly surprised, because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I searched the wound, and pulled out many bones, until the woman was in better condition; and the woman lived a long time like this, and a little pus would come out from the spot; and I have recorded this chapter only because, when the master encounters a strange thing, he should know how to provide assistance.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the swelling back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Here after comes the form of the press, with which one reads the books; and it has two turns at two heads of two liins.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the horns should be finer than the restrictor, and be made of ebony or boxwood; and the opening of the shaft should be one finger wide, and the margin of the trees one finger, and a palm and a half long; and between the two liins there should be two joints of this same wood, which should be fastened to each other, half a palm long or a little more; and these two joints are placed in the mouth of the swelling to open when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, similar but finer and lighter, should be made of ebony or boxwood, resembling pliers; and have two joints at the two ends, as you see, one palm long, and two fingers wide; and when you wish to open the swelling with the entire instrument, make the woman sit on a bed, feet hanging and legs open, then put the two joined joints into the swelling, and hold the head of the instrument underneath between her thighs; then work your hand with the entire instrument, as you did with the pliers, accordingly to the amount you wish to open the mouth of the swelling, until the swelling does what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all surmounted, and their designs are multiplied; and when the master has prepared them, the work is hastened, and the price increases for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not neglect the instrument until you have prepared it, for their necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, you should instruct the woman to hold her breath, and then make her sneeze with a concoction, and grasp her mouth and nose with your hands; and if she throws it up with that, so much the better.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take a pot and make a hole in the lid, and put herbs in it that can open the swelling, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked in water over the fire; then put one end of a tube into the hole of the pot, and the other end into the mouth of the swelling, and let it steam until the vapors go into the swelling; then make her sneeze, as we said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	The afterbirth will come out quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment, and does not come out easily, instruct the woman to moisten her left hand in oil of sesame or in a poultice of marsh-mallow, and then place it in the area, and search for the afterbirth; and when she has found it, let her gently and steadily pull it out, so that the swelling does not collapse in the extraction; but it should be moved slightly to the right and to the left, and then pulled; it will come out and detach itself.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the swelling's opening is tightly closed, we have described the treatment of sneezing and herbal fumigation; and if it does not come out with all of that we have said, then be careful not to force it out; but it is necessary to tie the part of the swelling that is on the surface of the body to the woman's thigh, and then administer a clyster of tetrapharmacon ointment; it will soften and release, and come out easily; however, if it does soften, a bad odour comes to the stomach and head, and harms the woman.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, suitable fumigations are needed for this: some of the ancients have tested fumigation with cress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman for the retention of the flowers and the afterbirth is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it resembles a chain, and one places the fine end in the area, and the wider ends over the fire; and let the fumigations be over the embers, and heat it until it is burned, and start another one.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have their foundation pierced, but have a thin plug: therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to pierce that plug with her finger, and not pierce it with a sharp instrument, and to be careful not to touch the binding; then place moistened wool in wine and oil, and then treat with ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you fear it might plug up again, place a lead chain in the hole and leave it for several days, and remove it when the child is able to go to the chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes these blockages come from the closing of a wound or abscess; so it is necessary to cut open that blockage; and then treat as we said for the lead chain.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from below the foundation are swellings, and those that come from beside the foundation, or in the space between the two parts, have one or more fistulas; and when that swelling is old, it opens and discharges white or thin pus, and sometimes these fistulas are discharging; and they are known because discharge or wind comes out when the patient is discharging, and perhaps a worm jumps out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And there are fistulas that pierce through to the bladder, and to the middle of the penis; and they reach to the hip joint, and to the inside of the thigh.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one recognizes a fistula that penetrates to the foundation, and one that does not: and this is how you put your index finger to the foundation and put a fine needle of bronze or iron into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is twisting, then put a thin lead tent, or a horsehair, until you feel the tent or hair against your finger; and if you do not feel it, and there is no discharge, wind, or worm coming from the opening, as we have said, know that it does not penetrate; so hurry to treat it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula penetrates to the bladder or to the urinary tract, urine escapes, and cannot be closed by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it pierces to the hip joint, the tent goes to the spot; if there is no twisting and the pain is localized, it often bursts and no medicine or sealing by ointment helps; and in these penetrating fistulas there is no cure but labor and the vanity of foolish quacks who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one that is not penetrating and is not old, there is hope of health through iron, as I have proven, and this is how the patient lies on their back in your hands; and lift their legs up to their thighs, and have their thighs inclined towards their stomach; then put a bronze tent, or lead if there is twisting, until you know where the tent reaches.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the fundament, you should put your index finger there; if you then feel the tent has pierced it, and is uncovered where you feel the surface or flesh between your finger, then know that it is penetrating; then do not try because it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One says, however, that some can be healed, but this happens rarely; and the help one gives is that one heats the fine cautery according to the width of the fistula, as previously stated; and places it very hot in the fistula, until it comes next to the fundament; and do this two or three times, until you know that those damaged tissues are burned, which are similar to a bird's feather; and then treat it with softened tents in butter, until the tissue comes out, then treat it with an ointment that creates flesh and seals it.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If this is not otherwise healed; and if the tent goes in, but does not pierce to the finger that is at the fundament, and there is a thick covering of tissue or surface between your finger and the tent, and you see the fistula at the beginning of the covering of the core; then cut from the beginning of the fistula, and push the tent further in, and then put the cautery afterward, until it comes to the head of the tent; and the tent will be delivered and fall; then clear those damaged tissues that look like a bird's feather, and nothing will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if blood flows between you and the work, cauterize it with fire or sharp medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the cautery of fire brings together two good things: that is to say, the burning of these added tissues, and the stopping of blood and the drying of moisture; then treat it with softened tents in butter or crushed herbs, until the place expels pus, and the burned tissues come out in the pus; then treat the wound with ointments that seal and create hard flesh, and the medicines are dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula goes down to the bottom of the fundament, and is distant from the body, put your finger at the fundament, and examine that.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and between the two is the cloth or the surface or the flesh, or it is close to piercing, then there is no other way than by hope and faith, by administering one of these three ways: either you cauterize it as we said, or you cut it to the bottom, or if you can, put tents in it and treat it as before; and do not go too deep, lest you cut the tissue that holds the fundament, and the expulsion of the matter comes from the will; then treat it as we said; perhaps it will be cured, or you separate that covering and clean it after it is cut from the fundament, either with a tent or another suitable instrument; then cleanse the corrupted flesh that is in the wound as much as you can; then try to restore the wound and to keep the fistula outside the fundament: that will be an easier thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are like this: and it is when you put the tent in the fistula, and it is on the side of the fundament next to the skin above, take a tent pierced at the head according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And put one twisted thread into two, and put the tent with all the thread into the fistula until it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is piercing into the edge of the fundament inside, then pull the thread out of the hole, as if you were putting your finger into the fundament; and pull the head of the thread, and gather the two ends together, and hold one to the other, and leave it for one or two days; and sometimes restrain it, until the thread cuts the flesh that is between them, and falls out; then treat the wound until it is healed and closed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, then make it pierce in all the ways you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not necessary to make it so deep with the lacing, and then cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spatumile spine, from which one makes the fistula, is very sharp on one side and sharp; and on the other side not, so that one does not cut what one should not cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are according to two types: either they are within the fundament, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and often blood flows from them, and there are one or more, and are outside the fundament and at the top of the fundament; but those that are outside have little moisture, and often a little yellow water or a little blood, and have the color of the body; and the cure for those that have them within the fundament is that you order the patient to strain himself to go to the chamber, until the fundament issues forth, and the filaments appear; hurry, and pinch them with pliers, or hold them with your nail, then cut them at their roots; and if the tweezers cannot hold them because of their moisture, then take them with a cloth, or cotton, or a piece of chamelot; and pull them out with your fingers, then cut them, and powder them with some warm powders that are in the place of cautery; or if you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter on cautery, then cure them with other cures until they are healed; and if the fundament cannot come out, then irrigate the patient with a corrosive and harsh enema to wash what is in the fundament, so that it can come out openly; when the patient strains, and the filaments are outside the fundament, the cure is easy; and it is that you take them with your fingernail or pliers, and cut them, then cure them as we have said until they are healed, and that they fear the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	You must administer the suture in this manner: take a twisted thread, and put it in a needle, and then pull the thread above and pierce the needle on the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread under the needle, and let it be wide; and tighten the thread tightly, then tie the thread, and remove the needle, and do the same for all the others, and leave one to run the excess blood; then put a damp cloth soaked in rose oil or in cerote on the fundament, and put it on the fundament, and order the patient to rest; and then let it be until they fall, and when they fall, cure them with ointment and other cures, until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the drying of the fundament's inflammation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times inflammation occurs in the intestine, and due to the constriction of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine is of no use.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	You must scrape the scab off with the point of a spatula or your fingernail, which prevents it from getting moist; then treat it until it is healed as is appropriate; and if it cannot heal, then scrape it more strongly than before, until it is very inflamed and scabbed over; then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	of the trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formice is a small, deceptive appearance under the skin, and goes very deep; and sometimes it finds the cold, and it is sensed just like trembling death, and it comes over the entire body, and more in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the treatment is that you take a stick from a goose feather, or a strong vulture feather, and place that stick over the trembling, so that the circle encompasses the trembling entirely; then turn your hand over the entire stick until you cut around the trembling, and insert it deep, and root out the trembling.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, make a tool from a copper or iron rod, following this shape, and let it be thin underneath and pointed above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	not pierced, to hold and press the spot. And if you wish, cauterize the trembling, as it is described in the chapter on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the clyster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes a clyster is made of silver or gold, or of melted or hammered copper; and sometimes these instruments are made small or large, according to those to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those, then, which are administered to the care of children and those who are weak and sorrowful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and large clyster is thus: wide at the top, where the belly is bound in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there be a separation or the belly be bound, as you see, and the bottom be pierced; and have at one side two holes, and at the other one; and let the belly, where one puts the medicines, be of a beast's bladder or parchment, and let it be pierced all around with small holes, and let there be between each hole one inch of space, then put in these holes a strong thread of strong thread twisted in an X or looped around, and assemble the belly as if it were a purse; and when the medicine is inside, bind it to the instrument beforehand with a strong thread, then clysterize; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clyster with oil or egg white, or something similar, then insert it gently; then the minister squeezes it with both hands together, until it is completely empty, then remove the clyster, and let the patient raise his legs against the wall, and if the medicine wants to come out, let him hold it as long as he can; and if he sleeps a whole night, it is more helpful.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you clysterize him for a disease of belly discharge, and the medicine is in a hurry to come out, then repeat it until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are in the fundament, or an abscess, let the clyster be as small as for a child; and this is the form of the small clyster, where the skin is tightened:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you the treatments of hands and medicine, according to the completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by the throwing of stones, and cuts from swords and knives, or lances or wood or arrows, or similar things; or that are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the face, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and will begin with the simple wounds of the head, for the remembrance will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound occurs on the head, and the bone is not broken, if it is from the throwing of a stone or similar things, and the skin is nonetheless broken and the wound is large, and you suspect the rise of a hot abscess: then immediately make it bleed, using the cephalic vein, especially if little blood comes from the wound, and let the bleeding be on the opposite side of the injured part; and avoid the patient's overindulgence in wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not wish to bleed, then reduce its food, and let it drink no wine, nor eat any meat; and put upon the wound, if a hot abscess comes, cotton moistened in rose oil only, or in astringent wine; and if there is no hot abscess, then put upon the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not dried out by the air, powder, which I will say a little later; and if the wound has been dried out, then put upon it some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like a cut from a sword or similar, and the edges cannot be brought together with bandages, then bring them together by stitching, as I will say about wounds of the belly, of the abdomen.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is open to the bone, and hangs, and holds only by a little, then cut it away; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and command the sick person to eat rich foods, such as breads and cooked grains, as well as pulses, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find rot in the skin, and it does not reach the bone, cut away all the rot, and burn it, then treat it; and if there is an artery or vein in the wound, from which blood flows, and it cannot be stopped by medicines, then search for the artery, and if you find it dislocated, then tie it with a thread; and if that does not help at all, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is easy: and that you put on this powder which quickly heals before the wound has dried out.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the method of the powder is this: take frankincense one part; dragon's blood two parts; live coals three parts, and pulverize it finely, and fill the wound, and bind it firmly, until it dries well and joins with all its blood; and then bind it well, and leave it without loosening, if it does not swell; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes this is done with coals alone, when one does not have frankincense or dragon's blood, but that the heat has not dried out the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the heat has dried the wound, especially in summer, one does not put this powder on it; but puts on some prepared ointments, or barley flour poultices made with water and honey, until it forms a poultice; then treats it with other cures until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if a bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, then you should hold it with delicate pincers; and I will tell you about the fractures of the head later.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound occurs in the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and one in the head, but if the nerve or artery in the neck is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is a nerve, there is no other remedy than to let it heal, and not put anything constricting on it, for it harms the nerves and causes them to recede; and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is also with the brain, which is the highest part; but let the medicine be warm, like warm water washed with sweet water and mixed with rose oil, and washed cupping also in sweet water, and other mineral stones according to this manner, and moist ointments.
