Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, stitch it and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and it is swollen and full of pus, pierce it in a lower place; and if the artery is cut, and bleeding occurs, cauterize it, and bandage it, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the heart, and the passage is protected, through which the food passes, stitch the heart to the throat’s cartilage, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural form; and then restrain the swelling, and leave it for some days, then treat it with drying ointments until it is healed; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, probe it; and if there are pieces of bone, remove all of them that you can, and those you cannot remove, let it be until the wound suppurates, and the outlet is freed and cleared; and if the wound is fresh, apply the powder I mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a lance or knife wound, and the wound is deep, check if gas escapes from the wound when the patient exhales: know then that the wound is fatal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put the powder on it at first, nor bandage it because the blood may not drain deeply, and return to the heart, and kill the patient; but put an attractive ointment, and bandage it twice a day; and if you do not have ointment, put old cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three, four, or more days; so no spasm, nor tremor of the heart, nor tightening of the breath will come; and when you see good signs, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Then treat it with poultices and other remedies until it is healed; and if it cannot heal, and it opens again, know that there is a fistula; treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, on the chest or back, treat it as described above; if it is large, with stitches; and if it is small, with powder, and if it has pierced the bone and broken pieces off, clean the wound, and remove them if they are detached; and if they are not detached, let the wound fester, so the removal will be easier; and for other wounds on other limbs, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the belly is large, medium, and small; from the large wound sometimes the intestines, or the nerves of the intestines, jump out, which causes their intrusion; and the suturing is more difficult, and sometimes the small wound is worse than the large one, because more effort is required to put the intestines back in if they are not put back in quickly; because the intestines swell as soon as they feel the cold, so they are more difficult to put back, and thus the medium wound is more difficult to treat because one has to put the intestines back in place than with the other two. And know that the rupture of the belly is according to four types: the two common sutures occur in the suture of the belly, and the suture of other wounds of the body and two other proper sutures are common to other wounds; and nevertheless, they are more proper with the suture of the belly, and I will explain each one and declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and some of the intestines come out, and it is difficult to put them back, this is due to one of these two reasons: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines have swollen due to the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this way: moisten a sponge or a linen cloth in lukewarm water, or boil it in water with squinant, and cypress and spikes, and stir the intestines until the swelling is removed; and sometimes wine astringents are used, and it is gentler than water alone for deflating.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestines with water or cooked mallow and aloes, because this facilitates easy entry with little difficulty; and if it cannot enter, then slightly widen the wound with the instrument with which hemorrhoids are cut; and the first treatment is gentler than cutting, and no one should cut unless great necessity exists; and this is the instrument for slitting: cut inside the curve and not outside, and see here the form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines jump out, put them back in their natural place according to their proper form, if you have the power to do so, for this is better.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the abdomen, you must make the patient lie on their back, and raise their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the lower part of the abdomen, place the head and chest higher than the lower parts, and likewise if the rupture of the abdomen is in one of the two parts, pay attention that the wounded part is higher than the other; and thus it is necessary to administer what I say in large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, do what your equipment allows, then take a gentle instrument that holds the entire rupture in its hand and brings the edges together; and this is the common method of stitching, and that you should take a needle, or several, according to the size of the wound, then leave an inch of space from the beginning of the wound, and insert a needle where there is a strong thread; and pierce the two edges of the skin with the two edges of the subcutaneous layer, which is beneath the skin, until you have pierced it on that side, and bring the two edges of the subcutaneous layer together; then tie a double thread around the needle from both sides, then bring the two edges of the wound together, then leave an inch of space, and insert another needle; then tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and do not stop doing this according to your need for needles until the entire wound is tightened; and the needles should be medium, between fine and thick, for fine needles cut all the flesh, and too thick ones cannot enter well; therefore, they must be medium; and do not stick the needles too far out from the flesh and skin, so they do not cut and open the wound before it is closed; and then cut the ends of the needles so they do not injure the patient when sleeping, and put bandages or cloths over the ends of the needles to hold them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed; and this method of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, for one or two needles suffice.  The second method of stitching is common, and is that you bring together the two edges of the skin and the two edges of the subcutaneous layer together with a needle with a strong medium thread; and when you have pierced all four edges together, bring the needle back to the place where you began, in the manner of sewing cloth; and put a space of the size of a little finger between each stitch; this stitch is known to men, and I sewed a wound a man had in his belly, which was wounded by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm in size, and intestines came out more than two palms in size, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestines after they had been out for twenty-four hours, and the wound was healed until fifteen days later, and I treated him, and he was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the doctors had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointments, because I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine; and I put old cotton over the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper methods of stitching: take the needle, and push it from the outside to the inside; when it has pierced the skin straight through, bring the edge of the subcutaneous layer, or where you put the needle, and pierce it on the other side, from the inside to the outside; and the understanding of this stitch is that you sew as the leatherworkers do with hides, and that you leave the subcutaneous layer on one side, and bring it back to the other side, until the stitch is entirely completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of stitching, which Galen properly describes, is as some do, who bring the two parts together naturally, and apply one edge of the subcutaneous layer to the other edge, in this manner: insert a needle into the edge of the wound close by, and pierce only that spot, and leave the two edges of the subcutaneous layer; then turn the needle, and pierce it from the outside to the inside, to the two edges of the subcutaneous layer; then pierce one and the other from the outside to the inside, to two other edges of the wound that are on the other side; and this is the finer and most common method of stitching.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen said this, and some testify, that one should sew the belly with two needles, with thread on each; and one should insert one needle on one side, and the other on the other, in the manner of those who sew straps; and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the stitching is more difficult than in other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The treatment of the wound is like the treatment of other wounds:  when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, before the flesh has changed, put the intestines back in place and stitch it; then put powdered healing earth on it, and if the flesh has changed, put on any available ointment until the wound begins to discharge; and remove the threads, and ensure the skin and the wound are closed; then treat the wound like any other, until it is healed; and if you lack medicine, as soon as it begins to discharge, apply old cotton and change it twice a day until healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you need no other medicine in many cases when the wounds are simple; and if you fear the wound might spread to the main limbs, you should soak light wool in oil of moderate heat, or rose oil, and put it around the joints and under the armpits; and if it feels pain or rotting in the boils, which often happens, irrigate with warm dark wine, especially if the rot reaches the intestines; and pierce it from inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine called "jejunum" cannot heal when wounded, and this is due to the network of veins within it, and due to the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the sinew has come loose from the wound, put it back in place just like the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and turned dark or black, you must tie the dark area, to prevent further blood flow, for there are veins and arteries there; then cut what is between the tie, and hang the two ends down from below the wound, to lessen the extraction when the sinew comes out, and the wound discharges.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the bowel
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is torn, and the wound is small, it can be restored in some men, for I saw a man wounded in the belly by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and became an ulcer, and the discharge and gas came out; I applied treatment as best I could, and did not cease to work on it until it was healed, and the area was closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it close, I feared the patient might have pain in his belly; and he had no pain, but remained in better condition, eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be bound in this way: take a leech with large heads, then bring together the edges of the wound, and when the leech has opened its mouth, place it over the two edges so that it closes its mouth over; then cut its head off, and it holds so that it cannot come loose, then put another leech in the same way as before, until the wound is completely closed; and stitch up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	These leeches cling to the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient, and the intestine can be tied with a thin thread cut from the intestine of an animal, in this way: take the end of this intestinal thread that is very thin, and then tie to the end of this thread a thin linen thread, then put the thread in the needle, and stitch the intestine, and bring it back together in the rupture; and this way of stitching with leeches is no more than according to the path of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially if it is in one of the large intestines, there is no device or cure, other than subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or where it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it becomes chronic, is universally called a "fistula", especially when it is festering and discharging pus.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula, according to truth, is a hard, white, and painful swelling, where no pain is felt, and is as festering as a bird's feather; and sometimes clear pus comes out, and sometimes thick; sometimes little, and sometimes quite a lot; and I have already spoken of this in the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, is no more than due to one of the eight causes: that is to say, by the smallness of the blood or body; or by its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside, and on the edges, that does not allow flesh to grow; or there is too much pus; or the place is rotten, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good for the treatment; or because the corruption is a kind of pestilence; or because the digestion and healing are slow in the region, and it swells naturally; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures with medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now it is necessary for me to tell you the treatment of a fistula that is done by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or the surface, or the intestines, or the bladder, or some of the ribs, or the spine of the back, or some joint of the hands or feet; and there are some that come to the property of the principal member, and to similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all fistulas of this kind are difficult to cure, and there is only labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not reach the place I have mentioned, and you have confidence in the treatment, and you want to know it, take a tin or iron probe, if the fistula is straight, probe it; and if the fistula is crooked, search it with a thin lead probe, for lead bends easily around the curve; and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot properly probe it with probes, then flush it through one of the openings, for the moisture flows from one opening to another, and cleans it; then carefully probe as best you can, to see if there are bones or nerves, and if it is deep, and ask the patient about the pain he feels when you press on it with your hand, and the place where he feels it; and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from joints, or nerves, or arteries, or veins, or in any of the places I told you, cut it according to what I have told you, and remove the swelling and the corrupted flesh that is inside; and then treat it until it is healed, and if the fistula is deep and straight, you must cut deep, as much as you can, then put moistened probes in sharp medicine, and put them to the top of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom; and then apply ointments to regenerate healthy flesh, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not bother the main limb, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, remove it until all corruption is removed, then treat it with things that regenerate flesh until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and pus returns as before, know that you have not reached the bottom: uncover and search until you are at the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach; there is no other remedy than to leave it to nature; and if there is a small piece of corrupted bone, and you can remove it with pliers, remove it with a suitable instrument for this, and if there are many bones, remove them all, leaving not one; and if the moisture makes it difficult, and there is no mistake or fear, cut the moisture and flesh, and expose the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them at once, apply something that causes decay to the wound, and leave it until the place around the bones decays, and then the bones will be easier to remove; and if it is a large bone, such as of a leg or thigh, remove only the corruption until the blackness is entirely gone, then restore the wound; and if there is a large part of the corrupted bone, and it reaches the marrow of the bone, it must be cleaned and cut all the way to the corruption, and then treated until it is healed; and I will tell you about a fistula that occurred to a man in his leg, so that you can take an example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man around 30 years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that originated within the body, until the matter reached the leg, and it swelled with a large abscess, and there was no reason to avoid opening it; but the doctors in their foolishness worked so much on it that the abscess opened, and much matter flowed out, and it became a fistula, and many openings appeared that all expelled pus and moisture from the body; and many doctors applied treatment for two years, and there was no wise man in the art of medicine until I was called, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which they treated him, and what flowed through the openings in large quantities; and the young man's body turned red, and his complexion was yellowish.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I placed a tent in one of these openings, and then searched all the openings, and found that one connected to another throughout all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then hurried and cut into one of the openings until I uncovered a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption reached the bone within; I cleaned what appeared of the corrupted bone, and thought there was no other corruption, except for what I removed; and I began to restore the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, but it would not heal; and then I started again, and uncovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing into the bone, and I cleaned it, and then removed it, and I tried to heal the place; but I could not until I cut around a palm's width of the bone, and extracted it down to its entire marrow, then I restored it with medicines; and he was healed and healed quickly, and it was not necessary to recommence the work except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure, and because of the fear of death I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For due to the evacuation he often bled, but he was completely healed, and hard tissue grew in place of the bone, and it was of good disposition, and had no harm or opposition at all, neither in appearance nor in action.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if a bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated in this manner: take a bandage, and tie it to the end of the exposed bone, and instruct someone to extend it upward; and place another thicker woolen bandage over the flesh covering the bone, and extend the end so you pull the corrupted flesh beneath, and expose the skin over the place where you wish to treat, so the treatment does not harm the skin; and put charcoal or a board under the bone to help cut away the corrupted flesh; and continue cleaning as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and clean it again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted, but not exposed, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, then expose all the skin; then place charcoal underneath, and then clean the corruption from one part to the other, and let the cleaning tool follow the length of the corruption a little, as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut the corrupted joint, and clean the bone on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, there is no other way than cutting; and if the corruption is in the finger of the hand, or the finger of the foot, then that is a very difficult thing, but still you must investigate that corrosion, how it appears; and clean it in every way you can, but that the veins or nerves do not oppose you; and know that the instruments and the methods for cutting these bones are many, according to the arrangement of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and thinness, and their size and smallness, and their hardness; and for this, it is necessary to prepare a tool for each type of work; and know that the work will show you the tool you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of illnesses; so consider the tool you need according to what is appropriate.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The shoulder might rot either due to internal or external causes; and once you have treated the corrosion with medicines, and they do not work, you must cut the limb down to the place where the corrosion is, so that the patient escapes death, or the worse, the limb's loss; and the sign is that the limb turns black, as if burned by fire, and will rot after the blackness, then the limb corruption spreads to other limbs, and affects the whole body; so hurry to cut it off, and if it is due to the sting of venomous creatures, such as sea scorpions and vipers and the like, if the corrosion is at the tip of the finger, cut it off and do not give it space to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it reaches the hand, cut it at the joint so the corruption does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, cut it at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, that is death, and no strong treatments are worth the quantity of its virtue; and do the same when the corruption reaches the foot: if it reaches the first joint, cut after the other joint; and if it reaches the foot, cut off the whole foot; and if it goes up the leg, cut at the knee joint; and if it goes above the knee, there is no other remedy than to leave the patient to die; and the way to cut or treat the limb is that you tie it above and below, and have some assistants pull one bandage down, and others pull the other bandage up, and you separate the flesh between the two bandages a wide space, so the bone is exposed; then cut or clean it, and put a linen cloth on each side, so the treatment does not touch the healthy part, and cause the patient more injury and festering.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs while working, cauterize the area quickly, or apply some astringent powders; then return to your treatment until it is complete, then bandage the injured limb with a suitable bandage and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in his foot: he had a blackness that looked like a fire burn, and this corrosion first came to his toe, until it affected the entire foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he quickly had the foot cut off, and was healed; and a long time later, the corrosion returned to the finger of his hand, and he came to me, and I applied repelling things after cleaning the body, but the corrosion could not stop; and he wanted me to cut off his hand, but I refused, because I had hope of repelling the matter; and I was also afraid that if I cut off his hand, he might die, as the man's strength was weak; and he despaired completely, and returned to his land, and hurried to cut off his hand, and was healed; and I have only recounted this so that one does the same if one has need.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes, an abscess appears in fleshy tissue, and remains so long that it gathers a large amount of pus; and then it bursts and the pus escapes, leaving the area empty, like a vessel; and the skin above is as thin as a delicate cloth, and does not reach the bone, nor the nerve, and such an illness is called "sain," and not "fistula"; but if it extends so far that it reaches the bone deep down, it is called "fistula"; and the treatment is that you cut the skin all around, especially when it is thin, like a cloth; and it does not spread due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	If you suspect that the skin is inflamed, and the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, treat it with a clyster like this: observe if the swelling is large, and the pus that emerges has a foul odor, then clysterize it with Egyptian medicine made thus: take figs, oil, and litharge, equally, and put them in a vessel over the fire until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey; then take of this according to your need, and mix it with water and honey, and clysterize the swelling, and contract the opening; and leave the medicine in for two hours, then remove it by squeezing; do this repeatedly until the swelling is cleansed and the odor is removed; and sometimes it is clysterized with ash water, when this medicine is not available, and is done by taking vine wood ash, pouring water over it, then straining it, and clysterizing it, until you know that the swelling is well cleaned; and if the patient cannot tolerate the Egyptian medicine or ash water, then clysterize it with water and honey, or add a little crushed litharge; or use honey and diluted wine, as the honey has the property of cleaning and washing, and the wine causes the sore to heal; and when this has been done, and you believe the swelling is well cleansed, then clysterize it with something that promotes flesh growth, such as diafinit plaster, mixed with rose oil and wine; or you can clysterize it with other medicines and ointments, whose properties I have described in the treatment of ointments; and if the opening of the sore is small, and the clyster tube cannot enter, enlarge it slightly with an iron instrument, and insert a tent of Egyptian or basilicon ointment until it is enlarged; and if the wound is too large, then stitch it, leaving only an opening for the clyster to enter, and if the pus-releasing opening is on top, cut it or at a lower location.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the pus is deep, it does not allow flesh to grow; and if you cannot cut the swelling from below as you wish, prepare it in such a way that the pus drains to the lowest point, for when the pus is deep, it does not allow flesh to grow, and if you cannot cut the swelling from below as you wish, prepare it in such a way that the pus flows easily downwards and does not leave any pus; and take strengthening medicines to place on the sore, and place a linen cloth covering the entire sore; then cut the opening of the sore a little wider than before, then apply a soft ointment over another cloth, according to the size of the opening, and place it over the sore opening to relieve the pus, and do not remove the large cloth except once after many days; and the one over the sore opening, remove frequently to remove the pus, and observe if the draining pus is poisonous, little or much, digested or indigested; and be aware if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been applied in this way and you see the nature jumping over the sore opening, know that the sore is healing, and health is approaching; and then unbind it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you unbind the wound, change the cloth and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the sore discharges undigested pus after many days, know that the sore will not heal.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons flow after a long time, do not despair of health, for health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For some people's wounds are slow to grow flesh, and others are the opposite; and if undigested pus flows from the sore after many days, know that the sore will not heal; and if the sore is slow to heal and is prolonged, add drying medicines, moist in substance and dry in virtue, such as diafinit ointment, for it contains a large amount of vitriol, and it is the last medicine; take diafinit ointment, mix it with rose oil and dilute it with equal amounts of old wine; then apply it and use it; and the same is done with honey, if diafinit ointment is not available, or take myrrh, aloes, and frankincense, grind them, and powder them over honey when it is over the fire; and then glue a cloth to it and apply it to the sore; and sometimes an aristologist applies long roots of celestial lily, which is like flour from vervain and centaury; and use these simple or compounded remedies: grind them into powder and place it on the honey I mentioned, and use it; and if the treatment is prolonged and not cured by this method, then know that the corruption is deep and has affected the bone, or the hard parts, or the ligaments; then treat it with the fistula treatment, as we have stated before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	Of the abscess of the nail.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	A whitlow is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the finger or toe, or perhaps on other fingers; and when it is old and is not cared for, a painful abscess develops, and it flows and discharges pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and perhaps even destroys the entire nail; and the corruption reaches the bone, until there is foul pain and the finger is swollen, and the color is dark.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment is not effective, you must cut away all the excess nail with a hot iron, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cauterization is a great help if the bone and nail are healthy; and if the nail presses on the flesh, begins to prick it, and injures it, you must place a splint under the nail that is pricking the flesh, and lift it up, then carefully and gently cut away the flesh; and apply burning and corrosive medicines to the remaining flesh to remove everything; then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corruption is in the bone, cut it, and remove it completely, for as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal; and if you see that the finger is corrupting, cut it as described above, then treat it until it heals; and if it is bruised and swollen, and it causes great pain, you must first cleanse it; then cut the nail with a sharp spatula, cutting across the top, and be careful that the cut does not reach the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if it happens, apply something that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the fingertip.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The extra fingers that occasionally grow on some men's hands are sometimes entirely fleshy, and sometimes they have bones, and sometimes a nail. Some of them grow at the base of the joint, or their origin is in one of the finger's joints.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	The one that grows on any part of the finger does not move, and the one that grows at the finger joint, possibly does move. The one that is fleshy is easily cut this way: cut it at its base with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	The one that grows at the base of the joint is difficult to cure: avoid cutting it.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For the one that grows on the finger's furthest part, you should first cut the fleshy part cleanly down to the bone, then cut the bone with a suitable knife, and then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The joining together of fingers comes about by growth, or by the healing of a wound, or by burning from fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	You should cut the adhesion, so that the fingers return to their natural shapes; then place between them wet cloths or bandages soaked in rose oil, so that they do not join together; or you place between them thin pieces of lead until the area is joined, as is appropriate.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If an adhesion occurs between any of the fingers and the palm, cut the adhesion as necessary.
des vils	(of) the wicked
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	The veins are large, swollen, full of melancholic superfluities, that appear in various parts of the body; and they are more frequent in the legs of those who walk and work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer a purge of the bowels, and then apply a treatment of basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment with iron is according to two methods: one is that they are cut and black blood is drawn out; and the other method is that you tie off the vein and draw it entirely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The procedure is as follows: first, raise the leg in very hot water, until the thick blood is thinned, then bind the patient's leg from above the thigh down to the part below the knee; then cut the vein in one, two, or three places, with a wide cut, and raise and draw out the black blood into your hand, from one end to the other, as much as the patient's constitution can tolerate; and then bandage it, and instruct him to eat foods that induce black bile; and repeat the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, and it harms the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The raising of the blood is done this way: shave the patient's leg, if there is a lot of hair, then place it in a bath, and raise the leg in hot water until it turns red, and the veins swell; and if you do not have a bath, heat it over the fire, and then cut the vein lengthwise from the top of the knee, or in the part below the ankle; then open the skin with a scalpel, and scrape the vein from each side, until it appears when touched; and it is seen red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white string; then place the lancet underneath, until it is raised from the skin, and then hang it gently on the scalpel, then cut it in another place above three fingers; then scrape the skin over the vein until it appears, then lift it with the lancet, as you did, and hang it on another scalpel, as you did before; then cut another incision, or more if necessary, then lift it and cut it to the toe, then draw and lift it to the second incision; then extract it from incision to incision, until it is all drawn out, then cut it; and if you cannot pull and lift it, insert a needle with a strong double thread, bind it and pull it, and place a lancet underneath, and turn your hand back and forth until it comes out; and be careful not to cut it, because if it is cut, it cannot be pulled or lifted, and this causes harm to the patient; and when you have drawn it all out, put wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is constricted, twisted, and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must carefully split it, but do not cut it; and draw it out as we have previously stated.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron with which one cuts the vein is curved, and it does not cut straight, so as not to cut the vein; and it is of a large curve, because if it were thin, it would cut the vein, but be thick as we have said, and this is the shape:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in legs, in warm areas where no herbs or trees grow, and in land where there is no moisture; and perhaps it arises elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens from the corruption that comes from beneath the skin, as it comes inside the body of serpents and worms, embedded between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the sign of the beginning of this vein is that a very great inflammation comes to the leg, then the place changes, and the vein begins to protrude, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the head appears, you must wrap a piece of lead around it, from one and a half to two ounces, and bandage it, and leave the lead hanging on the leg, and every time some protrudes outside, wrap it around the lead and bandage it; and if it is too long, cut off a part and wrap the remainder, and do not cut it at its root until it is all out; for if you cut it, it returns into the flesh and causes abscess and corruption in the place, and a bad disease; because of which it is necessary to treat it little by little until the end, and nothing remains in the body; and sometimes this vein, when treated, is five palms long, or ten, and a man came to me once, from whom it emerged ten palms long, and when you cut it, it forms one ray or opening, and pierce it to the bottom, so that everything comes out; and the matter inside should be emptied, and apply remedies to the place to prevent corruption for some days, then treat it like any abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes this vein has many branches, especially when it appears in the joint of the foot or on the foot, and many openings come from it, and from which blood oozes out; treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that arise between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This illness is called "bull's disease" in our land, because it often occurs in oxen, and it is a small worm that arises between skin and flesh, and it goes throughout the body, ascending and descending, and one feels it well when it moves from limb to limb, until it pierces the skin where it goes and oozes out; and it is caused by the corruption of certain humors, as worms and snakes and earthworms and threadworms in the belly; and its malice is feared, for when it travels through the body and reaches the head and comes to the eye, it may enter and destroy the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you wish to treat and remove it, it cannot be extracted except when it is moving; therefore you must tie the area above and below with a strong bandage tightly, then cut above and pull it out; and if the worm is deep in the flesh, and you do not find it, cauterize it with fire above until it dies; and the greatest harm it does is that it reaches the eye, as we have said; and if you see it approaching the head near the eye, press the eyebrow firmly below it, then cut above and pull it out; and the patient must use bodily cleansings with dissolving medicines for the corrupt bad humors, and abstain from foods that cause corruption.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes upon some limbs, and it can move from limb to limb; and I saw this that I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of her arm; and a little after, I saw it climb like a worm up her shoulder, faster than anything, like quick silver when it moves from place to place; the pain departed from that spot, and settled in her shoulder, and then a little after ran through all her body until it reached the other arm; then she told me it would often circle around her body, as I had seen it do.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly how it moved thus from limb to limb, for I had never seen this illness in this way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had seen many where pain had moved from place to place, but I had never seen it like this in the woman; and I thought it was because the woman had a dry body, and exposed veins, and because of this the flatulence appeared constrained; and it does not appear in this manner to those who are fleshy, and who have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you wish to treat this illness, and the patient feels this pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then carefully bind above and below it, and then cut until this constrained flatulence in that spot is released; and cauterize the spot; and if you do not see it with your eyes, then treat it with things that expel flatulence, such as foul-smelling pills, and pills of serapin, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places of the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	Their diversity is such that there are those with large points, and small, and feathered, and barbed; and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those with pieces; and the one that strikes any limb strikes in two ways: either in a principal limb, such as brain, heart, liver, lungs, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar limbs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.
