When it strikes then in any of these limbs, and the signs of death, which I will tell you afterward, appear to you: then you must refrain from extracting this arrow, for death follows in many cases; and when these bad signs do not appear, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then extract it, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the signs of the brain when the arrow strikes it and pierces the bone, and the soft matter that is upon the brain bursts forth, are when there is blurring of sight, stupor, fainting, and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps there is a flow of blood from the nostrils or ears; and perhaps he loses his speech and voice; and white moisture like pus bursts from the wound, and also a burning of the flesh; and if these signs appear to you, then refrain from treatment, and extract the arrow if it is not embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of the arrow when it strikes the heart are that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were lodged in a hard thing, and not hollow; and perhaps the arrow moves like a pulse, and black blood flows out, and coldness and cold sweat, and fainting occur: know then without doubt that death is imminent.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the signs of the arrow that wounds the lung are that frothy blood flows from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's complexion changes, and he gasps loudly and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow strikes the covering of the breast, it is beside the small ribs; and it throws out much pus and causes great pain and gasping; and all the members of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow strikes the stomach, perhaps something of indigested food comes forth from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow strikes the belly, and bits of straw burst forth from the bowels, there is no hope for healing, nor for the removal of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow strikes the bladder, and urine bursts forth and comes out, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the face and neck and throat and shoulder and shoulder joint and spine of the back and thighs and legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to many dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow struck his tear duct at the root of his nose: I tried it, and pulled it out the other side under the fat of the ear, and he was healed without harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I pulled out an arrow that struck the fat of the eye below the eyelid, and the arrow was lodged, and I could only reach the tip towards the shaft.  The arrow was large, from a Turkish bow, and very light without fletching; the man was healed, and no bad accident befell him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I pulled an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arab with fletching. I cleaned the beard, and worked carefully until I pulled it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I pulled an arrow from a man, that had struck his belly, and I thought he would die; and after 30 days, his condition did not change. I cut around the arrow, and grasped it, and pulled it out forcefully, and he had no bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And I saw a man whose arrow struck his back, and the wound was closed over it; and the arrow remained inside, and he did not change his natural disposition, nor did he suffer any harm in any of his natural actions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And I saw another man, whom an arrow struck in his face, and the wound closed; and it remained like that without suffering great pain; and many other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I pulled an arrow from a man of the king's princes, that had struck him in the middle of his nose, and it was slightly slanted to the right side. The arrow was completely embedded. I was summoned to treat him after it had been lodged for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I probed it with a very thin probe, and felt nothing; and he felt a prickling and pain below his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I applied an attractive and digestive plaster to the area, so that the area wouldn't swell; and the arrow's location appeared to me.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I kept the plaster on for several days, and the wound healed again, and the patient remained like that for a long time, until he felt the arrow inside his nose one day; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied an acute, corrosive medicine to the wound for several days, until it was open, and probed it, and felt the head of the arrow beginning to emerge; then I added more of that acute medicine to the opening of the wound, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly; and the healing process took about four months, and then the wound widened so I could use pliers, and I moved it from side to side, but it wouldn't come out; then I kept trying different tools, until one day I used well-crafted pliers, according to what their shape will be in the end of this chapter, until I pulled it out, and healed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the doctors judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored:  I restored it then, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely healthy.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Now I have told you the nature of extracting some arrows, so that you apply your treatment to what I have not said, for the book cannot encompass everything; but a skillful master considers even small things, and, based on what is present and lacking, finds new work and new instruments for the removal of strange things that occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not emerge from the limbs where they are lodged except in two ways: either through the place where they enter, or through another part; and the one that emerges through the place where it entered, is an arrow that entered fleshy areas, and sometimes emerges immediately.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not emerge immediately, leave it until the flesh is softened around it, and the exit is eased; and if it is lodged in the bone, and it cannot come out, leave it like that for a few days, and move it each day; and then it will emerge, and if it does not, then pierce around it with a very fine drill, until the area around is widened, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the head, and goes down to one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have mentioned appear in the patient:  do not extract it, but leave it until it is equalized after a few days, because if the arrow reaches that point, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is lodged only in the bone, and does not reach the surface, and the patient remains several days without bad symptoms, then consider the extraction.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very deeply lodged and cannot emerge, then use drills around it, as I have told you; then treat the area until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is lodged in a part of the body where it cannot be seen, search for it everywhere; and if you feel it, extract it with a suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve or vein, widen the wound as much as possible; and extract the arrow if you can, and if there are parts of the arrow that hold it, remove the flesh that is lodged on either side as much as you can, and then break or bend the parts that hold the arrow until you can pull it out; and be careful not to break the arrow, for this would make it harder to extract.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, leave it until the surrounding area is rotten, then extract it, because the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding makes it difficult, apply the treatment we have described in its chapter; and be careful not to cut the nerve or vein, and devise how you can extract the arrow without risk, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and put the patient in the position they were in when the arrow entered, for this is the greatest help possible, and if you cannot, place them as the signs indicate.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	If the arrow emerges from another part, or if something of it is visible, or the skin is swollen where it can be seen or felt clearly: cut then until the pliers can grip it, and then pull it out: it will now be able to emerge.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is lodged in the bone, rotate your hand smoothly, until it enters the bone and widens the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot emerge, leave it for a while, and then resume the extraction until it emerges; and if the shaft of the arrow is there, remove the entire shaft; and if the shaft has fallen, and you want to administer a thrust, apply a pointed instrument so that the point of the arrow enters the instrument's hollow; and then thrust it out, and if the arrow is pointed, apply an instrument with a point that enters it, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is poisoned, you must cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as necessary.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow pierces the thigh or the belly or the bladder or the ribs, and it is close to the surface, cut if you can; and be careful not to cut the vein or the nerve, then pull it out, and then close the wound if necessary; and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tongs used to extract arrows resembles a bird's beak, and see here the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many types: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is like the feather of a bird, to push at the point of the arrow, like this is the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the tongs for pushing and for extracting is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are thirty-one veins from which one bleeds, of which there are sixteen in the head, namely: two that are after the ears, which are called the two "herbech"; and the two arteries that are in the two visible temples; and two veins that are in the two tear ducts of the two eyes, which are called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the base of the nose; and the two windings that are on the neck; and the two veins that are on the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins from which one commonly bleeds are five in each arm: one is the cephalic, and is on the left side, and the common people call it "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called "faste", and is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and the common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right side, and the common people call it "vein of the belly", and is above the elbow, and is the one from which one bleeds, which is clearly visible on the forearm.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salvatelle is the vein that is between the ulnar and the radial, and has two branches; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is below the bend of the forearm on the left side, and the second, the sophene, is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein called "nesse", which is at the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg are three veins beneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	Bleeding from the veins behind the ears helps with chronic colds and headaches; and the method of bleeding, as I tell you, is that you raise the patient's head and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then the patient should tighten their neck with a vise, so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two hanging places on the head: then, with your finger, where you feel the pulse beneath your finger, draw it out; then take the lancet and place it beneath the vein down to the bone, then lift your hand all the way up the vein, and cut both the skin and the vein about two finger-widths apart, and let the blood flow as much as you wish; then bind and tie it, until it is healed; and I have already mentioned the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	Bleeding from the two arteries in the temples is good for chronic, severe headaches, habitual eye inflammation, and sharp eye pain; and the method of bleeding is as I said: the patient tightens their neck, so that the two veins become clearly visible; and feel the pulse beneath your finger, then draw it out; then lift the arm above the vein to your index finger, and place the lancet beneath, and lift the vein upward, and cut it, as you have done with the other two veins, and let the blood flow according to your need; then release the patient, and place your finger on the vein for an hour, then place cotton on it; then tie it tightly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have already spoken about their cutting and extraction, at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Bleeding from the vein of the forehead is as effective as bleeding from the cephalic vein for chronic facial ailments, headaches, and redness; and the method is that the patient tightens their neck by twisting, until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "digging tool", of which here is the shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the tip on the vein, and strike with your hand, or something else, and let blood flow according to the amount you want; then loosen the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is healed, and sometimes it is done with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, the flame should not be too sharp; and bleed across the vein, for the bone is close, and perhaps the flame will break if it is too thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Bleeding from the two veins in the temples helps with eye conditions, inflammation, redness, eye sores, and facial ailments; and the method of bleeding is that the patient tightens their neck by twisting, as before; then bleed, and the bleeding should be across, with the flame a little long and a little wide, because there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is thin, it may break; then make the blood flow as much as you need, and then bind with a bandage, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	Bleeding from the vein in the nose is good for headaches, severe madness, and facial ailments such as migraines and redness, especially if it has lasted a while; and the method of bleeding is that the patient tightens their neck, then tightens their nose with your left hand, and take a thin, long flame, and insert it into the space between the two nostrils, for the vein is not well visible there, and the blood will begin to flow; and do not go too deep, and make the blood flow as needed, and then bind it for a night, for it is quickly restored; and this is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	Bleeding from the two temples helps with constriction of the throat, the beginning of ulceration, and many illnesses, and to impetigo, and scabs, and herpes, and shingles; and the method of bleeding is that the patient tightens their neck, under and around as we said; and let the master be standing over the patient's head, and let the patient sit in a chair, then bleed the vein lengthwise, a little wide; then draw the blood moderately, or as needed; and then do the same thing to the other vein, then loosen the tie, and tighten both veins moderately, so that the patient doesn't choke; and leave it until morning, for the wound to heal.
de la sainie des leivres	of bleeding from the lips
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	Bleeding from the veins above the lips helps with ulcers in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and splits in the lips and nose, and around them.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the method of bleeding is to have the patient sit before you, and tighten their neck as I said; then turn the lip, and look for two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, which are recognizable because they are dark, and because there are small dark veins around them: cut both, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt, cut the largest one on each side, and do the same with the two veins above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of bleeding under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Bleeding from the veins under the tongue helps after bleeding from the cephalic vein, and it is for constriction of the throat, and diseases of the eyes, and diseases of the mouth; and the method of bleeding is that the patient sit between your hands in front of the sun, and lift their tongue, and look underneath on each side for a dark vein: bleed both, and do not go too deep, for the arteries are below.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the arm, which are commonly bled, are bled in two ways: either by pricking with a wide, flat lancet, or with a narrow, lancet-like instrument, called "anesil"; and they are wide or narrow according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flat lancet is very renowned, and is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is useful for opening veins filled with thick, visible blood, and that contain thick and troubled blood; and that is the shape of the narrow lancet:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more pointed and narrow, and it is for bleeding the narrow veins, where there is thin, yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The bleeding of the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps illnesses below the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the belly; and it is necessary for the leech to bleed wisely, and that he beware of the artery that is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery, and a flow of blood comes, then it must be stopped, as I have said; and the lancet should not be pointed, but cutting, like a knife.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilic vein does not appear clearly, then you must press it, and change to another; or you seek a branch of it, or you bleed in place of it the vein in the middle of the arm: it appears clearly; and you cut it with a knife-like lancet, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you want to know the place for bleeding, it is necessary first that you press the arm, that you touch the place until you know the pulse; then mark the place with a marker, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein with a knife-like lancet; and watch that you do not strike the artery when you see the place inflamed, for that is of the artery: dry it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it gush forth like a child's urine, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood from the artery: hasten then, and put your finger over it for a while, then remove your finger if the blood stops, for it happens many times; tie the arm and leave it like that, and do not move it, the sick person; and let it be by precaution, and do not move it until it has healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stopped, and it overwhelms you, and the medicine is not present, then cut the artery if it is visible, because its head will recede; and stop the blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a fig tree bark, and split it, and take one of the halves and tie it well until the next day; if the blood stops, that is good; if not, then treat it as we have said, with the powders that stop blood; and the stopping is not difficult in many cases due to the small size of the wound, and the strength of the bandage on the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	Bleeding from the vein in the middle aids in drawing blood from the head above and the body below, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said; and it is necessary for the bleeder to be careful of the nerve beneath, and if it pierces too deeply and finds the nerve, it will swell and the patient's health will be compromised, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve appears very often, and if it does not appear in some people because of its subtlety, then you must bleed it with a lancet; and dry the nerve to the best of your ability.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then split it lengthwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	Bleeding from the cephalic vein helps, as it draws blood from the head and aids the eyes; and it is necessary to bleed by piercing at the olive vein or the myrtle vein, because it is the safest of all the veins, since it has neither nerve nor artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is necessary to seek the easiest place, and nothing is harmed if one fails the first time, and one starts again; and perhaps the place swells in some people when one fails the first time, but nothing is harmed.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bleeding is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that it is not administered except to maintain health and to avoid future illnesses; and let the bleeding be done in one of the three veins that are on the arm: namely, the cephalic, the basilic, and the median cubital; and one should bleed at the beginning of spring fasting, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of fullness appear; and one should bleed on the first or third day, after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	Bleeding administered for illnesses has no specific time, but when necessary, by day or by night, at all hours and times; and one should not bleed children until fourteen years old, nor women pregnant except from the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Old people who have passed sixty years should not be bled.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wants to be bled, in whatever manner, it is necessary that they cleanse their intestines with a gentle clyster if they have retained much waste, so that the veins do not draw the putrid superfluities from the intestines which harm the principal members; and do not bleed those who are too full of food, or who are drunk, as long as they are so; nor the hydrops; and one should avoid bleeding after colic, vomiting, and bowel movements, and multiple sexual acts, and travail, from staying up late and fasting, and everything that exhausts the virtue, either by something of the body or of the spirit; then thin the humors, if the blood is thick, through food and drinks and medicines, if you have the means; then go into a bath, if anything does not prevent it, to thin the blood, and bleed from the vein of the arm near the elbow, as we have said; and avoid work and hardship, and lust, and similar things that day; and be calm and joyful, and let the bleeder be higher than the one being bled, and rub the arm two or three times, then moderately tighten the bandage above, for when it is too tight or too loose, the blood cannot flow; and then rub the area with your hands until the veins swell and are felt; then let the bleeder moisten the lancet with a little old oil, then place his left hand finger on the vein under the spot where he wants to bleed, so the vein does not burst and fail when struck.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flee like ropes when bleeding, and there are some that are full of wind, so that when one places the lancet on it, it retreats from the lancet, and the vein cannot open, and it is like that with those; and if he opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, therefore the bleeder must be careful in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, that is good; if not, he should begin again a little below or above that spot, if the area is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the area is swollen, and the patient is frightened, let it be a day or two, and do not tie the arm; perhaps there will be hot abscesses; do not go into a bath, then resume bleeding if it pleases him; and if the opening is small, or the blood flows subtly and you fear that it will not release as much blood as you want, thrust the lancet into that same opening straight; and open it slightly above, before the area is swollen; for this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the area swollen, do not resume bleeding, and place a little bit of oil-lime on it, for it lightens the body of the blood, and the lime is gentler than the oil in this place; and thus apply oil-lime in each bleeding when you bleed the veins, to stop the flow of blood; and the same applies to chalk and bole, when placed on the area; it thins the blood and separates it when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess arises, which happens often, especially when it is not bled often enough or the opening of the vein is small, hurry, and place a sponge moistened with hot water and salt on the area, and bind it for an hour; and you must do this after the blood has flowed from the vein, and if any blackness or greenness remains in the area after a few days, it does not harm; and if you wish, apply something made of aloes or myrrh mixed with the juice of calamint, mustard, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times abscesses and appearances occur in the bleeding of the basilica: therefore, place your hand on it, and if you find the area soft under the pressure of your hand, that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, do not apply anything of what we have said, for perhaps arterial blood is flowing; but make a dry poultice to harden the area, then treat it with another treatment, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw out each of the blood according to the quantity of its strength, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow out until it is red; and if you see it thick, let it flow out until it is thinner; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is fitting for one who is full and strong, and needs bloodletting, that a larger wound be made, and the incisions be wide; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and it should be bled little and often, and one should bleed by cutting across, not by pricking; and this manner of bleeding is safe from blood flow and nerve damage, and is better than bleeding from long or wide incisions.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for one whose body weakens during bleeding, one should give him bread soaked in pomegranate juice; if he is heated, draw blood three or four times. And if he is of a cold complexion, let him eat bread soaked in syrup of dates or syrup of aromatic honey with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and a well-scented syrup, before the bleeding.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints during bleeding, after the outflow of much blood, it is necessary that he drink broth of meat, and subtle fragrant syrup, and use the other things that we have said in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to have his arm lanced and bled again, it is necessary, when he is weakened by a large bleeding, that he be bled little by little, according to the amount of his continuing strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if someone wants to have his arm lanced after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, he should be bled seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if someone wishes to bleed from another part, he should bleed on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood within the body that is already heated, and causes fever; so a great quantity must be drawn, and the opening widened until it bleeds profusely; then you should observe all the conditions of bleeding, and place your hand on his pulse when he bleeds, so that death does not come instead of fainting, and this happens many times when the bleeder is negligent; and it is not appropriate when you want to untie the arm and cause blood to emerge a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press firmly on it; nor if it is bent, that he extend his arm hastily, for that would be harmful; but leave it until he bleeds a second time; or you should prick the opening with the point of a flame until the blood which has congealed at the opening of the vein flows out forcefully, and put a little salt dissolved in water on it, and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it and do not compress it until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, bleed him in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the middle of the arm is bled instead of the vein of the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the method of bleeding is that the patient puts his hand in warm water until the veins are red; then it is moderately tied so that the vein is clearly visible, then bleed it directly through the vein, not from the side or the length; and the opening should be wide, and bled close to the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot come out, put the hand back in warm water, and let the blood run into the water until you have enough; and if it is summer, do not put the hand back in warm water, for it is put more in winter than in summer; and bleeding from this vein is safer than any other vein, as there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	Bleeding from the vein of the right hand is good for all liver ailments, and this is the method: hold the hand and put it in warm water until the vein is swollen, so that it is visible; and if you bleed through it, and if you cut it all the way through, it will not hurt; and do not go too deep, because the nerves are all exposed beneath the flesh, and then put the hand back in warm water if the blood is congealed in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn blood as much as needed, put oil and a bandage on the vein to close it quickly, and do the same for each cut.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	Bleeding from the vein in the left hand is good for mouse disease, and do the same as I told you for the right hand.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	Bleeding from the vein of the sophene is good for all ailments below the body, such as ailments of the marris, and retention of flowers, and ailments of the kidneys, and thighs and old legs, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the method of this bleeding is that the patient puts his foot in warm water, and rubs the vein until it swells, and ties above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and many veins run from above the foot; bleed it then in the wider vein, or at the ankle, whichever is better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you bleed above the foot, be careful of the nerves below, and bleed it transversely, as when cutting; and let the flame be nearby.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, return the foot to the water and let the vein empty well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the bleeding fails the first time, start again a little higher, for the place is salted; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and thus do with the sophene of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The location of the sciatic vein is at the ankle, and its bleeding is useful for hip pain, when it is for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its bleeding is that the patient enters a bath, and tightens above the ankle four times by twisting, for otherwise the vein does not appear; and if it appears, bleed it in all the ways you can, and transversely; and it is better that you cut it, for the place is safe, and it is very prone to bleeding in the hands of men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, bleed any vein that appears on the back of the foot, towards the little toe, and guard against the nerves; and make as much blood flow as you wish, and then loosen the bandage, and put on cotton and tighten it; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	Of cupping.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cups are made of horn, or brass, or glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping without striking is also in two ways: either with fire, or without fire; and cupping done by striking and drawing blood is done in fourteen places on the body, of which one is right on the head; and another in the middle of the neck; and two others on the two sides of the neck; and one under the chin; and one on each shoulder; and one on the hips; and ones in the middle of the two arms; and ones on the two legs; and ones on the two ankles; and cupping does not draw much blood, except for small veins scattered in the flesh, and therefore it does not weaken a man, as is done with bleeding from a vein; and it should not be administered, neither with nor without fire, in any illness that comes from repletion, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of illness it is necessary to cup, or by custom, we administer it every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and at every time; for there are those who, when they need cupping, have a heavy head; and there are those who find fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and in the neck, and darkness in their eyes; and those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have their tongue swollen, and cough up blood; and there are those who dream, and see by night blood and wounds and deaths and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the middle of the month, we order them to be cupped after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	Bleeding from the temples helps the heaviness of the head...that comes to the eyes, and it should not be done after the evacuation of the whole body; and this cupping is in place of bleeding from the cephalic vein, and those of cold complexion should not use it, or those who have a cold, for this does them much harm; and therefore, the elderly should not use it, nor those who have cold ailments in their head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often bleed from it become forgetful, and therefore the cupping should be placed a little lower, out of concern for forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	Cupping in the neck is in place of bleeding from the head and the basilica vein, and therefore it is useful for tightening of the breast, and for fissures in the windpipe, and for coughs, and for fullness; and it should not be applied too forcefully, for if it holds too firmly, it will induce forgetfulness in the stomach and the heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	Cupping on the second ribs of the neck is useful for headaches, and eye inflammation and migraines, and for constriction, and for pain in the roots of the teeth, and is in place of bleeding from the basilica vein; and you must instruct the person that they should press their hand when applying it, so that they do not cut the artery, and do not cause a flow of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	Cupping under the chin is useful for mouth ailments, and for the corruption of gums, and similar maladies of the mouth; and it is in place of bleedings from the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Cupping on the shoulders is useful for illnesses arising from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	Cupping on the elbows is as effective as on the three veins of the arm, because it draws blood from these large veins; and instruct the person not to press too deeply, because the area is thin, and contains nerves and arteries underneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping placed on the rump is good for hemorrhoids of the fundament, and for maladies underneath, and it is necessary that the cupping be large, and made of bronze, as it needs to draw well; and perhaps, if it were flimsy, it would break; and it would cause large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	Cupping on the legs bleeds openly, because they draw blood from the whole body, and are useful for longstanding pains in the kidneys, and bladder, and uterus, and they reduce the symptoms; and they are in place of the two ankles, and the two heels, and nevertheless they weaken the body after prolonged use, and cause swelling in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying a cupping glass is to first make it empty, and gently suck it on, and quickly place it, and move it evenly, and do not cease doing this until you see the area reddened and swollen, and the redness of the blood appears; then, remove it, and replace the cups, and take precautions in the body's condition, for there are some who have thin skin, and light complexions: thus it is necessary to strike only once, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and a little deep; and to suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to make the thick blood flow easier.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we want to draw out a little blood gradually, it will be enough to strike once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want a lot of blood, we must repeat the process often; and if the blood is thick, strike deeply, and the end result is that the heart is pierced suddenly, and it is necessary for those with thick, hard skin and narrow pores, to anoint the places of the cupping glasses with warming and dissolving oils: if it is in summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or oil of pumpkin seed; and if it is in winter, with cress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are thick and cold, take bitter almond oil, or balsam oil, or anise oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the person being bled has tender skin and wide pores, no oil should be applied, but the area should be washed after cupping with rose water, or cold water, or black nightshade water, or pumpkin water, or porcelain water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, let them be bathed with willow bark water, or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those with large superfluities are bathed with old wine, or oak water, or anise or chamomile decoctions, or similar things; and one should not be bled with cupping before or during a bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and one should not sleep after being cupped, and it is necessary that they wash themselves, when they are to be cupped and when they have been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And be careful if the person being bled is choleric, and if the blood is too sharp and inflamed; they must take cool things, such as pomegranates, endive, and lettuce in the bath, and similar things; and eat puccins, and hare meat, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those with a cold constitution should take honey syrup, and moderately fragrant wine, which is between old and new, and eat little, and eat puccins and small birds and pigeons; and on the day they are to be cupped, they should drink more than they eat; and it is necessary to give some men sometimes treacle or nutmeg before or after cupping, to strengthen the main limbs; and let the blood be thinned, but those who are hot should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	Cups placed without striking are those placed on the liver, the spleen, gout, the stomach, the belly, the kidneys, and the hip, for these members do not tolerate being struck upon them, and this is done only to draw blood from limb to limb, as we put them on the breasts when someone is bleeding; to remove the viscosity in the limb, as we put cups on the stomach and belly to soften the limb; and it alleviates pain, when there is a blockage or stone, and it perhaps removes the blockage by its attractive virtue, or dislodges the stone from its place; and so it does when it is placed on the liver and spleen when there is retained wind, and these cups are administered empty just to suck; and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes filled with lukewarm water, as in the case of pleurisy, and in such a manner that one fills the cup with hot water alone, or water in which herbs suitable for this have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cup administered with fire is this:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it should have two fingers in width and half a palm in depth, and have a small hole on the side near the middle, as for pushing a needle, and be of bronze, so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb; and have in the middle a crosswise rod of bronze or iron, to place a lit candle; and there are large and small ones, according to the diseases and the age of those who take them; for the cups of children are different from those of the old, and of the thin from the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should place this cup on the limb in this way: take the candle of wax or linen, and put it in the middle of the cup through the rod that is in the middle of the cup, so that the flame is at the bottom of the cup so it does not burn the patient; and then place it on the limb, and your fingers are on the hole we mentioned, so that when one wishes, the vapor goes away, and one removes the cup; and one takes the linen as before, and repeats it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cup, then, which is administered in a pleurisy illness, with water only, there is no rod or hole, and it is administered only when it is full of water, and is placed on the limb only; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Leeches are administered only on limbs where cups cannot be placed due to their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in places devoid of flesh, such as the feet or the nails, and other similar places; and the quality of use is that when you find leeches that are in clear, fresh water without puncture, take them; and put them in fresh water for a night, so that they are full and have nothing in their stomachs; and then drain them from a vein and from a cup, then rub the limb until it is red, and place the leeches; and when they are full and fall off, if it is a place where one can place a cup, then place the cup, because it is very good afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.
