If not, remove the place of blood, and then water, well, and then squeeze it; and if the place bleeds too much after the leeches, moisten a linen cloth in cold water, and apply it until the blood is stopped; and if the blood is multiplied, apply powdered vitriol or gall, and similar things, until it stops; or put half of peeled beans on the area, and leave them until they burn on the area, it will stop immediately; and if you need more, take other leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the leeches will not adhere, rub the area with fresh blood, or insert a needle until blood comes out, then place the leeches, and as soon as they feel the blood, they adhere; and when you want them to drop off, sprinkle a little powdered alum and salt or ashes, and they will fall off immediately.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is about the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that fools scorn this chapter, as if they have never seen any of the ancient books, nor read any writings; and for this reason, learning is rare in our land, for I have never found any good; and I know nothing, except through the knowledge of ancient books, in which I have studied so much that I have mastered the subject, and through experience, and through the custom of my life; and I have described in this chapter what is contained, and have summarized it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, as I have done in these two previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is fitting that we state in the prologue of this book the main points of the subject and the chapters where the wise man applies his understanding, and remains focused on the truth, so that those who are skilled may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture, dislocation, twisting, or crushing occurs to someone, you must quickly bleed the patient on both sides, if nothing prevents you, such as weakness of the body, or if it is a child or old person; or if the weather is not very hot or too cold; and avoid cold foods, such as cold game, and the flesh of birds and roe deer, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not overfill with foods that fill the veins with blood, lest you fear a hot abscess, or the spreading of matter in the limb; let the patient return to his former practices.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that promote growth and viscosity, such as boiled wheat in water, rice, and the legs, feet, and belly of cows, eggs, fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment, the fracture heals more quickly and completely.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot heal properly or knit together according to their nature due to the dryness of the limbs, nor those that are too tender, such as the bones of young children; but there is no cure except to support the broken bone with strong splints that hold the limb together until it strengthens as it was before; and it does not completely do its work, and therefore, it is necessary to nourish it with substantial foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a fracture of the head is different from a fracture of the arm or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that extend outward, and others that are sharp, like the cut of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there are fractures with a wound, and fractures with only a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And for each type there is a specific method, and its own instrument in the restoration, according to what the memory brings to its place; and a fracture of the bone is recognized by the fact that the place is twisted, and it is evident from the appearance, and it sounds when pressed by the hand; and when there is no twisting or sound when touched, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no fracture; but there can still be twisting, or a crack, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	So you should not move it by hand, but apply the medicines that come afterward, and then hold it gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that fractures that extend outward, where the two parts are separated, must now be placed in equal alignment, lest a hot abscess arise; and if a hot abscess arises, leave it for a day or so until the abscess subsides; then set it in alignment gently and wisely, and know that the restoration is easier than if there are pieces; then hold it as is required later.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if the bone has broken pieces, extend it from two sides, if it's a hand or foot, or with your hand if it's a small limb, or with two cords, or with one cord and your hand; and place the limb according to its natural form, so that when the broken parts of the limb are separated, reassemble all the additions in their place as best you can, and be careful that your work does not cause the patient injury or pain; and well align the two ends of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it well with your hand if you think it is not properly aligned: then straighten it beautifully, and do not hold it too tightly, nor press it as those do whose work causes a hot abscess and contraction in the limb, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is in place, carefully instruct the patient not to move it, neither when awake nor when sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way; and carefully ensure that the limb is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, it is not properly aligned, and it must be put in such a position that he feels no pain; and be careful that it is placed straight, that no twisting occurs when it is restored; and the quality of the broken limb is as I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs vary in size and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as arms and fingers and similar ones: so it is necessary to wrap them in soft, fine linen cloths; and those that are large, such as thighs and legs: it is necessary to wrap them in a wide and hard bandage, for the wide bandages embrace the entire large limb, and bind it equally on all sides, so that there is no blemish; then tie around light padding, three or four turns according to the limb, and gently tighten the bandage all around, then move above the break and tighten less, gradually separating the break; and soften the bandage little by little, until you cover a large portion of the healthy area, then take another bandage and turn it around again over the broken area; then return to the area below the break, and bind it moderately, neither too tight nor too loose, as we have said in the first book above; then place linen pads or cloths between the bandages, until it is all even, then bind it all over with a bandage, and then put your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, place something that soothes the abscess and reduces the swelling, and leave it thus for a few days; then bind over your splints, and they should be half as wide as a well-cut cane, or of wood from which wedges are made, or of palm ribs, and be in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the splint placed over the break be somewhat larger and wider than the others; and be as long as is suitable for the limb, whether small or large; then bind over the splints as you did in the first section, then bind over a suitable thread, as in the first section over the break; tighter at the top, gradually less so; and the thread should be of moderate thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, and should be of soft linen; for if the thread is thick, as I have seen in the works of fools who make their bandages from twisted linen cords, and that is a great mistake, for the bandage cannot be even if it is too thin, and it should not have less than the width of a finger between each splint.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is injured by the edges of the splints after tightening them in healthy areas, then place linen padding or wool wadding beneath them so that he is not injured.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the fracture, and the bone is broken, I will describe the treatment afterward.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to bind splints to all fractured limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is large, it is not necessary to place splints firmly until after five or seven days, or more, according to your certainty of a subsequent inflammatory abscess; and see here the manner of ancient poultices for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: take the flour that adheres to the millstones, and mix it with abundant egg, and apply this mixture, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it; and this is the common manner of poultice for restoring fractures in many cases, especially for women and small children, for it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of poultice restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: take three parts of abareis, ladani, enule, and asefetide, and gum arabic and mugat, each ten parts; myrrh and aloes, each five parts; aloes wood nine parts; and make powder, and mix with abundant egg; if the patient's complexion is warm, use this poultice, for it is a good composition, and quickly restores broken bones and is beneficial to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another poultice that is good for twists: take mugat and vismalve, each ten parts; myrrh and aloes, each nine parts; acaice six parts; armenian bole ten parts, and grind well, and mix with water or abundant egg, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another poultice for dislocated joints and separated bones, easing the ensuing pain, and for use on the bone and fracture: take new wool, and soak it in warm oil and cooked oil, and apply to the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These poultices do not restore, but they are good for calming inflammatory abscesses and properly relieving pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another poultice that restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves and leaves of earth-pea, and grind together, and make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another poultice for the restoration of bone fracture and to lessen the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of marshmallow, chamomile, violet flowers, chickpea flour, one part of each; and grind, and mix with wine; and if the limb is inflamed, mix it with moist coriander water, or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another stronger poultice than the first, when a hard abscess arises in the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of marshmallow, flaxseed, balusters, melilot, and yarrow, and violet and chamomile flowers, one part of each; and grind, and mix with salt water, or fresh water, or wine, according to the warmth of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not put on a fractured limb to restore strength anything other than a cerote made of wax and oil, and nothing else; and says it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen seems to say that one should put on a fractured limb, for restoration, slightly warm, dry things, such as myrrh, aloes, frankincense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another kind of poultice that is good for injuries and pain: take mugwort and chopped human hair, or bird feathers, and marshmallow, and salt likewise, and grind them, and make a poultice and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then, after a while, remove it, and be mindful that the patient feels no pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; if not, do not remove it for several days. And if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hurry and remove the poultice immediately; and take light cloth, and a moist sea sponge, and immerse in water, and apply to the affected area, until the itching ceases, and the pain is soothed; then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry wool, moistened in water or rose oil, and bind for a night, until you are sure of a hot abscess; and relieve the inflammation of the limb, and the pain is removed, then resume the careful binding, and a little poultice, and do not bind it as tightly as before; and continue binding until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that a hot abscess, redness, pain, and swelling have completely disappeared, and you need a poultice and binding, then start again, just as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if nothing from what we have said comes to the limb, then do not remove the binding until after three or four or five or seven days; and sometimes leave it for twenty days, according to what one sees, until the fracture heals and the flesh approaches; then bind it more tightly than before, and increase its nourishment, as I said before; and if you see the place drying more than is necessary, know that nourishment cannot come; therefore, moisten it with lukewarm water every time you remove the binding, and this should be every third day, and loosen the bandage a little; by this work, then, nourishment comes to the limb, and quickly corrects what foolish surgeons do, who restore the limb wrongly: this is bad, and it is a fearful practice, and I see nothing else in it than letting it be and working correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of the various types of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many types of fractures exist, with diverse forms, and their causes are distinct; for there are fractures caused by a sword blow, and the collarbone breaks all the way down to the skin beneath the bone, as a hedge or a log does; and for this reason, this type of fracture is called a "hedge fracture".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Where the sword cuts the bone through, and is called this type of fracture "complete"; and the wound from these two fractures is large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a striking blow, or a fissure, or a blow from a stone, or from falling on a stone, or other similar causes.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture, which approaches the membrane beneath the bone, or which is above the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And there are wounds that are penetrating the bone as thin as a hair, and the fissure is small, and for that reason this fracture is called "capillary"; and if the wound is made either by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by a similar thing, and it forces a piece of bone inward, and the place is split as blacksmiths do when they strike on the cauldrons; so the stone enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those whose bones are moist or soft, like a child's head; and happens to all these types of fractures that small pieces are separated like stars; and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all types of fractures by the pulling on them, and by the investigation with probes, and by the corrupted flesh that is on them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary fracture is recognized by this: when the bone is uncovered, and one rubs it, the fracture appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, watch for the patient's accidents, and if you see any bad accident, such as vomiting of phlegm, and loss of consciousness, and swelling, and throbbing, and acute fever, and the eyes becoming bulging and red, and other similar conditions in various dispositions, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a frightening accident, and you hope for healing, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the injured person comes to you first, and it is in winter, then the bone must be removed before the fourteenth day, if you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, before the tissue under the bone is corrupted, and the accidents that we have mentioned come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone reaches the tissue that covers the brain, then you must split the fractured part like this:  and you should take the head of the injured person and expose the bone in every way you can, and over the wound surface as gently as you can.  And if a discharge of blood comes when exposing the bone, or a hot abscess, then help with what is necessary, and you should fill the space with cloths soaked in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the hot abscess is calmed, and be sure that the discharge of blood has stopped; then begin to remove the bone around it, and this is done in two ways: one way is that you cut a narrow incision in front, and that is the shape:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then put another incision larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have a number of different incisions, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed, and be of tempered iron; and work gently, so that you do not injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is strong and hard, you must pierce it around, before you apply incisions with drills, not so deep that they pierce the bone of the head, and there should be a margin or circle above the point, that prevents the point from passing through the bone; and you should have several, so that each one goes to its place in the thickness of the bone, so that you have drills for all the holes; and this is the form of the three types of drills:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the fractured bone is that you place a drill on the bone and turn it with your fingers until you know that the bone is pierced; then reposition the drill a little further and do this all around, then use scalpels to cut the space of the bone that is between the holes, and do this as subtly as you can, and gently, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand, or with any instruments that you have, such as pincers, tongs; and be careful not to touch the brain or the surface.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and extracted the bone, you must remove the remaining fragments of bone with any other instrument similar to a scalpel, but it must be thinner and more subtle than the other scalpel; and if any small bones or scales remain, remove them gently with one of the instruments; then treat the wound with dressings and ointments that we have mentioned.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way of working is that which Galen says, which is safer; and he praises it very much, and that is his opinion.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you must expose a portion of the bone, where the fracture is visible, so that when you have exposed that part, you will place the head of this lenticular scalpel underneath, of which this is the form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And it does not cut on one side, and the part is sharp on two sides, so that the cutting edge is towards the bone; then strike with a small mallet from above, so that you gently cut the bone all around, and pay close attention to the cloth underneath; if it adheres to the bone, remove it gently, as it can be removed without harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not pierce through to the cloth, and the bone is only cut superficially, and there are small pieces, you must remove those fragments and scrape off the scales with a fine scraper, of which you should have various sizes, to best fit each area, according to the task and the appearance of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Use larger scrapers first, and then finer ones afterwards, and do not cease until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other cuts and subtle fractures, you must apply a remedy according to its direction; and this is something not easily understood by those who have devoted themselves to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the surface is exposed, you must take a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and place it over the wound; then take another cloth doubled in two or three layers, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first cloth; and do this as gently as possible, so as not to irritate the surface; then apply another bandage, and do not bind it too tightly, just enough to hold the wound; and leave it like this for one or two days, until the inflamed abscess is calmed, then remove it, and apply medicines like lily roots, vetch flour, incense powder, and aristolochia, and similar things; and make a powder from these, and apply it to the wound, and apply remedies often without causing irritation; and ensure that the wound is kept clean, that you do not leave the ointment there, nor allow pus to accumulate, for when pus accumulates on the brain's tissue, it will fester and rot, and great harm will come to the patient; for when something caustic is applied to the surface, it will cause further harm from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, be warned, if any bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, it is undoubtedly dangerous.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the darkening is only due to the medicine applied, having such a property, you must take one part honey and three parts rose oil, mix them and apply a cloth to the affected area; then treat it with the necessary remedies until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two upper nasal bones are broken, or one alone, since there are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break, but only bends or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, you should insert your little finger or a small instrument into the nostril, and align the fracture with your index finger and thumb, so that the nose returns to its natural shape; and do this gently, and ensure that the patient does not experience pain during your procedure.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the upper part of the nose, and the finger cannot reach the place, you should place it aligned with the head of a stick, a little thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the fracture is of two parts, do the same, and try to restore it on the first day, if possible; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the inflamed swelling has subsided, then apply strips of linen cloth to the nose tip if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you place one on the other side, if the fracture is there; and let the strips be so large that they fill the nostrils.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some healers say that the strips should be soaked in butter and changed each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is good, but they should be soaked in a mixture of egg white and flour; then leave the strip until the bone is firm and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes goose feathers are placed in the nose in place of strips, and a soft cloth is wrapped around it, and the fracture is held, and the patient breathes through it; or do whatever you wish.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if a boil forms in the nose while you are working on it, put a cerate or cotton soaked in rose oil, or a little diachylon, there.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a boil does not form, apply a plaster from ground flaxseed and incense powder, mixed with egg white.  Then place light cotton wool on top and do not bandage the nose.  And if the nasal fracture is small and broken into small pieces, remove it with appropriate instruments, then close the fissure and treat with preparations for mending flesh and bones, like suitable plasters and ointments.  And if there is no wound inside the nose, treat it with strips and apply lead strips until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is fractured from below, and there is no external wound, and the fracture is only superficial, and not broken in two, except for splinters inside, it can be easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is on the right side, you should place your index finger into the patient's mouth; and if the fracture is on the left jaw, place your right index finger, and gently push the fractured part inward, and hold it in place with the other hand, and make it level.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jaw fracture is separated in two, you should apply extension to both sides until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the teeth are moved or fractured, tie them with a gold, silver, or silk thread, then place a plaster over the fractured jaw, and put a double bandage over it; and place a large, well-made splint, or a piece of equal-sized leather, long and wide according to the jaw, and bind it as tightly as possible, and tell the patient to rest and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the shape is changing, unbind it on the third day, and then put back in place what has changed; and apply a plaster of powdered millstone mixed with abundant egg or linseed flour, after removing the bandage; and place a light wool on the plaster, and if the plaster holds and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until he is healed; many times he is healed within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if a hot abscess comes, administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and a wound together, check if any piece of bone has been removed; if necessary, carefully remove it with suitable instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire according to your needs.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there remains none, if the wound is large, close it and apply suitable plasters to encourage the formation of flesh, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps break many times before, near the shoulder, and the fracture is in three ways: either it is broken and separated into two, with pieces, and is the easiest to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the procedure is, when the fracture is without a wound, that you have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder where the forceps broke; and the other stretches the neck towards the part; then place the fracture evenly with your fingers, so that the shape is as it should be, and there is neither an appearance nor a shift.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to stretch further, place a round pad of cloth or wool under the patient's shoulder, and it should be large according to your needs; and extend and lift the forceps, and hold the pad in your hand, so that you place the fracture evenly, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the forceps out, because it is deeply embedded, it is necessary that the patient lie often on their back, and place a medium-sized pillow under the shoulder, and the assistants push the shoulder down, until the bone of the forceps is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then straighten the fracture with your fingers, and if you find it fractured, you must split it open; and gently pull the pieces apart, and if the bone cannot be joined by any means, then cut it with one of the knives you have; but make sure you place this instrument under the forceps to protect the surface.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it resembles a spoon, and is not sharp, and should be as wide as needed, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and have two ends, as you see, and one wide and the other narrow, like the opening of the wound you made when you pulled the bones apart; and when you are sure of a hot abscess, then stitch the wound, and if the opening is small, or you doubt a hot abscess, then fill the wound with cloths and bandages, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a hot abscess comes, soak a cloth in rose oil, and vinegar, and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The setting of the bone, when it is without wounds and without cuts, is that you put the plaster of mill powder and egg white on the bone, and place soft pads on top, and put a splint under the arm, if you need it; then take a very wide bandage, a palm in width, then place a double cloth over the pads and the plaster; then take a thin splint three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage, so that the end of the bandage hangs down; and place the splint over the fracture, and turn the bandage over the neck, and under the healthy armpit, and under the injured armpit; and adjust it from each part, and when you see that the bandage holds the fracture properly, and you clearly see that the splint does not move over the broken bone, then watch it every day, and when the bandage loosens, then tighten it; and make the patient lie on their back, and place a small pillow under the armpit when they sleep, to raise the shoulder; this will ease the fracture of the forceps by relieving the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless an adverse accident occurs, until 20 days; then repeat the plaster, if you see it is needed, and tighten and leave it like that until it is restored; and it is restored in at most 28 days, and in less time in some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the fracture of the shoulder.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Often, the shoulder breaks in a wide or middle place, and it is not known for certain except by touch; then adjust it according to the shape of the fracture, and reposition it according to its natural form, in all the ways you can; then put on the place mill powder with plenty of egg white, and soft pads, and place a double cloth on top; then place a wide and thin splint, a little wider than the shoulder, and if there is hair under the splint in any place on the shoulder, fill that hair with linen pads, so that the splint is even; and then tighten it with a large firm bandage, so that the splint does not move from its place, and check the bandage every day; and every time it loosens, tighten it, and put the splint back in place if it moves from its place, and let the patient lie on their side; and the shoulder is restored in 20 or 25 days. And when this number is complete, untie it, and be sure, because it is not a bone that moves out of place easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes forward, and is not under the skin, then cut it open, and remove it, and do what we have said about treating a hot abscess in the fracture of the shoulder.
de la brisure dou pis	Of the fracture of the ribs.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The ribs are sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; but they often break on the outside.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it bends inwards, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of breath, and tightness, and perhaps vomits blood, and the hair appears on the broken bone, and one can feel it well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that the patient lies often on their back, and place a cushion between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and bring the ribs of the two ribs together with your hands, and carefully try to make it even in every way that you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then apply plasters and bandages over the slight layer of salt, or another lightweight material, and wrap it in a cloth, and bind it over the broken bone, so that it does not move; and wrap the bandage around the back, and tighten it appropriately, and check the bandage every hour, and if it loosens, tighten it; and if it needs to be untied, because of corrosion or itching that comes to the area, or pain or abscess, then hurry, and untie it, and remove the plaster, and address whatever has come from the methods of treatment; then reapply the plaster, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Of the fracture of the ribs.
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the fracture of the ribs usually occurs only in the thick areas behind the back, and at the head inside, and they only bend because they are brittle; and one feels this well by the examination of the ribs.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is that you align the fracture, as is proper.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and bind it with a bandage, if you need one.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is leaning inwards, the patient feels very great pain and stabbing, just like a pricking, because the bone pierces the tissue; and it spurts out with force, and the patient coughs and vomits a great deal of blood, and it is a serious illness, and the ancients have given much consideration to it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And some say that it is necessary to administer foods that inflate the belly, to push the fracture outwards.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do that, lest a hot abscess arise, if it has not already.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has arisen, treat it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some of you say that cupping should be applied to the area, to draw out strongly, and that seems reasonable; however, there is concern that cupping might draw out superfluities to the place due to the disposition of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of you say that the area should be covered with wool soaked in warm oil, and tents are placed between the ribs to equalize the wound around, then treated with pleurisy treatment, diet, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure because of the bone that pierces the flesh, and there is fear in the patient, then it is necessary to cut above the location of the broken rib, and one must place an instrument underneath to guard the surface; and then one must cut the bone, and draw it slightly, and then stitch the two edges of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with plasters until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hot abscess comes, place cloths soaked in rose oil on it; and treat the area as required for an abscess, and let him lie often on the side where it is, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes a fracture occurs in the bones of the neck, and rarely does it bend; and likewise in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, watch if you see his hands softened and swollen and lifeless, and he cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is fatal in many conditions, and if he moves them and feels them well when they are squeezed and pricked, know that the joint of the bone is safe, and that the patient will be cured if treatment is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar things happen to the spine of the back, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, watch if his feet are softened, and if the accidents are there as in the hands, and above the back there is wind and expulsion without will; and when he is turned on his stomach, there is expulsion without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is turned on his back and he wants to sit up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is fatal; therefore, do not labor in his cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these accidents do not come to him, the thing is less serious.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you observe if there is a hot abscess, then put rose oil or egg oil on the spine until it is calmed; then apply a comforting and drying plaster, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on the part where he feels pain until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone separates, it is necessary to cut on the affected area; remove the bone, then join the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with stitches, then treat it with a healing ointment, until it is healed; and if the bone head is fractured, which is called the "head of the arm," put the pad of your left hand on it, and align it with your right hand as much as possible, then apply the plaster and splint, if you need them; then bind it, and if there is a detached bone, cut it open and remove it, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	Sometimes the hip bone is fractured, and if it happens, there is little bruising around the head; and it splits lengthwise, and bends inward, and the patient feels pain, and a puncture, and swelling in the broken area.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above the fracture; and know what the fracture is and its shape; and if the fracture is only at the head, align the fracture until it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is lengthwise, or it bends inward, make the patient lie on their stomach until the restoration of the fracture is prepared.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have aligned it, place the plaster, then put a splint of wood or leather, and bind the fracture so that it does not move; and fill the space beneath the ribs, so that the space is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side, or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if a hot abscess comes, do not touch it until the hot abscess is calmed, and place on it what we have previously said; and then return to the restoration, and bind it as necessary, if there is no bad accident; and this is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the fracture of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is that which is between the ribs and the head of the shoulder, and if it is fractured, it should be restored according to one of the two methods: one of which is that you take a stick of medium thickness, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie two ligatures to the two ends, and hang them up, and let the patient sit on a chair; then place the broken arm on the stick, so that it reaches the armpit, and have a curve of the stick in the middle; then hang it on some heavy object or the attendant stretches it down; then the attendant should put the break even with their hands together, so that the break returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that the patient is supported on a stretcher, and the hand is tied to their neck, then instruct two attendants that one should hold what is above the fracture in their hands, and the other hold underneath with a whole ligature, and each stretches in their direction.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you wish the extraction to be stronger, tighten one ligature under the fracture and above the fracture, and each of the attendants stretches in their direction.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the head of the shoulder, you must place one ligature in the middle under the armpit, and another towards the rib, below the fracture; and also if the fracture is towards the ribs, you must lightly place a ligature without effort, so that the fracture is even above its place and above the ribs; then make the fracture even, as it should be, and tighten it, if no inflamed abscess has come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an inflamed abscess comes, do not tighten it for seven days, and put moistened wool in a mixture of oil and rose oil, until the inflamed abscess is calmed; then tighten it, and the way to tighten it is that you put the plaster over the fracture, then assemble the arm above the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and put the cloth, and tighten over the shoulder and over the arm, so that the arm is in the position of a straight line, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone is not displaced.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone will not move, use splints, and place a splint wider and stronger than the others over the fracture, and have one inch of space between each splint, and each splint should be so large that it extends three inches on each side of the fracture; then tighten over the splints, as I said at the beginning of the chapter about the fracture, more strongly and less loosely.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the placement of the splints, and the tightening, as we have said, at the time you restore the fractured limb, and you doubt a hot abscess, leave it untied until the seventh day, as we have said; then check the bandage every three days, that itching or swelling or any other harm does not come to the place, or that the nourishment cannot reach the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it is right, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accident occurs, do not loosen it until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back, with their hands on their stomach; and place one cushion full of wool under the shoulder; and check every hour of the day or night that the shape of the fractured limb does not move, or the bandage does not soften; correct it by the power of medicine, and give him the food that we have previously mentioned, in such a way that the food is subtle at first; and when it begins to recover, it should be more substantial.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and the leg should be recovered in 40 days in total; and then it should be loosened and administered baths and ointments to correct the place.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the tightness is severe and swollen, it remains unloosened for 50 days or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the two "fossils," of which one is small, and it is the one that supports the thumb; and the other is large, and it is the one that is underneath, towards the little finger; perhaps only the large fossil is broken, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small fossil is broken, the restoration is easy, and the healing; and when the large one is broken, the healing is difficult, and more serious than when they are both broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small fossil that is broken, it needs to be gently extended and put straight.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large fossil, it needs to be held tighter; and extend it on a cushion, and hold the thumb of the hand higher than the others, and the little finger lower than the other fingers, and let the patient lie across himself, and a cushion in front of him higher, so that the patient does not suffer any discomfort; then let the minister stretch his arm to the lower part of his hand, or to a strap, and another minister to another one on top.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then the surgeon must put it straight, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is broken into pieces, put each in its place, and if there is any that is separated which hurts the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, you must remove it and take it out, as we have said before.
