Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken of it in the singular chapter; thus take the cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the restoration, hot abscesses arise, apply a poultice of cerote made of rose oil and white wax, neither too hard nor too soft; and bind the poultice gently over it, until the hot abscess is appeased.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	Then remove the cerote and apply a plaster of mill powder with abundant egg, then put on the splints, and let the splint of the fracture be stronger and slightly wider than the others; and know that it should have six splints or more in various positions: whether the fracture is in one bone or two; and bind it more tightly over the fracture than elsewhere, and gradually less as it recedes, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the bandages over the fracture be soft and moist, and not hard or rough; and let the thread with which it is bound be linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And observe the limb and the bandage after several days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accident comes to the limb, such as itching which comes to the limb, then you must bathe the limb in hot water until the itching is appeased; and let the limb rest neither too tightly nor too loosely.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then recommence the binding, and if the bandages are softened and the bone separated, or similar things, then adjust it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you take care that nourishment cannot reach the limb because it is too tight, then you must loosen it a little, and leave it like this for a few days until nourishment flows there, and then bind it tighter.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the sick person, do not loosen it until 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	or, in the meantime, let him hang his hands at his neck, and let his neck be straight, and guard against movement and fidgeting, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture will be restored in 30 or 35 days, and perhaps in 20 days, according to the composition and the complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and at the ends of the fingers there are few fractures, and there are many times only bending.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is fractured or bent, the patient must sit cross-legged and sit straight in front of him, equally; then he places his hand on a flat surface, and the attendant extends the broken bones and aligns them, so that they are properly joined; and he places the plaster and bandages, if no abscess forms, then he places a splint according to the size of the area; and it is wrapped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is within or around the sole of the palm, make a ball of cloths and instruct the patient to hold it to his broken palm; and then bind it with a long cloth, and let the splint be of soft leather, as large as the sole of the hand, and bind it, as necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is outward, you must place a splint above and another below in the palm, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie it all around the hand, and bandage the space between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture is on any of the fingers, if it is the thumb, place it straight as appropriate; and bind it with the palm, and if you wish, place a small straight splint to raise the fracture, and keep it still; and if the fracture is in the other fingers, such as the index or one of the others, place it straight and bind it with the healthy finger that is next to it; or you bind them all together in one holding, as you please, or you place a splint as in the thumb; and be careful in restoring and arranging any abscesses that form, and help those that come about, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the thigh is often broken, and it is well seen when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration is done by binding one bandage above the fracture and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on their face, then each attendant extends their bandage equally to their side; and this is when the fracture is in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is near the root of the thigh, one bandage should be towards the groin, and the other below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is near the knee, then one bandage should be beside the knee, and the other extended downwards; then let the attendants place the bone equal with their two hands, so that it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the plaster, and bandage it, if no abscess forms there.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it calm down, then return to your work and your treatment; the cure is done in this way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You must wrap over the fracture one hard bandage doubled in two or three, and the excess should remain. Then turn the leg so the heel comes to the root of the hip, and insert a long thread between the thigh and the leg, beside the knee below, and let the thread's ends be above. Then turn the bandage over the leg and over the thigh, then place splints over the fracture, and place a splint over the bone of the leg. Then fill the empty space between the leg and thigh with soft cloths to ensure equal tightness. Then start to bandage firmly with three or four turns over the fracture. And as you go further up from the fracture, tighten it less. Then tie the two ends of the thread that you have inserted between the leg and the thigh, and bandage three splints that are above, then go back below to the thread's end, until you come to the edge of the foot. And tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like that, provided that neither abscess nor swelling nor anything similar appears.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, untie it and correct what has occurred, as we have said many times. And if there are pieces of bone that pierce, then it must be removed, if possible; and if it cannot be, then the area must be cut open and the cause removed; and treat it as we have described, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thigh is broken, and splints are put on it, as in the shoulder and the arm; however, in the restoration done in this way, the patient does not limp.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in 40 days, or a little less or a little more, according to the differences in complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the joint of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the joint of the knee, there is little breakage, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is only a fissure, or a hole, and happens with all wounds, and without wounds, and this is well felt.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that you put the broken pieces in place, as close together as you can; then put the plaster, and place a round splint, if you need it, and bind it as necessary, then follow all the instructions we have given in other fractures, such as hot abscesses and others similar; then apply what is appropriate for each accident until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called, properly, "mustel," and the other "foscile"; and there is the same type of fracture as occurs in the arm, and therefore the restoration is the same as for the arm, likewise, and the work is all the same. And if the two bones are broken together, the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the smaller bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain, and sees it clearly; and it turns beneath.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then administer extension, and place it straight, and tie the splints equally; however, if the fracture is severe, and there are many pieces, the extension should be gentler and lighter; and adjust the treatment according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed all your work, take two bundles of wood splints that grip the leg on either side, and are the length of the leg from the knee down; then wrap two bandages above and below, and bind it in the middle as well. With this binding, the leg will not deviate to the right or left, and thus it is well done. And some administer a single splint the length of the leg, made of wood, and place the leg on it to prevent movement. This is done properly in a fracture with a wound; and move the leg each day, to see if there is any hot abscess or other accident; treat it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but at the bones of the foot, there are sometimes fractures, and in the toes, too. And there are no breaks except for splintering in various ways.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if a fracture occurs in the bones of the foot, and you see these bones overlapping, place the patient's foot on the ground, as if they were going to walk, and then place your foot on theirs, over where the bones are raised, and press them until they return to their place; then apply a plaster and bandages, and put a small board with two flat sides under the sole of the foot, then bind it to the foot firmly, after you have wrapped bandages around it, and other things you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, untie the bandage, for you will find the bones even, whether fractured or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the toes are fractured, treat them as we described for the fingers of the hand; then place a splint along the length of the fractured toe, slightly wider; then put the board I mentioned under the foot, and bind it firmly; and if there are two or three, or more, fractured toes, place a splint on each toe according to its size, wrapped in a linen bandage, and bind the board under the foot; and let the edge of the board be over the sole of the foot, so that it supports it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things I have said about other fractures, as we have already discussed; and treat each accident as is appropriate.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the forearm
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When a woman's bone is fractured, make her sit up straight, then lean her back, and support her from behind; then fill the woman's vaginal area with cotton, putting in as much as a fist; then raise her up, and slowly straighten her back, and the cotton will rise until it reaches the opening, and the bone will return with the fist; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, replace it, and do this for seven days or so: then the fracture will be restored, and if you wish, take a sheep's bladder, and tie a reed to the opening, and place the entire bladder into her vaginal area; then blow into the reed forcefully, until the bladder is inflated inside; the bone will return to its place; then fill it with cotton, and leave it thus for a few days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the forearm bone of a man, or a woman, is fractured, treat it as we have described for the hip bone; and these fractures are not hidden from those who apply themselves to study and practice this, and understand my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture signifies, in many ways, the correct path to restoration: understand it therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	For the penis, when it is fractured, take a goose's throat and place it on the penis; then wrap bandages around it, and leave it three days or so, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with a wound, especially if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or the shoulder or similar, that it be healed now, so that the healings we have described bear witness to it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then stop it with vitriol, if you have nothing else, then recommence restoring the fracture at that same hour, or that day, if no festering sores come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if festering sores come, then leave the restoration until the ninth day, so that the festering sores are calmed, and do not touch it on the third day or the fourth, for you would cause bad accidents.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is apparent on the exposed flesh, then it is necessary that you put it in place gently with your hands, with small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not suitable for putting it equal with your hands, then reposition it with this instrument that is of iron, which has seven or eight fingers in length, and the width is according to the size of the wound; and for this, the smith needs to forge three or four, according to what is needed in each fracture treatment; and it should be round and slightly thick, so that it does not bend at all when compressing on the limb in your work, and it should be pointed at the front, and thick from the middle onwards, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", so that the curved portion must be placed on the head of the exposed bone; and push it at once, until it returns, and be equal one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot properly grasp the bone, then it is necessary that you cut the head of the bone, so that the instrument has power over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot reposition the bone, as we have said, then cut it with a suitable instrument, either a chisel or a saw, to your ability; then remove what remains of the bone's roughness and small fragments.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is repositioned, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not yet in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	So do so until it is in its place, then soak a cloth in black astringent wine, and properly if it is summertime; and do not put any ointment or anything oily on the wound, lest it cause rot and corruption; then apply compresses once you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut away the surrounding covering according to the size of the wound, and be very careful that the wound is not constricted by the fracture; and many times have foolish physicians done this, and caused death or sores upon the patient; and let the constriction be softer and gentler than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you fear that bad accidents may come to it, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then you should not apply compresses; but wrap it around, instead of compresses, with hard cloths, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see pus forming on the wound after one or two days, remove what you have applied with wine, and apply a healing ointment for wounds, such as tetrafarmacon ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you must untie the limb twice a day, morning and evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limb must be arranged in such a way that the pus runs down easily.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many days pass and it cannot heal but repeatedly produces pus, know that there are small pieces of bone, so you must probe the wound with a probe and remove all those separated pieces that cause that pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula forms in the place, or another manner of corruption, you must treat it according to what he says in his previous chapter.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and exposed on the limb, like the bone of the thigh or the shoulder, and other similar large limbs, do not pull it out, for often death results, but allow it to fester; perhaps it will fall out after twenty or thirty days, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of bruises that arise above the healing.
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often experience them after the healing of the fracture, especially when it is near the joint, and the limb's appearance is unsightly; and perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then if the swelling is fresh; administer astringent medicines, such as aloes, frankincense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, acacia, and similar others, as you take any of these things, or all together, and mix them with astringent wine or with egg white or vinegar; and place them on the knot in bandages, and tie it tightly, and do not loosen it for many days; and then loosen it, and begin another, until the swelling is removed; or you bind it over a piece of well-made lead; for the property of lead is that it removes all swellings from the limbs; and if the swelling has already turned to hardness like stone, and it needs to be removed, cut it open and remove the excess; or you scrape it with a razor until it is removed, and treat it until it is healthy.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the limb that is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fractured bone is healed, and the limb remains weak and fragile afterwards, this happens for many reasons: one of which is that it was bound too tightly, and not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages, and nourishment could not reach the limb; or because of excessive soaking; or because of too much movement, not at the right time; or because there is little blood in the body, it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you should make the patient eat, and make the body strong, so that the blood is multiplied within; and give them baths, and give them joy and ease; then place poultices on the limb, so that the poultices attract great nourishment, and frequently bathe it in warm water, so that nourishment flows to the limb; and it returns to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of the limb crooked after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is crooked after the restoration, and the broken bone is exposed, and the shape of the limb is unsightly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function:  do not believe the fools who say one should break the limb anew, and many fools have done this in our land; and this practice is reprehensible, and great harm, and perhaps death, comes from it. However, if the knots and distortions are fresh, they should be bathed in warm water, or softening herbs should be cooked, such as mallow leaves, roots, and melilot, and similar things; and make a softening poultice, such as a well-made diachylon, and take the mucilage of mallow, and mix it with goose fat or linseed oil, and make a poultice.  Or, take ripe figs, and mash them with fine flour, and similar medicines that soften the adhesion.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the knot is removed by constantly rubbing with wet hands for a long time.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And movement should be administered to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the distortions are old and hardened, like stone, and it is necessary to remove them with an iron, they should be cut to the bone with a sharp, light incision; and care and attention should be given to the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, preventing movement, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs, it should be immediately returned without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the area swells, and perhaps it is difficult to return it to its place; therefore, one should not move it while it is swollen: this often causes inflammation and other pains; however, when this happens, make the patient bleed, then leave it until the inflammation subsides; then bathe the limb in warm water and oil, then gently return it, and treat each limb as it is restored to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters on dislocations from the head down to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jaw(s)
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Sometimes the jaws are dislocated, and the dislocation of both is according to two ways: either they are slightly displaced from their place and slightly softened; or they are entirely dislocated, and hang towards the chest, and the saliva flows from the mouth so that it cannot hold it, nor can it close its mouth, and wraps its tongue with the speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is slight, it returns through several positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is complete and accomplished, you must reset it quickly, and delay not; and in such a manner that the attendant holds the patient's head, and the attendant puts the palm of one of his hands into the root of the dislocation of the jawbone inside the mouth, if the dislocation is from two sides; and the other hand's fingers should be put aside, to put it equal; and instruct the patient to soften its jaw, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the attendant puts it in place, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the resetting is difficult, especially if it is the two jawbones together, then warm water and oil, until you reset them gently; and delay not in resetting, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are reset equally, and the patient's mouth closes well without being forced, then put damp cloths, in a plaster made of rose oil and wax, then bind it lightly with soft bandages; and let the patient sleep on his back, and his head be between two cushions, so that he does not move it to the right or left, and does not strive to open the mouth, but take light food, until the pains are gone, and the jawbones are healed; and then let him eat whatever he wants lightly, and let him not attempt to open his mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaw is well healed and sound.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be reset immediately, and are not returned to their places, then fever and persistent discomfort, and possibly a loosening of the bowels, and possibly a spitting up of pure phlegm, will result.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is perilous; and often the one who experiences this dies within four days.
de la forcelle	of the fork.
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The shoulder cannot dislocate from inside the arm and ribs, and it sometimes dislocates from the outside, and one can certainly feel it.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on their back, and extends their arms; and then press the place firmly with your palm, and it will return; then place the plaster and bandage, and bind it tight; and the shoulder near the ribs cannot dislocate; if not, and if it dislocates sometimes, reset it to its place, as we have said; then place the plaster and bandage, and bind it tight, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healthy; and in the same way the shoulder is reset, when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the dislocation of the shoulder.
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in only three ways: one is that it dislocates toward the armpit below; and the second is toward the ribs; and perhaps it dislocates above, and this happens rarely; and it does not dislocate behind due to the shoulder, and does not dislocate inside due to the nerves; and many times it dislocates below towards the armpit, especially in those who have little flesh, because in them it jumps easily; in those who have enough flesh, it jumps with difficulty, and returns with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And perhaps some men experience a blow or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated because of that.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	You should therefore test it, until you are certain; and then begin the cure.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And dislocation is recognized when it is downward toward the armpit, and when you compare the sick shoulder to the healthy one, you will find a clear difference; and you will find a hollow at the head of the shoulder, and under the armpit when touching the head of the shoulder, as if it were a bone; and the patient cannot bring their hand to their nose, nor move it in any way; and likewise, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you will find it clearly when touching; and this kind of dislocation is only to be brought back, when it is new, or if the patient is a child.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the physician raises the patient's hand upwards, then puts their hands under the armpit, and pulls the joint upwards into its place with force; and the physician raises the hand, and extends it upwards, then puts it underneath; it will come back easily.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come back as we have said within a few days, the patient must be bathed in warm water; and the minister should apply a softening and soothing treatment, such as a decoction of elder, fenugreek, and melilot in water, and administer it; then the patient should be laid on their back, and a piece of wool equal in thickness, neither too soft nor too hard, should be placed under the armpit; then the physician should place their heel on the wool, and lift the head of the shoulder firmly, and pull the patient's hand; and another physician should hold the patient's head so that it does not move downwards; this shoulder will return immediately, and if you wish to see it restored in this way: and for that, you should have a man present who is taller than the patient; and he should stand straight facing the side, and put his shoulder under the patient's armpit, and lift the armpit upwards, so that the patient leans back; and another physician should pull the patient's hand downwards towards the stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, then something heavy should be placed upon him, and the dislocation returns immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And it is also brought back in another way: and it is done by placing a long piece of wood in the ground, whose head is as round as a pestle, and is neither too thick nor too thin; then it is placed under the patient, but with soft cloth over it, and the patient is placed lengthways on the stick; then his hand is stretched down the other side forcefully, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not wish to return through all these things that we have said, do this treatment: take a piece of wood two arms long and four fingers wide, which has a round head for entering deeply under the armpit, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then tie soft cloths over the head of the stick, so that the stick does not injure the patient, then place it under the patient's armpit; and extend his arm along the stick, and bind the shoulder to the stick, and the arm to the top of the hand, then place the arm on a rung of a ladder of suitable width, and stretch the hand downwards, and let the body hang on the other side: the joint will return immediately.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, in whatever manner, you must place a piece of equal thickness wool under the armpit, then apply a prepared plaster of powdered millstone, with incense and egg white, over the entire shoulder and around it, then gently tie it under the armpit, and wrap the bandage over the plaster, and embrace the hand to the neck, and the hand should remain so.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he eat little, until the limb is strengthened, for it will heal sooner; and then eat more after five or seven days, and move it; and if it is firm and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come to it, or for another reason, you must apply cauteries to three places, as it is shown previously in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it comes loose after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot raise their arm upwards, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Dislocations towards the breast, or the back, are caused by impact and the extension of the arms, and another bandage is applied; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if, after healing, there is stiffness in the limb, and slowness in movement, let the patient use baths many times, until that stiffness is lessened and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	Of the dislocation of the ribs
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the ribs is dislocated in points, and returns in points; and if it is dislocated on all sides, especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not healed, because one can clearly see and feel it; and dislocates according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the diseased rib with the healthy one, you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is dislocated, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch the shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary to reset it before suppurating boils appear, for if suppurating boils were to come, it would be difficult to reset; and perhaps it cannot be completely reset, especially when it is in the back; it is worse than other dislocations, and is of greater pain, and perhaps death ensues.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, when it is such that it can be reset, that you extend his hand with your two hands; and his arms are spread out, and the hands of the helper around the rib, above and below, and push the joint to his shoulders together, or to the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and strikes the root of the palm with the dislocated rib.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, administer strong extension; and it is that two assistants extend the arm and hold it, so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm from each side, after you have wrapped a double bandage long and wide; and when the helper has joined the joint to his hand, apply some oil to soften the joint, then push the joint firmly until it returns; and when it is in place, place a dry plaster with some egg white on it, and bind it tightly, and hang the arm on the patient's neck, and leave it for several days, then untie it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, untie the bandage and leave it; and if you see that the joint is not well set, reapply the plaster and bandage, and leave it thus for several days, until it is firmly set; then untie it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels tightness after the joint has been reset, and it moves, bathe and rub it well, and press until it is relieved; or you put a layer of fatty mutton on the joint, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and have him enter a bath; and when he sweats, gently rub the joint, then replace the mutton, and then enter the bath; and do this two or three times, until he is healed; and if you wish, put moist, warm cow dung with butter on it, and bind it on; it will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand dislocates, and its return is easier than other joints.  However, it must be returned to its place quickly, at the very moment it is dislocated, before the area swells or a hot abscess forms there.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the resetting is done by placing the injured hand on a table, and the attendant extends the hand, and the attendant places it straight, so that he places his palm over the area of the joint, and pushes until it returns.  However, you must check to see if it is properly in place; then have the patient put the back of their hand on a table during the extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, have the patient place the back of their hand on the table, and the attendant place their hand over that area of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, that is good. If not, apply soothing plasters to any hot abscesses, and leave it like that without trying again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot tolerate it, and you cannot put it back in place after a few days, the joint remains crooked; and it does no harm to the patient except that the hand is softened and cannot grasp anything at all: then know that the nerves or the arteries are severed; there is no other remedy except to cauterize nearby in the case, and perhaps nothing else will work.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, apply the plaster that we have mentioned, then bandage it and leave it for five days, then unbandage it and leave it like that.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is any stiffness, soak it in warm water and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the finger of the hand is dislocated to either side, sometimes on the back of the palm or the front; then straighten the finger, and push the dislocation with your fingers until it returns, then support the head of the finger, and bend it towards the part where it is disjointed; and leave it for two days, and then put it straight that day; and at night tie it, as we have said, and untie it during the day, and make it move, and tie it again at night; and do this often, until it is straight, and do the same if it is dislocated on the front of the hand, and do as you did before, until it is healed; and do the same if it is dislocated on the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Of the dislocation of the spine of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine of the back or the neck is dislocated, or if there are multiple dislocations, there is no cure, for death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the bowels discharge involuntarily, and cannot be held back, and many times various limbs, or the two thighs or the two arms or one are weakened.  And many times the spine moves in four directions; that which moves to the rear is called "gibbosity." The treatment is to examine if the gibbosity developed in childhood; if so, there is no cure or complete healing.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or from blows or similar things, the ancients described cures with grand words, where there is not always great benefit; but I have abridged it according to my intention, and have devised instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that for gibbosity that comes to the chest in front, there is no remedy nor health; and also that which comes straight to both sides, and one cannot cure anything other than that which comes to the back, as I say; and that the patient be laid out on his face in one even place, and have restraint beneath him, so that he is not injured; then place one burning stick at the head in the ground firmly, and another at the feet, and tie a bandage under the armpits of the patient, and another at the hips, and at the knees, and at the ankles; and two attendants hold the bandages, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two burning sticks; and let them be firmly held, the sticks as we have said, and the physician put their palms on the spine firmly, until it returns to its place.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this treatment, then take a board three arms long, and place it under the wall, and let the patient lie on their side, and put the head of the board under the wall, then put the middle of the board on the spine; and let the physician place their feet on the other end of the board, and press firmly, until it returns to its place; and if you wish, do it with a hand-turned device.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And you should place two burning sticks at the patient's head, one arm's length apart, and two others towards the feet, and have between each stick, above and below, a palm's width of space; and have a hole in each stick, through which the device turns, and let the sticks be firmly in the ground, so that they do not move; and between each pair of sticks, have one turning stick, on which the bandages turn, and have two small sticks of a palm's length on the two turners, to turn the device; and then tie the bandage that is among the armpits to the device towards the head, and the other bandage toward the feet to the other device, and each of the assistants turns their device on the whole bandage, and the physician puts the spine straight as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is straight, then apply a desiccant plaster with abundant egg white, then the bandages, and then a splint of a tablet three fingers long, which covers the gibbosity and the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with a bandage, as we have said, and the patient should use subtle nourishment until he is healed; and if anything happens at the end of the healing process, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the splint that we have mentioned before; and sometimes a piece of lead is administered, and sometimes the appearance appears on the posterior spine of the back, and one believes it to be a dislocation; and it is the exposed bone, for which one should not have any presumption; otherwise, it might bring about death.
des dislocations de la hainche	Of dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that at the joints of the hip and the shoulder, only dislocations occur, and not as at other joints; and the hip joint is dislocated in four ways: inward and outward, and forward and backward; and more inward than outward, and little dislocated forward and backward.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the sign of its inward dislocation is that when the sick leg is joined with the healthy one, it is longer, and the patient's knee appears more prominent than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend their knee forward; and the place next to it is swollen with a hot abscess, because the head of the thigh has come there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of that which comes outward is that these symptoms are contrary to those above.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of that which happens forward are that they extend their leg fully; however, they do not bend their knee without pain, and if you want to make them walk, they cannot go forward, and they retain their urine, and their groin swells, and when they walk, they step on the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of that which happens behind are that they cannot straighten or bend their knee, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the groin is softened, and the head of the thigh is in the place beneath the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The treatment of this type of dislocation is that you observe if the dislocation is old, and it remains in its position, there is no cure; and you should not have any presumptions.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in that in which the dislocation is fresh, and it is of the four types of dislocation, hurry to turn the joint, and extend it inward and outward, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return, and no other treatment is necessary.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, you must prepare a strong assistant, and extend the leg strongly with two hands, or with a strap tied above the knee; and another assistant extends their hand above in such a way that they place their hands under their armpits, and then bind it gently with a strap above the thigh; and another holds the end of the strap; and all extend upwards and downwards at once, so that the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to the four types; and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, that is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, you must apply treatment according to its type.  When the dislocation is inward, you must turn the patient onto their healthy side, then place a strap on the root of the thigh, and the area below the groin, then extend the strap upwards towards the groin, and towards the hip; then another assistant places their arms around the thick part of the affected thigh and extends it outwards forcefully: it will return to its place immediately; and this type of dislocation is easier than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot correct it in this manner that we have said, you must tie the patient's two feet together with a strong strap gently above the two heels, and above the two knees, and the affected leg should be extended two fingers more than the other; then be suspended from the top of a pole, and be above the ground two arms' length; then command an assistant to grasp the top of the thigh, and have another assistant hang with the patient, who grasps the thigh firmly, for the joint will return quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is outward, the patient lies down, as we said for the one with a hip ailment, and bind a strap to the affected leg properly, and also to the foot; then place two poles, one at the head and another at the feet, then place a pole between the patient's thighs in the middle; and have soft cloths spread around so they do not injure the patient, then each assistant pulls towards themselves, and the practitioner places equal force to the dislocation on their side.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place him/her on a table, and press him/her as we said for the hip ailment, and the patient lies on their healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, you must extend the affected leg quickly, as I have said; and the practitioner must exert effort on the affected area, then press with the other hand and pull it down towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is outward, the patient should not be pulled down nor lifted from the ground, but rather be positioned as if the hip were dislocated outward, as we have described for the positioning on two hips; and he/she should be on their face, and the bandage is stretched as we have previously said, and one must press on the joint towards the table; and it will be right when the patient extends their legs and they are equal; then join the thighs, place the plaster, and bind it with a bandage, so that the hip does not move; and rest for three or four days, then unbind it, and place the plaster; and if you see that they are equal, bind it as before, and leave it for three days; then unbind it, and allow the limb to move gently, until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: namely, inward, outward, and backward; and it does not dislocate forward.
