Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the sign is that you instruct the patient to bend their leg at the thigh, and if it does not fit into the thigh, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration for all of them is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend the leg if possible, and put your back on their face, and put their foot on your feet; then take their knee in your palms, and pull it between your fingers, then bend the two sides of the knee firmly; and another assistant extends the foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that the leg fits into the thigh slightly; and place the plaster over it, and make the leg fit into the thigh, and bind them together firmly for three or four days, then unbind it; and the patient does not move at all until the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not right, administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	Of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is sometimes moved, and sometimes fully dislocated, inward and outward.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the sign is that the ankle is swollen, and bulges forward on the side where it is dislocated: the resetting is gentle, and one should gently extend it with their hands when it is only moved.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, you must have the patient sit upright, and hold it firmly by the leg, above the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then with your left two times, then extend it upwards, and gently push the foot upwards; and do this twice, as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, then repeat the procedure, because it returns; and if it cannot return thus, then have the patient lie on their back on the ground, and place a firm peg in the ground between their thighs, and tie bandages around it so that it does not injure the patient; then let the assistants hold the thigh, and another assistant extend the foot with their hands or with a strap that they tie around the top of the foot; then extend each assistant equally, and the peg should be constantly between the patient's thighs to hold the patient when extending it; then let the physicians hold the dislocation with their hands, and another assistant hold the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is in place, apply a plaster and bandages, and hold it firmly, and bind the foot to the leg, and watch the nerves on the back of the ankle, that the bandage is not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the bandage loosens, then tighten it; then untie it on the third or fourth day, and forbid the patient from walking for four days; and if they walk before that time, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a painful abscess appears, you must treat it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	of the fingers
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the fingers are dislocated, they must be gently straightened without force, and it is an easy task.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any part of the back of the foot, you must have the patient sit on a flat surface or a table, straight, and place your foot on the exposed joints, then press firmly on your foot until it returns; and when it is aligned and nothing is visible, place a plank under the sole of the foot, two inches thick, and hold it firmly, and leave it for three days, then release it; and keep it at rest, until it is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with a dislocation, and one wants to restore it, many times the patient dies: do not be presumptuous in the treatment unless you are wise in the art and have practiced it for a long time, and if you are compassionate and merciful and patient, and not rash; and use calming things at the beginning, like hot poultices, and leave the patient in the hands of God if you do not see hope for health; and when you see hope, then restore the limb to its place, before the hot abscess comes; and when the limb is in place, administer calming things for the hot abscess, and treat the wound as appropriate with drying ointments; and if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones are separated, remove them, and do what we have said in simple illnesses; and be careful not to enter a state of fear, as I have said, because this will harm you according to your Creator, and for the safety of your soul and body.
Amen	Amen
